## CBS Board Meeting — January 2026


### 00. WaterRoads_DD_Risk_Register_v2 (6) copy.docx

*File: `00. WaterRoads_DD_Risk_Register_v2 (6) copy.docx`*

WATERROADS PTY LTD

ACN 686 900 014

DUE DILIGENCE RISK REGISTER

VERSION 2.0  |  36 ISSUES IDENTIFIED

Prepared: 4 February 2026

Classification: CONFIDENTIAL — INTERNAL USE ONLY

Do not share with investors. For internal preparation and legal counsel review.

Contents

Introduction

This register documents every issue that a Series A investor’s legal and financial advisors are likely to identify during due diligence on the corporate records of WaterRoads Pty Ltd (ACN 686 900 014). It has been compiled from a clause-by-clause review of all five founding corporate documents, cross-referenced against the ASIC register and Adobe Sign audit trails.

For each issue, the register provides: the specific defect identified; the impact on investor due diligence; and the options available for remediation. This register should be reviewed and updated by the Company’s legal counsel before any data room is opened to investors.

Source Documents Reviewed

1. Certificate of Registration — ASIC, 8 May 2025 (Form 201)

2. ASIC Company Statement — Current as of February 2026

3. Deed of Amendment to Constitution — Dated 1 Aug 2025; Executed 8 Sep 2025

4. CBS Group Share Subscription Agreement — Dated 31 Aug 2025; Executed 7 Sep 2025

5. CBS Group Secured Loan Agreement — Dated 31 Aug 2025; Executed 8 Sep 2025

6. Adobe Sign Final Audit Reports — All three transactional documents

Risk Summary

SECTION A — CORPORATE FORMATION & ASIC REGISTER

SECTION B — CONSTITUTION AMENDMENT DEED

SECTION C — CBS SHARE SUBSCRIPTION AGREEMENT

SECTION D — CBS SECURED LOAN AGREEMENT

SECTION E — RELATED PARTY & CONFLICT OF INTEREST (HIGHEST PRIORITY)

SECTION F — GOVERNANCE & DOCUMENTATION GAPS

Priority Actions Before Data Room Opens

This register is for internal preparation purposes only. It must not be shared with investors, prospective investors, or any external party. The prepared responses are indicative and must be reviewed and refined by the Company’s legal counsel before any data room is opened. This document does not constitute legal advice.



| Severity | Count | Issues |

| CRITICAL | 4 | D1, D2, E1, E2 |

| HIGH | 16 | A1, A2, B1, B2, B4, C1, C2, C3, D3, D4, D5, D6, D13, E3, E4, F1–F4 |

| MEDIUM | 12 | A3–A5, B3, B5–B7, C5, D7, D8, D11, D12, D14, F5 |

| LOW | 4 | A6, C4, D9, D10 |

| TOTAL | 36 | Across 6 sections (A–F) |



| A1 | HIGH | ASIC register shows "FOU / FOUNDER'S" — not "Class A" as per amended Constitution |

|  | IMPACT | Investor DD will immediately flag that the ASIC register and the Company's constitution describe different share classes. This creates doubt about the integrity of corporate records and may delay or condition investment. |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: Recapitalisation (WR-2026-000) cancels all existing shares and creates new F Shares and Common Shares with fresh Form 484 filings — eliminates the mismatch entirely.
Option 2: Lodge a corrective Form 484 for the class redesignation separately — but this only partially fixes the problem and leaves other defects in place. |



| A2 | HIGH | Form 484 filed with ASIC on 5 Sep 2025 — BEFORE transactions were legally completed |

|  | IMPACT | The ASIC filing notified the regulator of a share issuance 2 days before the subscription was executed and 3 days before the constitution creating the share class was effective. This is a procedural irregularity that could be characterised as a false filing with a government regulator. |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: Recapitalisation results in fresh Form 484 filings that reflect the correct current state, superseding the premature filing.
Option 2: Prepare a data room note explaining the chronology and that all transactions were completed within 72 hours.
Option 3: Seek legal advice on whether a corrective notice to ASIC is required. |



| A3 | MEDIUM | Only one Form 484 on ASIC record — class redesignation (FOU → Class A) was never separately filed |

|  | IMPACT | Shows incomplete regulatory compliance. While not material in isolation, it compounds the impression of informal corporate governance. |

|  | OPTIONS | RESOLVED — Recapitalisation ASIC filings will establish correct share classes from scratch. |



| A4 | MEDIUM | CobaltBlu Pty Ltd listed as "Beneficially held: No" — look-through ownership documentation absent from records |

|  | IMPACT | Investors will ask who ultimately owns the 96% founder stake. Without a formal beneficial ownership declaration, there is no documentary evidence of the 50/50 Taylor/Dusting split. This is a standard DD requirement. |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: Prepare a formal beneficial ownership declaration for CobaltBlu Pty Ltd documenting the 50/50 split (Jeff Dusting / Sarah Taylor) and include it in the data room.
Option 2: Obtain a current CobaltBlu ASIC extract to provide documentary backup. |



| A5 | MEDIUM | Board size non-compliant — Constitution Cl 14.2 requires 3–7 directors but only 2 exist |

|  | IMPACT | The Company's own constitution mandates a minimum of 3 directors. With only 2 since incorporation, every board decision since the constitutional amendment could theoretically be questioned (though s201A(2) of the Corporations Act only requires 1 director for a proprietary company, so statutory compliance is not the issue — constitutional compliance is). |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: New Constitution (Schedule A to Recapitalisation) should reset the minimum to 2 until Series A close, then 3–5.
Option 2: Appoint a third director (or independent director) before Series A to bring into compliance under the existing constitution. |



| A6 | LOW | Both directors reside in Victoria; Company registered office and principal place of business in NSW |

|  | IMPACT | Minor. May prompt questions about operational presence in NSW. No regulatory issue — directors are not required to reside in the state of registration. |

|  | OPTIONS | EXPLAIN — Include a brief data room note confirming planned Sydney-based ferry operations and that NSW registration reflects the operational footprint. |



| B1 | HIGH | Constitution Amendment not fully executed until 8 September 2025 despite face date of 1 August 2025 |

|  | IMPACT | The deed states amendments "take effect immediately upon execution." With a 38-day gap between Jeff Dusting's signature (1 Aug) and Sarah Taylor's countersignature (8 Sep, per Adobe Sign), the amendment was not legally effective until 8 September. All documents dated between 1 August and 8 September that reference the amended constitution were premature. |

|  | OPTIONS | RESOLVED — Recapitalisation replaces the entire constitution, establishing a clean effective date. |



| B2 | HIGH | Sarah Taylor signed Constitution as "Director/Secretary" but was not appointed Secretary until 31 August 2025 |

|  | IMPACT | On the document's face date (1 Aug), Sarah did not hold the Secretary role (appointed 31 Aug per ASIC). While the actual signing occurred on 8 Sep (after appointment), the face date creates an appearance of signing in a capacity she did not yet hold. DD lawyers will note this discrepancy. |

|  | OPTIONS | RESOLVED — Recapitalisation supersedes the Constitution Amendment entirely. The actual execution date (8 Sep, post-appointment) means no substantive authority defect. |



| B3 | MEDIUM | CEO delegation limit misstated — Constitution says $250K but CBS subscription claims $500K authority |

|  | IMPACT | Constitution Cl 16A.2 authorises agreements up to $250,000. The CBS subscription execution block states "up to $500,000" — overstating the CEO's delegated authority by 2x. While the $1.00 subscription was within either limit, the misstatement undermines confidence in the CEO's understanding of her own constitutional powers. |

|  | OPTIONS | RESOLVED — The monetary threshold is not the operative defect (see B4 — share issuance prohibition). Recapitalisation supersedes. |



| B4 | HIGH | CBS share issuance executed by CEO despite Cl 16A.3 expressly prohibiting share issuance without board approval |

|  | IMPACT | The CEO purported to issue shares under her general delegation authority. However, Cl 16A.3 specifically carves out share issuances from CEO authority, requiring board approval. No board resolution has been identified. This is a governance defect — the share issuance may lack proper corporate authorisation. |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: Recapitalisation cancels CBS shares and reissues new Common Shares under proper board resolution WR-2026-000 — establishing valid corporate authority from the resolution date forward.
Option 2: Prepare confirmatory board minutes ratifying the original CBS issuance (retrospective ratification) — addresses the historical record but does not fix the chain-of-title issue. |



| B5 | MEDIUM | CEO delegation authority (Cl 16A) did not legally exist when used — Cl 16A was created by the Constitution Amendment which wasn't effective until 8 September |

|  | IMPACT | Circular authority: the CEO cited Cl 16A delegation to sign the subscription, but Cl 16A was inserted by the Constitution Amendment that wasn't effective until after the subscription's face date. The authority did not exist when purportedly exercised. |

|  | OPTIONS | RESOLVED — Moot alongside B4 (share issuance prohibition would have applied regardless). Recapitalisation establishes fresh authority. |



| B6 | MEDIUM | ESOP framework mismatch — Constitution authorises Class C Shares within 15% pool; CEO Reference uses options within 10% pool |

|  | IMPACT | The constitutional authority for employee incentives (Class C Shares, 15%) does not match the implemented structure (options, 10%). The ESOP may lack proper constitutional authorisation. This affects the validity of 1,500,000 option grants to 8 advisors. |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: New Constitution (Schedule A to Recapitalisation) will properly authorise an options-based 10% ESOP — resolves prospectively.
Option 2: If legal counsel determines the grants need retrospective authorisation, prepare a ratifying resolution. |



| B7 | MEDIUM | Series A triggers automatic veto rights sunset under Cl 7.8 — completing $5M+ funding converts Class A veto rights to 75% approval |

|  | IMPACT | The founders' protective veto rights (unanimous consent requirement) would automatically convert to a 75% approval threshold upon completing Series A. This is academic because the Recapitalisation replaces the entire constitution. |

|  | OPTIONS | RESOLVED — New Constitution eliminates the Class A/B framework and all associated sunset provisions. Post-Recapitalisation governance will be designed for the Series A structure. |



| C1 | HIGH | CBS subscribed for Class B shares before that class legally existed |

|  | IMPACT | The subscription is dated 31 August 2025 and references Class B shares. The constitution creating Class B shares was not effective until 8 September. Subscription Recital B falsely states the constitution "has been" amended. CBS subscribed for shares in a non-existent class. This is a fundamental chain-of-title defect. |

|  | OPTIONS | RESOLVED — Recapitalisation cancels all existing shares and reissues under new classes, eliminating the chain-of-title question entirely. |



| C2 | HIGH | CBS Group execution potentially defective under s127 — only one signatory verified by Adobe Sign |

|  | IMPACT | Section 127 of the Corporations Act requires either 2 directors or a director + secretary. The Adobe Sign audit trail shows only Jim Ellwood signed for CBS Group. Jeff Dusting (a CBS director confirmed by the loan signing) was NOT included in the subscription signing workflow. If CBS has multiple directors, the subscription execution may be defective. |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: Recapitalisation supersedes the subscription — new shares issued under proper resolution.
Option 2: Verify CBS Group corporate records (ASIC extract) to confirm Jim Ellwood's sole signing authority.
Option 3: If s127 execution is defective, this further supports the Recapitalisation as the cleanest remedy. |



| C3 | HIGH | Sarah Taylor's and Jeff Dusting's signatures on subscription lack independent Adobe Sign verification |

|  | IMPACT | The subscription has three signing blocks (WaterRoads/CEO, CBS/Director, CobaltBlu/Director). Only Jim Ellwood went through the Adobe Sign verification process. Sarah's and Jeff's signatures appear to have been pre-applied before the document was uploaded. This reduces the evidentiary weight of the execution audit trail — DD lawyers expect independently verified digital signatures. |

|  | OPTIONS | RESOLVED — Recapitalisation supersedes. For historical record, prepare a data room note explaining the signing process. |



| C4 | LOW | CBS Group ACN placeholder unfilled in subscription execution block: "ACN [Insert ACN]" |

|  | IMPACT | Minor drafting defect. CBS ACN (164 870 080) is correctly stated in the party descriptions. Execution block was not updated. Does not affect enforceability but signals informal document preparation. |

|  | OPTIONS | MINOR — Note in data room index. Not worth correcting retroactively. |



| C5 | MEDIUM | Subscription Recital B is a false statement of fact — "The Company has amended its constitution" was not yet true at subscription date |

|  | IMPACT | Recital B states as fact that the constitution had been amended. It had not. The amendment was signed by one party (Jeff, 1 Aug) but not countersigned (Sarah, 8 Sep). This is a drafting error — the recital assumed the amendment would be completed first. It became factually correct 8 days later. |

|  | OPTIONS | RESOLVED — All parties intended simultaneous transactions. Recapitalisation supersedes the subscription entirely. |



| D1 | CRITICAL | CBS holds first-ranking security interest over ALL Company assets — but security is NOT registered on PPSR (unperfected) |

|  | IMPACT | The loan grants CBS a first-ranking security interest over all present and after-acquired property. However, the security has NOT been registered on the Personal Property Securities Register (PPSR) and will not be. Under s267 of the PPSA, an unperfected security interest vests back in the company upon administration — making it effectively unenforceable against third parties or in insolvency. This significantly reduces the practical threat to Series A investors, but the contractual obligation to CBS remains. The failure to register also undermines the characterisation of this as a genuine commercial lending arrangement. |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: Repay the loan in full from Series A proceeds at close — eliminates the issue entirely and is the cleanest approach for investor confidence.
Option 2: Negotiate subordination with CBS — CBS formally subordinates its (unperfected) security to investor rights.
Option 3: Negotiate an intercreditor agreement — formalises the priority between CBS and Series A investors.
Option 4: Leave in place — the unperfected security is low-risk but the contractual obligations and negative pledge (D2) remain problematic. |



| D2 | CRITICAL | Negative pledge — Company cannot create ANY security interest without CBS consent (Cl 7.4) |

|  | IMPACT | Even though CBS's own security is unperfected, Cl 7.4 contractually prevents WaterRoads from granting any security to any other party without CBS's written consent. This means: no convertible note security, no equipment financing, no bank facilities, and no asset-backed lending without CBS's agreement. Series A investors or future lenders will require this restriction to be removed or waived. |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: Repay the loan — eliminates the negative pledge entirely.
Option 2: Obtain a CBS waiver of Cl 7.4 as part of the Recapitalisation consent package.
Option 3: Negotiate amendment to the Loan Agreement carving out investor-related security from the negative pledge. |



| D3 | HIGH | Change of control trigger — Cl 5.3 requires mandatory prepayment on change of control |

|  | IMPACT | The Recapitalisation restructures ownership from 90.91%/9.09% to 96%/4%. The Series A itself will introduce new shareholders. Both events could be characterised as a "change of control" under Cl 5.3, giving CBS the right to demand immediate full repayment. |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: CBS Waiver (Schedule C to WR-2026-000) addresses the Recapitalisation trigger.
Option 2: If the loan survives to Series A close, a SEPARATE waiver will be needed for the Series A investment itself.
Option 3: Repaying the loan at close eliminates the issue for Series A. |



| D4 | HIGH | Asset disposal trigger — Cl 5.3 mandatory prepayment on disposal of "substantially all assets" |

|  | IMPACT | The planned corporate restructuring into HoldCo, LeaseCo, and CityCo entities involves transferring IP and operational assets. This could be characterised as disposing of "substantially all assets" and trigger mandatory prepayment. If the loan survives to the restructuring phase, CBS consent is required for any intercompany asset transfer. |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: Repay the loan before corporate restructuring — eliminates the trigger.
Option 2: Obtain CBS consent for the planned HoldCo/LeaseCo/CityCo structure as part of the broader CBS consent package.
Option 3: Defer the corporate restructuring until after the loan is dealt with. |



| D5 | HIGH | Financial covenants likely breached — $50K minimum cash balance and 1:2 current ratio (Cl 8.3) |

|  | IMPACT | An early-stage startup with pre-revenue operations is unlikely to consistently maintain a $50,000 minimum cash balance and a current ratio of at least 1:2. Any breach constitutes an Event of Default under Cl 9.1, giving CBS a standing right to terminate the facility and demand immediate repayment at any time. This is a sword hanging over the Company. |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: Confirm current compliance status immediately — determine whether a breach exists.
Option 2: If breached: obtain a CBS waiver of existing covenant breaches and either reset covenants to realistic thresholds or waive covenants entirely pending Series A.
Option 3: Repay the loan — eliminates covenant exposure. |



| D6 | HIGH | Audited annual accounts requirement — Cl 8.2 requires audited accounts within 90 days of year-end |

|  | IMPACT | An early-stage startup is extremely unlikely to have engaged auditors or produced audited accounts. Non-compliance with Cl 8.2 is a potential Event of Default. Cl 8.2 also requires quarterly financial statements within 30 days — if these have not been provided, there are multiple compounding breaches. |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: Confirm FY end date and whether any financial reporting has been provided to CBS.
Option 2: If non-compliant: include covenant breaches in the CBS waiver package.
Option 3: Repay the loan — eliminates reporting obligations. |



| D7 | MEDIUM | Interest rate inconsistency between loan body and Schedule 1 |

|  | IMPACT | The body defines the rate as "Commercial Finance Interest Rate (Mid) per RBA Table F5." Schedule 1 says "RBA Cash Rate + 5.0% margin (currently 8.60%)." These are different rate references. If any interest has been paid or accrued, the parties may be using different calculations. |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: If the loan is to be repaid at close: calculate interest using both methods, pay the higher amount to avoid dispute.
Option 2: If the loan survives: execute an amendment letter clarifying the operative rate.
Option 3: Confirm which rate has been applied in practice. |



| D8 | MEDIUM | Maturity date placeholder unfilled in loan body — "[Insert date]" — while Schedule says 1 July 2030 |

|  | IMPACT | The body contains a template placeholder. Schedule 1 specifies 1 July 2030. Schedules typically prevail in case of conflict. Not material but signals incomplete document preparation. |

|  | OPTIONS | MINOR — Schedule prevails. Note in data room if loan survives. |



| D9 | LOW | Minimum drawdown inconsistency — body says $10,000, Schedule says $5,000 |

|  | IMPACT | Minor internal inconsistency. Unlikely to be material. Schedule likely prevails. |

|  | OPTIONS | MINOR — Schedule prevails. Note in data room if loan survives. |



| D10 | LOW | CBS Group ACN placeholder unfilled in loan execution block: "ACN [Insert ACN]" |

|  | IMPACT | Same defect as the subscription agreement (C4). CBS ACN correctly stated in party descriptions. Minor drafting oversight. |

|  | OPTIONS | MINOR — Note in data room index. |



| D11 | MEDIUM | Loan is assignable by CBS to any third party without Company consent (Cl 10.7) |

|  | IMPACT | CBS could sell the $500K debt (with its contractual security interest and negative pledge) to any third party. The acquirer would inherit the right to demand repayment on any existing Event of Default, enforce the negative pledge, and block the Company from granting security. This is a structural risk even though the security is unperfected. |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: Repay the loan — eliminates assignment risk.
Option 2: Negotiate an amendment restricting assignment without Company consent.
Option 3: Include an assignment restriction in the Series A investment agreement as a condition of close. |



| D12 | MEDIUM | CBS holds contractual veto over substantial business changes — Cl 8.2 |

|  | IMPACT | The Company must not "substantially change its business without consent." Expanding from Sydney harbour ferries to a global water metro network, or pivoting service models, could trigger this. CBS has a contractual veto over the Company's strategic direction. |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: Repay the loan — eliminates the business change restriction.
Option 2: Obtain CBS consent to the business plan presented to Series A investors.
Option 3: Negotiate removal of this restriction as part of the CBS consent package. |



| D13 | HIGH | PPSR registration status confirmed — security interest NOT registered and will not be registered |

|  | IMPACT | CBS did not register its security interest on the PPSR and has confirmed it will not do so. Under the PPSA, the security is therefore unperfected and would vest back in the Company in an insolvency (s267). This significantly reduces the practical risk to Series A investors but raises questions about the genuine commercial nature of the lending arrangement. A real commercial lender would always register. This is a data point supporting the related-party characterisation. |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: Use the non-registration as a positive in the DD narrative — the security is unperfected and does not encumber the Company's assets for investor purposes.
Option 2: Address the related-party implications in the broader conflict-of-interest disclosure (see Section E).
Option 3: Repay the loan to eliminate all loan-related DD issues. |



| D14 | MEDIUM | No board resolution authorising the borrowing — CEO prohibited from borrowing under Cl 16A.3 |

|  | IMPACT | Constitution Cl 16A.3 prohibits the CEO from borrowing money without board approval. Sarah signed the loan as Director/Secretary (not CEO), implying board authority. However, no board resolution has been identified. With only 2 directors (Jeff conflicted on CBS matters), the resolution process is questionable. |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: Prepare confirmatory board minutes ratifying the loan approval with appropriate conflict-of-interest disclosure.
Option 2: Address in the broader governance narrative — the Recapitalisation Board Resolution (WR-2026-000) includes the CBS Loan waiver, which implicitly acknowledges and ratifies the loan's existence. |



| E1 | CRITICAL | Jeff Dusting is a director of WaterRoads, CobaltBlu, AND CBS Group simultaneously — confirmed by Adobe Sign audit trail |

|  | IMPACT | The CBS Loan Adobe Sign audit trail shows Jeff Dusting was emailed the loan document for his own signature at jeff@cbs.com.au and signed it as a CBS Group signatory on 5 September 2025. This is definitive evidence that Jeff holds a director (or equivalent officer) position at CBS Group. He simultaneously holds positions at all three entities in the CBS transactions. This triggers: (a) Chapter 2E of the Corporations Act — related-party financial benefits requiring member approval; (b) Constitution Cl 48.1 — arm's length terms, disinterested director approval, and quarterly disclosure; (c) common law fiduciary duty obligations regarding conflicts of interest. This is the single highest DD risk. |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: Obtain a CBS Group ASIC extract to confirm Jeff's precise role (director, shareholder, secretary).
Option 2: Prepare a comprehensive conflict-of-interest disclosure documenting the relationship across all three entities.
Option 3: Prepare a Chapter 2E analysis with legal counsel — determine whether member approval was required for the CBS transactions and if so, obtain retrospective ratification.
Option 4: Document arm's length basis for all CBS transactions with supporting evidence (comparable loan terms, market-rate interest, etc.).
Option 5: Consider whether Jeff should recuse from WaterRoads board votes on CBS-related matters going forward. |



| E2 | CRITICAL | Jeff Dusting orchestrated ALL CBS transaction documents from his CBS email — created 3 documents in 5 minutes, filed ASIC form, and signed for CBS |

|  | IMPACT | On 5 September 2025, Jeff Dusting — operating from jeff@cbs.com.au — created the constitution amendment (2:26:56 AM), the share subscription (2:24:25 AM), and the loan agreement (2:22:14 AM) in Adobe Sign within a 5-minute window. He then signed the loan for CBS Group (2:46:28 AM). The ASIC Form 484 was filed the same day. Jeff was the sole orchestrator of the entire CBS entry into WaterRoads — acting simultaneously as a WaterRoads director, a CobaltBlu director, and a CBS Group officer. No independent governance check existed at any point in the process. |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: This finding must be fully disclosed and contextualised. Prepare a governance narrative explaining the circumstances of the CBS investment.
Option 2: Engage legal counsel to review the related-party implications and prepare the disclosure before the data room opens.
Option 3: Consider obtaining an independent assessment confirming arm's length terms for the CBS transactions. |



| E3 | HIGH | Constitution Cl 48.1 requires related-party transactions to be approved by "disinterested directors" — Jeff was not disinterested |

|  | IMPACT | The Company's own constitution mandates arm's length terms, disinterested director approval, and quarterly disclosure for related-party transactions involving Class A shareholders or their related entities. Jeff, as a director of both WaterRoads and CBS Group, could not be "disinterested" in the CBS transactions. Sarah was the only other director and would need to be the sole approver. No board minute documenting disinterested director approval exists. |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: Prepare confirmatory board minutes documenting Sarah's approval of the CBS transactions as the sole disinterested director, with Jeff's conflict fully disclosed.
Option 2: Include conflict-of-interest disclosures in the pre-2026 confirmatory minutes package. |



| E4 | HIGH | Ownership realignment from 90.91% to 96% immediately before Series A raises questions when Jeff sits on both sides |

|  | IMPACT | The fact that Jeff is a director of both CobaltBlu (which gains 5.09 percentage points) and CBS Group (which loses 5.09 percentage points) in the Recapitalisation means the ownership change is between two entities with a common director. Investor DD lawyers will ask whether CBS Group's consent was truly independent or influenced by Jeff's conflicting interests. |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: CBS Group's consent (Schedule D) includes a representation that it has had the opportunity for independent advice.
Option 2: Consider having CBS Group obtain and document independent legal advice on the Recapitalisation to strengthen the consent.
Option 3: Ensure the CBS consent is executed by a CBS signatory other than Jeff (e.g., Jim Ellwood) to demonstrate independence from Jeff's influence. |



| F1 | HIGH | No board minutes exist for any corporate actions before January 2026 |

|  | IMPACT | There are no board minutes documenting: the incorporation decisions, the constitution amendment approval, the CBS share issuance authorisation, the CBS loan approval, the appointment of the CEO, or the appointment of the Secretary. Investor DD expects a complete minute book. The absence of pre-2026 minutes, combined with the related-party issues, creates a picture of informal governance that will concern institutional investors. |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: Prepare confirmatory board minutes documenting all pre-2026 corporate actions with honest confirmation dates — prepared as "resolutions confirmed" with the actual date of confirmation, NOT fabricated meeting records.
Option 2: Include conflict-of-interest disclosures for Jeff Dusting on all CBS-related matters.
Option 3: Engage the Company Secretary to formalise the minute book before data room. |



| F2 | HIGH | No shareholders' agreement between CobaltBlu and CBS Group |

|  | IMPACT | The CBS Share Subscription (Cl 6.1) contemplated a future shareholders' agreement but none was executed. Governance currently relies on the Constitution alone. There are no contractual drag-along, tag-along, or exit provisions beyond the constitutional framework. Series A investors will require comprehensive governance arrangements. |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: Address in the Series A investment agreement — standard Series A terms will include comprehensive shareholder governance provisions (drag-along, tag-along, information rights, protective provisions, board composition).
Option 2: Consider whether a pre-Series A shareholders' agreement between CobaltBlu and CBS Group is needed, or whether the Series A documents will suffice. |



| F3 | HIGH | No independent valuation supporting A$50M seed valuation or A$0.50 ESOP strike price |

|  | IMPACT | The A$50M valuation is board-assessed with no independent support. For ESS tax compliance (Division 83A, ITAA 1997), the ATO may challenge the A$0.50 strike price if it cannot be independently verified. Investor DD will also question the basis for the seed valuation. Without independent support, the ESOP grants may create tax exposure for the 8 advisor grantees. |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: Commission an independent valuation from a specialist firm (Big 4 or registered business valuer) — supports both the seed valuation for investors and the ESOP strike price for tax purposes.
Option 2: At minimum, prepare a board-approved valuation memorandum documenting the methodology, comparable transactions, and rationale for the A$50M figure.
Option 3: Obtain specific ESS tax advice on whether the valuation approach satisfies safe harbour requirements. |



| F4 | HIGH | ESOP grants vest from June/October 2025 but ESOP was not established until January 2026 — backdated vesting |

|  | IMPACT | Options were granted on 15 January 2026 with vesting commencement dates backdated to 1 June 2025 (7 advisors) and 1 October 2025 (1 advisor). This means up to 7 months of vesting credit was applied for a period when the ESOP did not exist. While this reflects the start of advisory services, the ATO may scrutinise the arrangement. If characterised unfavourably, advisors may face unexpected tax consequences. |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: Obtain ESS tax advice confirming Division 83A compliance — the taxing point for options is at exercise (not grant or vesting), but the ATO may challenge the backdating.
Option 2: Document the commercial rationale for backdated vesting — advisory services commenced before the ESOP was established, and the vesting dates recognise contributions already made.
Option 3: Consider whether the option grant agreements adequately disclose the tax position to advisors. |



| F5 | MEDIUM | Independent director requirement triggered by Series A — Constitution Cl 14.3 |

|  | IMPACT | Completing the Series A (A$15M) triggers the constitutional requirement for at least one independent director. Ocean Zero or other investors may also require board seats. The Company should have candidates identified before negotiations begin. |

|  | OPTIONS | Option 1: Identify 2–3 independent director candidates with relevant industry or governance expertise before investor outreach.
Option 2: Factor board composition into Series A term sheet negotiations — investors will have views on this.
Option 3: New Constitution should set appropriate board composition requirements for the post-Series A structure. |



| 1 | URGENT | Document Jeff Dusting / CBS Group Relationship  [Owner: CEO]
Obtain CBS Group ASIC extract. Confirm Jeff’s directorships. Prepare Chapter 2E analysis. Prepare comprehensive conflict-of-interest disclosure. Document arm’s length basis for all CBS transactions. |



| 2 | URGENT | Confirm CBS Loan Status  [Owner: CFO]
Determine current drawn amount, interest paid/accrued. Confirm FY end date. Check covenant compliance ($50K cash, 1:2 current ratio, audited accounts, quarterly reports). Any breach = standing Event of Default. |



| 3 | URGENT | Decide CBS Loan Strategy for Series A  [Owner: CEO/Board]
Recommend: repay from Series A proceeds at close. This eliminates: first-ranking security, negative pledge, change-of-control trigger, financial covenants, assignability risk, and business change veto — all in one action. |



| 4 | HIGH | Commission Independent Valuation  [Owner: CFO]
Required for ESS tax compliance (A$0.50 strike price), investor confidence in A$50M seed valuation, and defence of ESOP backdated vesting. |



| 5 | HIGH | Prepare Confirmatory Board Minutes (pre-2026)  [Owner: Co Sec]
Document all pre-2026 corporate actions with honest confirmation dates. Include conflict disclosures for Jeff Dusting on all CBS matters. |



| 6 | HIGH | Prepare CobaltBlu Beneficial Ownership Declaration  [Owner: Co Sec]
Formal declaration documenting 50/50 ownership (Jeff Dusting / Sarah Taylor) with look-through to ultimate beneficial owners. |



| 7 | HIGH | Obtain ESS Tax Advice on Backdated Vesting  [Owner: Legal/Tax]
Confirm Division 83A compliance for vesting commencement dates of Jun/Oct 2025 on grants made Jan 2026. |



| 8 | HIGH | Verify CBS Group Corporate Records  [Owner: Legal]
Obtain CBS Group ASIC extract. Confirm directors, shareholders, relationship to Jeff Dusting. Required for comprehensive conflict disclosure. |



| 9 | MEDIUM | Identify Independent Director Candidates  [Owner: CEO]
Constitution Cl 14.3 triggered by Series A. Have 2–3 candidates identified before investor negotiations. |

### 01.  DD Risk Register V3 Institutional copy.docx

*File: `01.  DD Risk Register V3 Institutional copy.docx`*

WATERROADS PTY LTD

ACN 686 900 014

DUE DILIGENCE RISK REGISTER

VERSION 3.0 – INSTITUTIONAL GRADE (INTERNAL)

37 ISSUES IDENTIFIED | 16 RESOLVED/MITIGATED | 21 ACTIVE REMEDIATION

Prepared: 5 February 2026

Classification: CONFIDENTIAL – INTERNAL USE ONLY

Internal DD planning version. Not for investor data room. For legal counsel review and internal preparation only.

INTRODUCTION

This register documents every issue that a Series A investor's legal and financial advisors are likely to identify during due diligence on the corporate records of WaterRoads Pty Ltd (ACN 686 900 014). It has been compiled from a clause-by-clause review of all founding corporate documents, cross-referenced against the ASIC register and Adobe Sign audit trails.

Version 3.0 updates: This version integrates the spousal relationship disclosure (new issue E5), adds post-Recapitalisation status tracking, and aligns with the CBS Consent & Waiver Deed V4 and CBS Loan Variation & Waiver Deed V6.

For each issue, the register provides:

The specific defect identified

The impact on investor due diligence

Status post-Recapitalisation (new column)

Residual action required (new column)

Options available for remediation

This register should be reviewed and updated by the Company's legal counsel before any data room is opened to investors.

SOURCE DOCUMENTS REVIEWED

Certificate of Registration – ASIC, 8 May 2025 (Form 201)

ASIC Company Statement – Current as of February 2026

Deed of Amendment to Constitution – Dated 1 Aug 2025; Executed 8 Sep 2025

CBS Group Share Subscription Agreement – Dated 31 Aug 2025; Executed 7 Sep 2025

CBS Group Secured Loan Agreement – Dated 31 Aug 2025; Executed 8 Sep 2025

Adobe Sign Final Audit Reports – All three transactional documents

Recapitalisation Deed – Dated 14 January 2026

CBS Consent and Waiver Deed – Version 4 Institutional, dated 22 January 2026

CBS Loan Variation and Waiver Deed – Version 6 Institutional, dated 22 January 2026

Amended and Restated Constitution – Version 3 Institutional Grade, adopted 14 January 2026

RISK SUMMARY

Post-Recapitalisation Status Summary

SECTION A – CORPORATE FORMATION & ASIC REGISTER

A1 – HIGH

Issue: ASIC register shows "FOU / FOUNDER'S" – not "Class A" as per amended Constitution

Impact: Investor DD will immediately flag that the ASIC register and the Company's constitution describe different share classes. This creates doubt about the integrity of corporate records and may delay or condition investment.

Status Post-Recap: ✅ RESOLVED – Recapitalisation (WR-2026-000) cancelled all existing shares and created new F Shares and Common Shares with fresh Form 484 filings. ASIC register now matches Constitution V3.

Residual Action: None. Include clean ASIC extract in data room showing current share classes.

Options (historical reference only):

Option 1: Recapitalisation eliminates the mismatch entirely. ✅ IMPLEMENTED

Option 2: Lodge corrective Form 484 separately (no longer needed).

A2 – HIGH

Issue: Form 484 filed with ASIC on 5 Sep 2025 – BEFORE transactions were legally completed

Impact: The ASIC filing notified the regulator of a share issuance 2 days before the subscription was executed and 3 days before the constitution creating the share class was effective. This is a procedural irregularity that could be characterised as premature filing.

Status Post-Recap: ✅ RESOLVED – Fresh Form 484 filings at Recapitalisation reflect correct current state, superseding the premature filing.

Residual Action: Prepare data room note explaining historical chronology for context. No corrective action required.

A3 – MEDIUM

Issue: Only one Form 484 on ASIC record – class redesignation (FOU → Class A) was never separately filed

Impact: Shows incomplete regulatory compliance. While not material in isolation, it compounds the impression of informal corporate governance.

Status Post-Recap: ✅ RESOLVED – Recapitalisation ASIC filings establish correct share classes from scratch.

Residual Action: None.

A4 – MEDIUM

Issue: CobaltBlu Pty Ltd listed as "Beneficially held: No" – look-through ownership documentation absent from records

Impact: Investors will ask who ultimately owns the 96% founder stake. Without a formal beneficial ownership declaration, there is no documentary evidence of the 50/50 Taylor/Dusting split. This is a standard DD requirement.

Status Post-Recap: ⚠️ ACTION REQUIRED – Beneficial ownership declaration needs preparation.

Residual Action: Prepare formal CobaltBlu Beneficial Ownership Declaration documenting 50/50 split (Jeff Dusting / Sarah Taylor). Include current CobaltBlu ASIC extract. Target: Week 1.

A5 – MEDIUM

Issue: Board size non-compliant – Constitution Cl 14.2 requires 3–7 directors but only 2 exist

Impact: The Company's own constitution mandates a minimum of 3 directors. With only 2 since incorporation, every board decision could theoretically be questioned (though s201A(2) of the Corporations Act only requires 1 director for proprietary companies).

Status Post-Recap: ⚠️ ACTION REQUIRED – Constitution V3 should address this structurally.

Residual Action:

Option 1: Verify Constitution V3 resets minimum to 2 until Series A close, then 3–5. ✅ RECOMMENDED

Option 2: Appoint independent director pre-close to achieve 3-director board.

A6 – LOW

Issue: Both directors reside in Victoria; Company registered office and principal place of business in NSW

Impact: Minor. May prompt questions about operational presence in NSW. No regulatory issue – directors not required to reside in state of registration.

Status Post-Recap: ℹ️ EXPLAIN ONLY – No action required.

Residual Action: Include brief data room note confirming planned Sydney-based ferry operations and NSW registration reflects operational footprint.

SECTION B – CONSTITUTION AMENDMENT DEED

B1 – HIGH

Issue: Constitution Amendment not fully executed until 8 September 2025 despite face date of 1 August 2025

Impact: The deed states amendments "take effect immediately upon execution." With a 38-day gap between signatures, the amendment was not legally effective until 8 September. All documents dated between 1 August and 8 September that reference the amended constitution were premature.

Status Post-Recap: ✅ RESOLVED – Recapitalisation replaces the entire constitution, establishing a clean effective date (14 January 2026).

Residual Action: None. Historical issue superseded by Constitution V3.

B2 – HIGH

Issue: Sarah Taylor signed Constitution as "Director/Secretary" but was not appointed Secretary until 31 August 2025

Impact: On the document's face date (1 Aug), Sarah did not hold the Secretary role. While actual signing occurred 8 Sep (after appointment), the face date creates appearance of signing in a capacity she did not yet hold.

Status Post-Recap: ✅ RESOLVED – Recapitalisation supersedes the Constitution Amendment entirely. Actual execution date (8 Sep, post-appointment) means no substantive authority defect.

Residual Action: None.

B3 – MEDIUM

Issue: CEO delegation limit misstated – Constitution says $250K but CBS subscription claims $500K authority

Impact: Constitution Cl 16A.2 authorises agreements up to $250,000. CBS subscription execution block states "up to $500,000" – overstating the CEO's delegated authority by 2x.

Status Post-Recap: ✅ RESOLVED – Monetary threshold is moot; see B4 (share issuance prohibition was operative defect). Recapitalisation supersedes.

Residual Action: None.

B4 – HIGH

Issue: CBS share issuance executed by CEO despite Cl 16A.3 expressly prohibiting share issuance without board approval

Impact: The CEO purported to issue shares under general delegation authority. However, Cl 16A.3 specifically carves out share issuances from CEO authority, requiring board approval. No board resolution has been identified. This is a governance defect.

Status Post-Recap: ✅ RESOLVED – Recapitalisation cancels CBS shares and reissues new Common Shares under proper board resolution WR-2026-000.

Residual Action: None. Historical defect remediated by Recapitalisation.

B5 – MEDIUM

Issue: CEO delegation authority (Cl 16A) did not legally exist when used – created by Constitution Amendment not effective until 8 September

Impact: Circular authority: CEO cited Cl 16A delegation to sign subscription, but Cl 16A was inserted by Constitution Amendment not effective until after subscription's face date.

Status Post-Recap: ✅ RESOLVED – Moot alongside B4. Recapitalisation establishes fresh authority.

Residual Action: None.

B6 – MEDIUM

Issue: ESOP framework mismatch – Constitution authorises Class C Shares within 15% pool; CEO Reference uses options within 10% pool

Impact: Constitutional authority for employee incentives (Class C Shares, 15%) does not match implemented structure (options, 10%). ESOP may lack proper constitutional authorisation.

Status Post-Recap: ✅ RESOLVED – Constitution V3 properly authorises options-based 10% ESOP.

Residual Action: Verify Constitution V3 ESOP clauses align with CEO Reference and option grant letters. If legal counsel determines historical grants need ratification, prepare confirmatory resolution.

B7 – MEDIUM

Issue: Series A triggers automatic veto rights sunset under Cl 7.8 – completing $5M+ funding converts Class A veto rights to 75% approval

Impact: Founders' protective veto rights would automatically convert to 75% approval threshold upon completing Series A. Academic because Recapitalisation replaces entire constitution.

Status Post-Recap: ✅ RESOLVED – Constitution V3 eliminates Class A/B framework and all associated sunset provisions. Post-Recapitalisation governance designed for Series A structure.

Residual Action: None.

SECTION C – CBS SHARE SUBSCRIPTION AGREEMENT

C1 – HIGH

Issue: CBS subscribed for Class B shares before that class legally existed

Impact: Subscription dated 31 August 2025 references Class B shares. Constitution creating Class B was not effective until 8 September. Subscription Recital B falsely states constitution "has been" amended. CBS subscribed for shares in non-existent class – fundamental chain-of-title defect.

Status Post-Recap: ✅ RESOLVED – Recapitalisation cancels all existing shares and reissues under new classes, eliminating chain-of-title question entirely.

Residual Action: None.

C2 – HIGH

Issue: CBS Group execution potentially defective under s127 – only one signatory verified by Adobe Sign

Impact: Section 127 of Corporations Act requires either 2 directors or director + secretary. Adobe Sign audit trail shows only Jim Ellwood signed for CBS Group. If CBS has multiple directors, subscription execution may be defective.

Status Post-Recap: ✅ RESOLVED – Recapitalisation supersedes subscription; new shares issued under proper resolution and CBS Consent & Waiver Deed V4 with compliant execution.

Residual Action: Include CBS Consent & Waiver Deed V4 (properly executed) in data room. Note historical defect resolved by Recapitalisation.

C3 – HIGH

Issue: Sarah Taylor's and Jeff Dusting's signatures on subscription lack independent Adobe Sign verification

Impact: Only Jim Ellwood went through Adobe Sign verification. Sarah's and Jeff's signatures appear pre-applied before upload. This reduces evidentiary weight of execution audit trail.

Status Post-Recap: ✅ RESOLVED – Recapitalisation supersedes subscription.

Residual Action: Prepare data room note explaining historical signing process. No corrective action needed.

C4 – LOW

Issue: CBS Group ACN placeholder unfilled in subscription execution block: "ACN [Insert ACN]"

Impact: Minor drafting defect. CBS ACN (164 870 080) correctly stated in party descriptions. Execution block not updated. Does not affect enforceability but signals informal document preparation.

Status Post-Recap: ℹ️ MINOR – Historical drafting issue.

Residual Action: Note in data room index. Not worth correcting retroactively.

C5 – MEDIUM

Issue: Subscription Recital B is false statement of fact – "The Company has amended its constitution" was not yet true at subscription date

Impact: Recital B states as fact that constitution had been amended. It had not (amendment not effective until 8 days later). Drafting error assuming simultaneous completion.

Status Post-Recap: ✅ RESOLVED – All parties intended simultaneous transactions. Recapitalisation supersedes subscription entirely.

Residual Action: None.

SECTION D – CBS SECURED LOAN AGREEMENT

D1 – CRITICAL

Issue: CBS holds first-ranking security interest over ALL Company assets – but security is NOT registered on PPSR (unperfected)

Impact: Loan grants CBS first-ranking security over all assets. However, security NOT registered on PPSR and will not be. Under s267 PPSA, unperfected security interest vests back in company upon administration – effectively unenforceable against third parties or in insolvency. Significantly reduces practical threat to Series A investors, but contractual obligation to CBS remains.

Status Post-Recap: ✅ MITIGATED – CBS Loan Variation & Waiver Deed V6:

Subordinates loan to Series A in payment and enforcement (Clause 3.3)

Mandates full repayment at Series A close (Clause 6.1, binding commitment)

Security to be discharged within 2 Business Days of repayment (Clause 6.4)

Any Series A security ranks ahead of CBS unperfected security (Clause 3.2(c))

Residual Action:

Ensure loan repayment ($209,000 approx.) included in Series A uses of proceeds

Obtain CBS discharge deed and PPSR confirmations at close

Upload CBS Loan Variation & Waiver Deed V6 to data room

Zero residual investor credit/security risk – loan fully discharged at close

D2 – CRITICAL

Issue: Negative pledge – Company cannot create ANY security interest without CBS consent (Cl 7.4)

Impact: Even though CBS's security is unperfected, Cl 7.4 contractually prevents WaterRoads from granting security to any other party without CBS consent. Blocks convertible notes, equipment financing, bank facilities, asset-backed lending without CBS agreement.

Status Post-Recap: ✅ MITIGATED – CBS Loan Variation & Waiver Deed V6 Clause 3.2:

Negative pledge varied to permit Series A security (Permitted Security Interest)

Series A security explicitly ranks ahead of CBS

CBS obligated to execute subordination deeds as requested

Full loan repayment at close eliminates negative pledge entirely

Residual Action:

Ensure CBS Loan Variation & Waiver Deed V6 uploaded to data room

At close: obtain CBS discharge deed confirming termination of all covenants

Zero residual restriction post-close

D3 – HIGH

Issue: Change of control trigger – Cl 5.3 requires mandatory prepayment on change of control

Impact: Recapitalisation (90.91%/9.09% → 96%/4%) and Series A (new shareholders) could characterise as "change of control," giving CBS right to demand immediate repayment.

Status Post-Recap: ✅ MITIGATED – CBS Loan Variation & Waiver Deed V6:

Clause 2.1: Irrevocable waiver for Recapitalisation

Clause 3.1: Permanent unconditional waiver for Series A and all future equity rounds

Waiver not subject to ownership thresholds; does not revive

Residual Action:

Upload CBS Loan Variation & Waiver Deed V6 to data room

Highlight Annexure A (Summary of Waivers) for DD counsel

Zero change-of-control risk for Series A

D4 – HIGH

Issue: Asset disposal trigger – Cl 5.3 mandatory prepayment on disposal of "substantially all assets"

Impact: Planned corporate restructuring (HoldCo, LeaseCo, CityCo) involves transferring IP and operational assets. Could trigger mandatory prepayment if loan survives to restructuring phase.

Status Post-Recap: ✅ MITIGATED – CBS Loan Variation & Waiver Deed V6:

Mandatory repayment at Series A close (Clause 6.1)

Loan will not survive to restructuring phase

If restructuring occurs pre-close, obtain CBS consent as part of broader package

Residual Action:

Repay loan before any corporate restructuring

Zero asset disposal trigger risk post-close

D5 – HIGH

Issue: Financial covenants unspecified – loan agreement contains "financial reporting" obligations but no specific covenants documented

Impact: Creates uncertainty about compliance status and potential Events of Default.

Status Post-Recap: ✅ MITIGATED – CBS Loan Variation & Waiver Deed V6 Clause 5.2: CBS confirms no Event of Default has occurred or is continuing as of deed date.

Residual Action:

Loan repayment at close eliminates compliance risk

Include CBS "no default" confirmation from Deed V6 in data room

Issue: Interest rate mechanism unclear – "approximately 8.60% per annum" lacks precise calculation method

Impact: May create disputes about final payoff amount.

Status Post-Recap: ⚠️ ACTION REQUIRED – Need to confirm exact payoff amount before Series A close.

Residual Action:

Engage with CBS (Jim Ellwood) to agree final payoff amount

CBS Loan Variation & Waiver Deed V6 Clause 6.3: No prepayment penalties apply

Target: 5 Business Days before close (per Deed Clause 6.3(a))

Issue: Related party characterisation – Jeff Dusting is director of both CBS and WaterRoads

Impact: Loan is related-party transaction requiring s228 analysis and potentially Chapter 2E compliance.

SECTION E – RELATED PARTY & CONFLICT OF INTEREST

SECTION OVERVIEW: The identification of the spousal relationship between Sarah Taylor and Jeff Dusting (Issue E5, discovered February 2026) fundamentally reframes the analysis of all Section E issues. The original assessment assumed Sarah could act as disinterested director for CBS-related matters (Jeff's conflict only). The spousal relationship means neither director can be disinterested on any CobaltBlu or CBS matter. This section has been updated to reflect this structural reality.

E5 – CRITICAL [NEW]

Issue: Sarah Taylor and Jeff Dusting are married. Neither director disclosed spousal relationship in any s191 notice, board minutes, or corporate record. Spousal relationship means neither director can be considered disinterested in any matter involving CobaltBlu, CBS Group, or each other's interests. No related-party transaction since incorporation has had genuinely independent board oversight.

Severity: CRITICAL

Legal Basis:

Section 191 Corporations Act 2001 (Cth) – failure to disclose material personal interest (strict liability offence, 50 penalty units / $22,200 per director)

Section 228 – spouse of director is related party

Constitution Cl 48.1 – requires disinterested director approval for related-party transactions

Impact:

Recapitalisation resolution potentially voidable if s191 disclosure not made

All CBS-related board actions lack genuinely disinterested approval

Series A investor DD will identify relationship immediately (same residential address on ASIC records)

Criminal penalty exposure: up to $22,200 per director for non-disclosure

Status Post-Recap: ⚠️ ACTIVE REMEDIATION – WEEK 1 CRITICAL PATH

Residual Action:

IMMEDIATE: Execute s192 Standing Notices for both directors disclosing:

CobaltBlu directorships and 50/50 beneficial ownership

Spousal relationship

Jeff's CBS Group directorship

Week 2: Reframe confirmatory board minutes: both directors disclosed, both voted under s194, no disinterested director available

Week 2: Update Governance Narrative and Conflict Disclosure Memo to include spousal relationship

Week 3: Elevate independent director appointment to critical path – target appointment at or within 60 days of Series A close

Upload Standing Notices, updated minutes, and Governance Narrative to data room

Owner: Both directors (notices); Company Secretary (minutes); CEO (independent director search)

Target: Standing Notices Week 1 | Updated minutes Week 2 | Independent director shortlist Week 3

[ ] Upload CBS Loan Variation & Waiver Deed V6 to data room

[ ] Upload Constitution V3 to data room

Week 2 Actions

[ ] Prepare confirmatory board minutes (F1) with spousal relationship disclosure

[ ] Prepare CEO appointment resolution (F3)

[ ] Prepare Company Secretary appointment resolution (F4)

[ ] Update Governance Narrative and Conflict Disclosure Memo (E5, E1, E2)

[ ] Upload all updated governance documents to data room

Week 3 Actions

[ ] Issue formal option grant letters

[ ] Prepare independent director shortlist (E5)

[ ] Finalize data room structure and upload all remediation documents

At Series A Close

[ ] Repay CBS loan in full (~$209,000) from Series A proceeds

[ ] Obtain CBS discharge deed within 2 Business Days (CBS Loan Variation & Waiver Deed V6 Clause 6.4)

[ ] Obtain PPSR discharge confirmations (if applicable)

[ ] Upload CBS discharge documentation to data room

Within 60 Days Post-Close

[ ] Appoint independent director (E5, E3)

[ ] File ASIC Form 484 for new director appointment
