### 03.1 WaterRoads_Constitution_V3.1_COMPLETE.docx

*File: `03.1 WaterRoads_Constitution_V3.1_COMPLETE.docx`*

WATER ROADS PTY LTD

ACN 686 900 014

AMENDED AND RESTATED 

Adopted by special resolution on [  ] 2026

Effective from 15 January 2026

This constitution replaces in its entirety the constitution adopted on incorporation (8 May 2025) and the Deed of Amendment to Constitution dated 1 August 2025.

CONFIDENTIAL

TABLE OF CONTENTS

PART 1 — PRELIMINARY

1.	Name

1.1	The name of the Company is Water Roads Pty Ltd.

2.	Replaceable Rules

2.1	The replaceable rules in the Corporations Act do not apply to the Company to the extent they are displaced or modified by this Constitution.

2.2	To the extent a replaceable rule is not displaced or modified by this Constitution, it applies as a term of this Constitution.

3.	Definitions and Interpretation

3.1	In this Constitution, unless the context otherwise requires:

"ASIC" means the Australian Securities and Investments Commission.

"Board" means the board of directors of the Company from time to time.

"Business Day" means a day that is not a Saturday, Sunday, or public holiday in New South Wales, Australia.

"CBS Group" means CBS Group Pty Ltd (ACN 164 870 080).

"CEO" means the chief executive officer of the Company appointed under clause 19.

"CobaltBlu" means CobaltBlu Pty Ltd (ACN 103 595 071).

"Common Shares" means the class of shares in the capital of the Company designated as Common Shares and having the rights, privileges, and restrictions set out in clause 5.

"Company" means Water Roads Pty Ltd (ACN 686 900 014).

"Corporations Act" means the Corporations Act 2001 (Cth), as amended from time to time.

"Director" means a director of the Company from time to time.

"ESOP" means the Employee Share Option Plan established under clause 26.

"F Share Majority" means the holders of more than 50% of the F Shares on issue (calculated on an as-converted basis), voting as a separate class.

"F Shares" means the class of shares in the capital of the Company designated as F Shares and having the rights, privileges, and restrictions set out in clause 4.

"Founder Directors" means directors appointed by the F Share Majority under clause 16.2.

"Founders" means, collectively, Sarah Margaret Taylor and Jeffrey Alan Dusting, and their respective controlled entities (including CobaltBlu), and “Founder” means any one of them.

"Fully Diluted Basis" means the total number of Shares that would be on issue if all options, warrants, convertible securities, and other rights to acquire Shares were exercised or converted in full.

"Independent Director" means a Director who is not: (a) a Founder or an associate of a Founder; (b) an employee or officer of the Company (other than as a non-executive director); (c) a director, officer, or employee of any entity that is a related party of the Company within the meaning of section 228 of the Corporations Act; or (d) a spouse, de facto partner, parent, child, or sibling of any person described in (a) to (c).

"Investor Director" means a Director nominated by the Investor Majority under clause 16.3.

"Investor Majority" means: (a) while any single holder of Series A Preferred Shares holds 40% or more of all Series A Preferred Shares on issue, that holder; or (b) otherwise, the holders of more than 50% of the Series A Preferred Shares on issue, voting as a separate class.

"Investor Reserved Matters" means the matters listed in clause 21.2.

"Member" means a person entered in the Register as a holder of one or more Shares.

"Qualifying Financing" means the completion of one or more equity capital raisings by the Company in a single round or series of related closings, with aggregate gross cash proceeds to the Company of not less than A$5,000,000, on terms approved by the Board and the F Share Majority.

"Register" means the register of members maintained under section 169 of the Corporations Act.

"Related Party Transaction" means a transaction or arrangement in which a Director, a Founder, or an associate (within the meaning of sections 10–12 of the Corporations Act) of any of them has a material personal interest.

"Series A Preferred Shares" means the class of shares in the capital of the Company designated as Series A Preferred Shares, to be created and issued on terms determined by the Board and the F Share Majority in connection with a Qualifying Financing, and having such rights, privileges, and restrictions as are set out in the SHA or any amendment to this Constitution adopted in connection with that Qualifying Financing.

"SHA" means any shareholders’ agreement entered into by the Company and its Members (or any of them) from time to time, as amended or restated.

"Shares" means shares in the capital of the Company, including F Shares, Common Shares, and Series A Preferred Shares, and “Share” means any one of them.

"Special Majority" means a resolution passed by at least 75% of the votes cast by Members entitled to vote on the resolution.

3.2	In this Constitution, unless the context otherwise requires:

(a)	a reference to a clause is a reference to a clause of this Constitution;

(b)	a reference to a statute includes any amendment, re-enactment, or replacement of that statute;

(c)	headings are for convenience only and do not affect interpretation;

(d)	words importing the singular include the plural and vice versa;

(e)	where a word or phrase is defined, its other grammatical forms have a corresponding meaning;

(f)	a reference to a person includes a body corporate, partnership, unincorporated association, trust, and governmental or semi-governmental body;

(g)	a reference to “in writing” includes email and any other form of electronic communication permitted by the Corporations Act; and

(h)	a reference to A$ or dollars is a reference to Australian dollars.

PART 2 — SHARE CAPITAL

4.	F Shares

4.1	Voting. Each F Share confers on its holder the right to one vote on a poll at a general meeting of the Company or on any written resolution of Members.

4.2	Dividends. F Shares rank equally with Common Shares for dividends, with each F Share entitled to participate pro rata in any dividend or distribution declared by the Company on the same terms as each Common Share.

4.3	Capital. On a winding up or return of capital, F Shares rank equally with Common Shares, with each F Share entitled to participate pro rata in the distribution of surplus assets on the same basis as each Common Share, subject to the prior rights (if any) of Series A Preferred Shares as determined at the time of the Qualifying Financing.

4.4	Conversion. Each F Share will automatically convert into one Common Share, on a one-for-one basis, upon the earlier of:

(a)	completion of a Qualifying Financing; or

(b)	a written election by the F Share Majority to convert all (but not some only) F Shares to Common Shares.

4.5	Upon conversion under clause 4.4, the Company must update the Register to reflect the conversion. No additional consideration is payable. Conversion does not affect the number of Shares held, only the class designation. Following conversion, the converted Shares carry the rights of Common Shares.

4.6	Class rights. The rights attaching to F Shares are class rights for the purposes of section 246B of the Corporations Act and may only be varied or cancelled with the written consent of the F Share Majority.

5.	Common Shares

5.1	Voting. Each Common Share confers on its holder the right to one vote on a poll at a general meeting of the Company or on any written resolution of Members.

5.2	Dividends. Common Shares rank equally with F Shares for dividends, with each Common Share entitled to participate pro rata in any dividend or distribution declared by the Company on the same terms as each F Share.

5.3	Capital. On a winding up or return of capital, Common Shares rank equally with F Shares, with each Common Share entitled to participate pro rata in the distribution of surplus assets on the same basis as each F Share, subject to the prior rights (if any) of Series A Preferred Shares as determined at the time of the Qualifying Financing.

5.4	Class rights. The rights attaching to Common Shares are class rights for the purposes of section 246B of the Corporations Act and may only be varied or cancelled with the written consent of holders of more than 75% of the Common Shares on issue.

6.	Series A Preferred Shares

6.1	The Company is authorised to create and issue Series A Preferred Shares on completion of a Qualifying Financing. The rights, privileges, restrictions, and conditions attaching to Series A Preferred Shares will be determined by the Board and the F Share Majority, and will be set out in:

(a)	an amendment to this Constitution adopted by special resolution in connection with the Qualifying Financing; and/or

(b)	the SHA.

6.2	To the extent of any inconsistency between this Constitution and the SHA in relation to the rights attaching to Series A Preferred Shares, the SHA prevails (clause 22).

6.3	Until Series A Preferred Shares are created and issued, the provisions of this Constitution relating to Series A Preferred Shares, Investor Majority, Investor Director, and Investor Reserved Matters are dormant and have no effect.

7.	Issue of Shares

7.1	Subject to the Corporations Act, this Constitution, and the Founder Protective Provisions (clause 20), the Board may issue, or grant options over, Shares on such terms as the Board determines.

7.2	The Board must not issue Shares, or grant options over Shares, without the prior written approval of the F Share Majority, except:

(a)	Shares issued pursuant to the Qualifying Financing on terms approved by the F Share Majority;

(b)	Shares or options issued under the ESOP within the 10% pool authorised by clause 26; and

(c)	Shares issued on conversion of F Shares under clause 4.4.

7.3	All Shares must be fully paid on issue.

8.	Pre-emptive Rights

8.1	Subject to clauses 8.3 and 8.4, before issuing any new Shares (other than on conversion of existing securities), the Company must first offer those Shares to the existing Members pro rata to their existing holdings (calculated on a Fully Diluted Basis), on the same terms and at the same price as the proposed issue.

8.2	The offer under clause 8.1 must be in writing, specify the number and class of Shares, the issue price, the terms of issue, and the date by which the offer must be accepted (which must be at least 15 Business Days after the offer is given).

8.3	ESOP carve-out. Pre-emptive rights under this clause 8 do not apply to the issue of Shares or options under the ESOP within the 10% pool authorised by clause 26.

8.4	Qualifying Financing carve-out. Pre-emptive rights under this clause 8 do not apply to the issue of Series A Preferred Shares pursuant to a Qualifying Financing, provided the F Share Majority has approved the terms of that Qualifying Financing.

8.5	If any Member does not accept its full entitlement under clause 8.1, the Shares not taken up may be offered to other Members who accepted their entitlement in full, pro rata, before being offered to any third party.

PART 3 — TRANSFER OF SHARES

9.	Transfer Restrictions

9.1	A Member must not transfer any Shares except in accordance with this Part 3.

9.2	The Board may, in its absolute discretion, refuse to register a transfer of Shares. The Board is not required to give reasons for any refusal.

9.3	No transfer of Shares may be registered unless:

(a)	the transfer instrument is in a form approved by the Board and is delivered to the Company, together with any certificate for the Shares and such other evidence of title as the Board may require;

(b)	the right of first refusal process in clause 10 has been completed or waived; and

(c)	any applicable restrictions in the SHA have been satisfied.

9.4	Permitted transfers. A Member may transfer Shares without complying with the right of first refusal in clause 10 to:

(a)	a body corporate controlled by that Member (within the meaning of section 50AA of the Corporations Act);

(b)	a trustee of a trust of which that Member (or, in the case of an individual, that individual or their spouse) is a beneficiary;

(c)	in the case of an individual Member, the Member’s spouse, de facto partner, or immediate family member; or

(d)	any person approved in writing by the F Share Majority and (if Series A Preferred Shares are on issue) the Investor Majority,

provided the transferee agrees in writing to be bound by this Constitution and the SHA (if any).

10.	Right of First Refusal

10.1	A Member who wishes to transfer Shares (Selling Member) must, before offering the Shares to any third party, give written notice to the Company (Transfer Notice) specifying the number and class of Shares proposed to be transferred, the proposed price per Share, and the name of the proposed transferee (if known).

10.2	Within 5 Business Days of receiving the Transfer Notice, the Company must give a copy of the Transfer Notice to each other Member.

10.3	Each other Member may, within 20 Business Days of receiving the Transfer Notice (Acceptance Period), give written notice to the Company that it wishes to purchase some or all of the Shares specified in the Transfer Notice, at the price and on the terms specified in the Transfer Notice, pro rata to its existing holding (calculated on a Fully Diluted Basis).

10.4	If the other Members in aggregate elect to purchase all of the Shares specified in the Transfer Notice, the Selling Member must transfer those Shares to the purchasing Members within 10 Business Days of the end of the Acceptance Period.

10.5	If the other Members do not in aggregate elect to purchase all of the Shares specified in the Transfer Notice, the Selling Member may, within 60 Business Days after the end of the Acceptance Period, transfer the unsold Shares to the proposed transferee (or any other bona fide third party) at a price not less than, and on terms no more favourable than, those specified in the Transfer Notice.

10.6	If the Selling Member does not complete the transfer within the period specified in clause 10.5, the Selling Member must recommence the right of first refusal process before making any further transfer.

11.	Drag-Along Rights

11.1	If the F Share Majority resolves to accept a bona fide offer from an arm’s length third party to acquire all of the issued Shares in the Company (Sale Offer), and the Sale Offer has been approved by:

(a)	the F Share Majority; and

(b)	if Series A Preferred Shares are on issue, the Investor Majority,

then each other Member (Dragged Member) must transfer its Shares to the acquirer on the same terms and at the same price per Share (adjusted for class rights) as the F Share Majority and Investor Majority (if applicable) have agreed.

11.2	The Company must give each Dragged Member at least 20 Business Days’ written notice of the Sale Offer, including full details of the price, terms, and identity of the acquirer.

11.3	The price payable to each Dragged Member must be:

(a)	not less than the price per Share payable to the F Share Majority (adjusted for any liquidation preference or priority applicable to the Dragged Member’s class of Shares); and

(b)	determined on a basis that is fair and equitable to all Members, having regard to the rights attaching to each class of Shares.

11.4	No Member may be required to give warranties, indemnities, or representations in connection with a drag-along transfer other than: (a) as to title and authority to transfer; and (b) a several (not joint) pro rata share of any general warranty cap agreed by the selling Members.

12.	Tag-Along Rights

12.1	If any Member or group of Members holding in aggregate 50% or more of the issued Shares (Majority Seller) proposes to transfer Shares to a third party (other than a Permitted Transfer under clause 9.4), each other Member (Tagging Member) has the right to participate in the transfer on the same terms and at the same price per Share (adjusted for class rights).

12.2	The Majority Seller must give each Tagging Member at least 20 Business Days’ written notice of the proposed transfer, including the price, terms, and identity of the proposed acquirer.

12.3	Each Tagging Member may, within 15 Business Days of receiving notice under clause 12.2, give written notice to the Majority Seller that it wishes to include some or all of its Shares in the transfer.

12.4	If the proposed acquirer is unwilling to acquire all of the Shares that Tagging Members wish to include, the number of Shares to be sold by the Majority Seller and each Tagging Member must be reduced pro rata to their respective holdings.

12.5	If the Majority Seller does not comply with this clause 12, the Company must refuse to register the transfer.

13.	Transmission of Shares

13.1	If a Member who is an individual dies, the Company must recognise the Member’s personal representative as having the rights of the deceased Member in relation to the Shares, subject to production of such evidence of title as the Board may require.

13.2	A person who becomes entitled to a Share by reason of the death, bankruptcy, or mental incapacity of a Member may elect to be registered as the holder of the Share or to have some other person registered, subject to clause 9.

PART 4 — GENERAL MEETINGS

14.	General Meetings

14.1	General meetings of the Company must be convened and held in accordance with Part 2G.2 of the Corporations Act.

14.2	A Director or any Member holding at least 5% of the issued Shares may call a general meeting.

14.3	At least 10 Business Days’ notice of a general meeting must be given to all Members entitled to attend and vote, or such shorter notice as all Members agree.

15.	Proceedings at General Meetings

15.1	A quorum for a general meeting is two Members present in person or by proxy, representative, or attorney holding in aggregate at least 50% of the issued Shares.

15.2	If a quorum is not present within 30 minutes of the time appointed for a meeting, the meeting is adjourned to the same day in the following week at the same time and place. If a quorum is not present within 30 minutes at the adjourned meeting, the Members present constitute a quorum.

15.3	Resolutions of Members may be passed as ordinary resolutions (more than 50% of votes cast) or special resolutions (at least 75% of votes cast), as required by this Constitution or the Corporations Act.

15.4	A resolution in writing signed by all Members entitled to vote on the resolution is as valid as if it had been passed at a general meeting. The resolution may consist of several documents in the same form, each signed by one or more Members.

15.5	On a show of hands, each Member present has one vote. On a poll, each Member has one vote for each Share held. A poll may be demanded by the chair, by any Member present, or by a proxy.

PART 5 — DIRECTORS

16.	Appointment and Composition of the Board

16.1	Board size. 

(a)	Pre-Qualifying Financing: The Board must consist of not fewer than 2 and not more than 5 Directors.

(b)	Post-Qualifying Financing: The Board must consist of not fewer than 3 and not more than 7 Directors, including at least one Independent Director appointed at or within 60 days of completion of the Qualifying Financing.

16.2	Founder Director right. While the Founders (directly or through CobaltBlu or any controlled entity) hold Shares representing at least 20% of all issued Shares (on a Fully Diluted Basis), the F Share Majority has the right to appoint and remove:

(a)	if the Board has fewer than 5 Directors, at least 2 Founder Directors; or

(b)	if the Board has 5 or more Directors, a number of Founder Directors equal to 50% of the Board (rounded up to the nearest whole number),

by written notice to the Company. The F Share Majority’s right to appoint Founder Directors subsists regardless of whether a Qualifying Financing has been completed.

16.3	Investor Director right. Following completion of a Qualifying Financing, the Investor Majority has the right to nominate one person for appointment to the Board as the Investor Director, subject to the following:

(a)	the nominee must be reasonably acceptable to the F Share Majority (such acceptance not to be unreasonably withheld, but may be withheld on grounds of material conflict of interest, lack of relevant expertise, or conduct that would be inconsistent with the Company’s values or regulatory obligations);

(b)	if the F Share Majority objects to a nominee, the F Share Majority must provide written reasons within 10 Business Days and the Investor Majority may nominate an alternative person;

(c)	the Investor Director right subsists while the holders of Series A Preferred Shares hold in aggregate at least 10% of all issued Shares (on a Fully Diluted Basis); and

(d)	the Investor Majority may remove and replace the Investor Director by written notice to the Company.

16.4	Independent Director. Following completion of a Qualifying Financing, the Board must include at least one Independent Director. The Independent Director must be appointed by ordinary resolution of the Board with the approval of both the F Share Majority and the Investor Majority (if Series A Preferred Shares are on issue). If the parties cannot agree on an Independent Director within 60 days after completion of the Qualifying Financing, any party may refer the appointment to binding nomination by a mutually agreed independent body (such as the Australian Institute of Company Directors).

16.5	Removal. A Director may be removed by the person or class that appointed that Director. For the avoidance of doubt:

(a)	Founder Directors may only be removed by the F Share Majority;

(b)	the Investor Director may only be removed by the Investor Majority; and

(c)	the Independent Director may be removed by ordinary resolution of the Board with the approval of both the F Share Majority and the Investor Majority (if applicable).

16.6	Casual vacancies. The Board may appoint a person to fill a casual vacancy, but any such appointment must be confirmed at the next general meeting.

16.7	No retirement by rotation. Directors are not required to retire by rotation.

16.8	Remuneration. Directors are entitled to such remuneration for their services as the Board determines, subject to any limits imposed by the SHA or by resolution of Members. Directors are entitled to be reimbursed for reasonable expenses incurred in performing their duties.

17.	Proceedings of Directors

17.1	Directors may meet together to transact business, adjourn, and otherwise regulate their meetings as they see fit.

17.2	A Director may call a meeting of Directors at any time by giving reasonable notice to each other Director.

17.3	Quorum. A quorum for a meeting of Directors is a majority of the Directors holding office at the time of the meeting. If an Independent Director has been appointed, the Independent Director must be present (in person or by electronic communication) to constitute a quorum for any resolution involving a Related Party Transaction.

17.4	If a quorum cannot be formed because the only Directors available are interested Directors, the interested Directors may meet and transact business in reliance on section 194 of the Corporations Act, provided all interests have been disclosed in accordance with clause 18.

17.5	Chair. The Directors may elect a chair from among their number. If no chair is elected, or the chair is not present within 15 minutes of the time appointed for the meeting, the Directors present may choose one of their number to chair the meeting.

17.6	A resolution in writing signed by all Directors (or all Directors entitled to vote on the resolution, in the case of a resolution from which a Director has been excluded under clause 18) is as valid as if it had been passed at a meeting.

17.7	Directors may participate in meetings by telephone, video conference, or other electronic communication, and are taken to be present in person.

18.	Director Conflicts and Related Party Transactions

18.1	Disclosure. A Director who has a material personal interest in a matter relating to the affairs of the Company must disclose the nature and extent of that interest to the other Directors in accordance with sections 191 and 192 of the Corporations Act.

18.2	Standing notices. A Director may give a standing notice of interest under section 192 of the Corporations Act, which must be tabled at the next meeting of Directors.

18.3	Where Independent Director available. Where the Company has appointed an Independent Director, a Related Party Transaction must be approved by a resolution of the Board that includes the affirmative vote of at least one Independent Director. The interested Director(s) may be present and vote on the resolution (in reliance on section 194 of the Corporations Act), but the approval of an Independent Director is required in addition to any majority otherwise required.

18.4	Where no Independent Director available. Where the Company has not yet appointed an Independent Director, or the Independent Director is unable to act (by reason of vacancy, illness, or own interest in the matter), the following procedure applies:

(a)	all interested Directors must disclose their interests in accordance with clause 18.1;

(b)	the interested Directors may be present and vote on the resolution in reliance on section 194 of the Corporations Act (the Company being a proprietary company);

(c)	the Board must record in the minutes: the nature and extent of each Director’s interest, the disclosure made, the reliance on section 194, and the commercial rationale for the transaction; and

(d)	the Board must consider whether the transaction is on arm’s length terms and, if not, whether it is reasonable and in the best interests of the Company.

18.5	Chapter 2E. Nothing in this clause 18 limits the application of Chapter 2E of the Corporations Act (related party transactions) to the Company. Where Chapter 2E requires member approval for a related party benefit, the Company must obtain that approval unless an exception in sections 210–216 applies.

18.6	Record keeping. The Company must maintain a register of all Related Party Transactions approved under this clause 18, including the date, parties, terms, disclosures made, and the basis of approval. This register must be available for inspection by any Director or Member on reasonable notice.

19.	CEO and Officers

19.1	The Board may appoint a CEO on such terms as the Board determines. The appointment and removal of the CEO is a Founder Protective Provision matter under clause 20.

19.2	The CEO may exercise such powers and perform such duties as the Board delegates, subject to:

(a)	the Corporations Act;

(b)	this Constitution;

(c)	any resolution of the Board; and

(d)	any SHA.

19.3	Unless the Board otherwise determines, the CEO may not, without prior Board approval:

(a)	issue, allot, or grant options over Shares;

(b)	enter into any commitment, contract, or arrangement with a value exceeding A$500,000 (or such other amount as the Board determines);

(c)	commence or settle any litigation or arbitration;

(d)	hire or terminate senior employees (being those reporting directly to the CEO); or

(e)	incur any capital expenditure exceeding A$250,000 (or such other amount as the Board determines).

19.4	The Board may appoint a Company Secretary and any other officers on such terms as the Board determines.

PART 6 — GOVERNANCE AND PROTECTIVE PROVISIONS

20.	Founder Protective Provisions

20.1	This clause 20 applies while the Founders (directly or through CobaltBlu or any controlled entity) hold Shares representing at least 30% of all issued Shares (on a Fully Diluted Basis).

20.2	The Company must not, and the Board must not resolve to, take any of the following actions without the prior written consent of the F Share Majority:

(a)	amend, vary, or repeal this Constitution, or adopt a new constitution;

(b)	create any new class of Shares, or vary or abrogate the rights attaching to any existing class of Shares;

(c)	issue any Shares or securities convertible into Shares, or grant any options, warrants, or other rights to acquire Shares, other than: (i) pursuant to a Qualifying Financing approved by the F Share Majority; or (ii) under the ESOP within the limits of clause 26;

(d)	undertake any share buyback, capital reduction, or return of capital;

(e)	appoint or remove the CEO;

(f)	change the Company’s name, or the nature or scope of the Company’s business;

(g)	enter into any merger, consolidation, scheme of arrangement, or other business combination;

(h)	sell, transfer, or dispose of all or substantially all of the Company’s assets, or any asset or group of related assets with a value exceeding A$1,000,000;

(i)	voluntarily wind up the Company, appoint an administrator, or pass a resolution for the Company to enter into any form of external administration;

(j)	declare or pay any dividend or make any distribution to Members;

(k)	incur or guarantee any indebtedness exceeding A$1,000,000 in aggregate (other than trade payables incurred in the ordinary course of business);

(l)	grant any security interest over the Company’s assets (other than liens arising by operation of law in the ordinary course of business);

(m)	enter into any Related Party Transaction with a value exceeding A$50,000;

(n)	appoint or remove any Director other than the Investor Director (whose appointment and removal is governed by clause 16.3);

(o)	adopt or materially amend the Company’s annual budget or business plan;

(p)	enter into any agreement that restricts the Company’s ability to conduct its business in any material respect; and

(q)	approve any transaction or series of related transactions outside the ordinary course of business with a value exceeding A$500,000.

20.3	ESOP cap. The total number of Shares and options available under the ESOP must not exceed 10% of the total issued Shares (on a Fully Diluted Basis), unless an increase is approved by ordinary resolution of Members.

20.4	Interaction with Founder Director rights. For the avoidance of doubt, the threshold for Founder Protective Provisions under this clause 20 (30% on a Fully Diluted Basis) is higher than the threshold for Founder Director appointment rights under clause 16.2 (20% on a Fully Diluted Basis). If the Founders’ holding falls below 30% but remains at or above 20%, the Founder Protective Provisions in this clause 20 will cease to apply, but the Founders will retain their rights to appoint Founder Directors under clause 16.2 and will continue to have board-level governance participation.

20.5	Residual protections below 30%. If the Founders’ holding falls below 30% (on a Fully Diluted Basis) such that this clause 20 ceases to apply:

(a)	the Founders retain their Founder Director appointment rights under clause 16.2 (subject to the 20% threshold in that clause);

(b)	the Founders retain all class rights attaching to F Shares under clause 4, including the right under clause 4.6 to consent to any variation or cancellation of F Share class rights;

(c)	the Founders retain the right under clause 22.3 to withhold consent to any SHA provision that would derogate from the Founder Protective Provisions; and

(d)	any amendment to this clause 20 (including to the 30% threshold) continues to require the consent of the F Share Majority under clause 30.4, regardless of the Founders’ percentage holding at the time.

21.	Investor Reserved Matters

21.1	This clause 21 applies from and after the completion of a Qualifying Financing, and only while the holders of Series A Preferred Shares hold in aggregate at least 20% of all issued Shares (on a Fully Diluted Basis).

21.2	The Company must not, and the Board must not resolve to, take any of the following actions without the prior written consent of the Investor Majority:

(a)	amend this Constitution in a manner that adversely affects the rights of holders of Series A Preferred Shares;

(b)	create any new class of Shares ranking in priority to, or pari passu with, the Series A Preferred Shares as to dividends, return of capital, or voting;

(c)	issue any Shares or convertible securities (other than under the ESOP within the limits of clause 26) at a price per Share lower than the price per Series A Preferred Share at the most recent Qualifying Financing;

(d)	undertake any share buyback or capital reduction affecting Series A Preferred Shares;

(e)	incur or guarantee indebtedness exceeding A$2,000,000 in aggregate;

(f)	grant any security interest over the Company’s assets;

(g)	sell, transfer, or dispose of all or substantially all of the Company’s assets, or any asset with a value exceeding A$1,000,000 (other than in the ordinary course of business);

(h)	enter into any merger, consolidation, or scheme of arrangement;

(i)	voluntarily wind up the Company or enter into any form of external administration;

(j)	declare or pay any dividend or distribution;

(k)	enter into any Related Party Transaction exceeding A$50,000;

(l)	change the nature or scope of the Company’s business;

(m)	adopt or materially amend the Company’s annual budget or business plan; and

(n)	approve any transaction or series of related transactions outside the ordinary course of business with a value exceeding A$1,000,000.

21.3	For the avoidance of doubt, where an action requires both F Share Majority consent under clause 20 and Investor Majority consent under this clause 21, both consents must be obtained.

22.	Shareholders’ Agreement Supremacy

22.1	The Members acknowledge that the Company may enter into a SHA that addresses matters also covered by this Constitution, including (without limitation) transfer restrictions, pre-emptive rights, board composition, reserved matters, information rights, and exit provisions.

22.2	To the extent of any inconsistency between this Constitution and the SHA:

(a)	as between the parties to the SHA, the SHA prevails; and

(b)	the Members must exercise their rights and powers under this Constitution in a manner consistent with the SHA.

22.3	Nothing in the SHA may derogate from the Founder Protective Provisions (clause 20) without the prior written consent of the F Share Majority.

22.4	A Member who is not a party to the SHA is not bound by its terms, but may not exercise its rights under this Constitution in a manner that would cause the Company to breach the SHA.

PART 7 — DIVIDENDS, ACCOUNTS, AND FINANCE

23.	Dividends and Distributions

23.1	The Board may determine that a dividend or distribution is payable to Members and fix the amount, the time for payment, and the method of payment.

23.2	Subject to any preferential rights attaching to Series A Preferred Shares (as determined at the Qualifying Financing and set out in the SHA), all dividends and distributions must be paid to holders of F Shares and Common Shares pari passu, pro rata to the number of Shares held, without distinction between classes.

23.3	No dividend may be paid except out of profits or as otherwise permitted by the Corporations Act.

23.4	The Board may deduct from any dividend payable to a Member any amount due from that Member to the Company.

23.5	A dividend unclaimed for one year after being declared may be invested or otherwise dealt with by the Board for the benefit of the Company until claimed.

24.	Capitalisation of Profits

24.1	The Board may resolve to capitalise any profits, reserves, or other amounts and apply them in paying up in full unissued Shares to be distributed to Members in proportion to their existing holdings.

25.	Accounts and Audit

25.1	The Board must cause proper financial records to be kept in accordance with section 286 of the Corporations Act.

25.2	The Board must cause financial statements to be prepared for each financial year in accordance with the Corporations Act and applicable Australian Accounting Standards.

25.3	Following completion of a Qualifying Financing, and for so long as any Series A Preferred Shares are on issue, the Company must provide to each Member holding at least 5% of the issued Shares:

(a)	audited annual financial statements within 120 days after the end of each financial year;

(b)	unaudited quarterly management accounts within 45 days after the end of each quarter; and

(c)	any other information reasonably requested by the Investor Majority, provided it is not commercially prejudicial to the Company to provide.

PART 8 — EMPLOYEE SHARE OPTION PLAN

26.	ESOP

26.1	The Company is authorised to establish and administer an Employee Share Option Plan for the purpose of attracting, retaining, and incentivising directors, employees, contractors, and advisers of the Company and its related bodies corporate.

26.2	The Board may adopt ESOP Rules governing the terms on which options or other equity incentives may be granted, including vesting conditions, exercise price, exercise period, forfeiture, and transfer restrictions.

26.3	Pool limit. The maximum number of Shares that may be issued or subject to options under the ESOP must not exceed 10% of the total issued Shares (on a Fully Diluted Basis) at any time, unless an increase is approved by ordinary resolution of Members.

26.4	Exercise price. The exercise price for options granted under the ESOP must be determined by the Board at the time of grant, having regard to any independent valuation obtained and any applicable requirements under Division 83A of the Income Tax Assessment Act 1997 (Cth) for start-up concession eligibility.

26.5	Pre-emptive rights carve-out. The issue of Shares or options under the ESOP within the limits of this clause 26 does not give rise to pre-emptive rights under clause 8.

26.6	No grants before Qualifying Financing pricing. Unless the Board otherwise determines by specific resolution, no ESOP options will be granted until the Series A term sheet is agreed and the option exercise price can be set by reference to the Series A share price or an independent valuation.

26.7	Shares issued on exercise of ESOP options will be Common Shares.

PART 9 — GENERAL

27.	Notices

27.1	A notice may be given by the Company to a Member by delivering it personally, sending it by prepaid post to the Member’s address in the Register, or sending it by email to the email address provided by the Member.

27.2	A notice sent by post is taken to be given 3 Business Days after posting. A notice sent by email is taken to be given on the Business Day after it is sent.

27.3	A notice given to joint holders must be given to the joint holder whose name appears first in the Register.

28.	Indemnity and Insurance

28.1	To the extent permitted by law, the Company indemnifies each person who is or has been a Director, secretary, or officer of the Company against any liability incurred in that capacity, except a liability:

(a)	owed to the Company or a related body corporate;

(b)	for a pecuniary penalty or compensation order under the Corporations Act; or

(c)	incurred in circumstances where the person failed to act in good faith in what the person believed to be in the best interests of the Company.

28.2	The Company may pay a premium for a contract of insurance for a Director, secretary, or officer against any liability incurred in that capacity, except a liability arising out of conduct involving a wilful breach of duty or a contravention of sections 182 or 183 of the Corporations Act.

28.3	The Company may advance legal costs to a Director, secretary, or officer in defending proceedings, on terms determined by the Board, subject to repayment if the person is not entitled to indemnity.

29.	Winding Up

29.1	If the Company is wound up, the liquidator may, with the authority of a special resolution:

(a)	distribute among the Members in kind the whole or any part of the assets of the Company; and

(b)	for that purpose, value any assets and determine how the distribution is to be carried out as between the Members.

29.2	Subject to any preferential rights attaching to Series A Preferred Shares, the surplus assets of the Company on a winding up must be distributed to holders of F Shares and Common Shares pari passu, pro rata to the number of Shares held.

30.	Amendment of Constitution

30.1	This Constitution may only be amended or repealed by special resolution of Members in accordance with section 136 of the Corporations Act.

30.2	While clause 20 applies, any amendment to this Constitution requires the prior written consent of the F Share Majority.

30.3	While clause 21 applies, any amendment to this Constitution that adversely affects the rights of holders of Series A Preferred Shares requires the prior written consent of the Investor Majority.

30.4	For the avoidance of doubt, the following clauses may not be amended without the consent of the F Share Majority (regardless of the Founders’ percentage holding at the time) and (if applicable) the Investor Majority:

(a)	this clause 30;

(b)	clause 16.2 (Founder Director appointment rights), including the 20% threshold;

(c)	clause 20 (Founder Protective Provisions), including the 30% threshold and clauses 20.4 and 20.5; and

(d)	clause 22.3 (SHA may not derogate from Founder Protective Provisions).

SCHEDULE 1 — INITIAL SHARE STRUCTURE

The following share structure is in effect from 15 January 2026, being the date of the Recapitalisation:

Post-Recapitalisation, Pre-Split

Post-Split (10-for-1, effective 22 January 2026)

Fully Diluted (Post-Split, Including ESOP Pool)

Note: CobaltBlu Pty Ltd is beneficially owned 50% by Sarah Margaret Taylor and 50% by Jeffrey Alan Dusting.

EXECUTION

2. DRAFT MINUTES

CBS GROUP PTY LTD

ACN 164 870 080

MINUTES OF BOARD MEETING

Date: 16 January 2026
Time: [Insert time]
Location: [Insert location / video conference]

Directors present:

Jim Ellwood (Chair)

Jeff Dusting

In attendance:

[Company secretary / adviser, if any]

1. Opening, Quorum and Chair

The Chair noted that due notice of the meeting had been given to all directors and that a quorum was present. The meeting was declared open at [time].

Jim Ellwood was elected Chair of the meeting.

The Chair noted that the primary purpose of the meeting was to consider CBS Group's position in relation to the proposed WaterRoads Pty Ltd recapitalisation, shareholding realignment and loan arrangements, following Mr Ellwood's attendance as observer at the WaterRoads board meeting on 15 January 2026.

2. Directors' Interests and Conflicts

2.1 Tabling of Standing Notice

The Chair tabled the Standing Notice of Material Personal Interest dated [insert date] from Mr Jeff Dusting, disclosing his interests in WaterRoads Pty Ltd (ACN 686 900 014), CobaltBlu Pty Ltd, and his spousal relationship with Sarah Margaret Taylor.

The Standing Notice disclosed the following interests:

Directorship and 50% beneficial ownership of CobaltBlu Pty Ltd, which is the majority shareholder of WaterRoads (96% post-Recapitalisation)

Directorship of WaterRoads Pty Ltd

Directorship of CBS Group Pty Ltd

Spousal relationship with Sarah Margaret Taylor, who is also a director of WaterRoads and 50% beneficial owner of CobaltBlu Pty Ltd

The board RESOLVED that the Standing Notice be entered into the Company's records and treated as a standing disclosure for all WaterRoads-related matters.

2.2 Recognition of Related-Party Transactions

The board recognised that CBS Group's dealings with WaterRoads (both the Company's shareholding and loan facility) constitute related-party transactions from Jeff Dusting's perspective.

2.3 Conflict Management Process

The board considered the appropriate process for managing this conflict and RESOLVED that:

Jeff Dusting may remain present during the meeting to provide factual background and answer questions about the WaterRoads position

Jeff Dusting will not vote on any resolutions concerning WaterRoads to ensure an independent CBS Group decision

Jim Ellwood, as the non-conflicted director, will make decisions on behalf of CBS and, where relevant, sign documents for CBS Group Pty Ltd

This approach was adopted to ensure that CBS Group's consent and approvals are given independently of the Taylor–Dusting family interests in CobaltBlu and WaterRoads.

Mr Dusting remained present for background discussion but abstained from voting on all resolutions concerning WaterRoads.

3. Report on WaterRoads Board Meeting – 15 January 2026

Jim Ellwood provided a detailed report of his attendance as observer at the WaterRoads Pty Ltd board meeting held on 15 January 2026.

Mr Ellwood reported that the WaterRoads board meeting covered:

3.1 Due Diligence Risk Register

The WaterRoads board reviewed a comprehensive Due Diligence Risk Register identifying 37 issues across five categories:

Corporate formation and ASIC filings (Section A: 5 issues)

Constitution amendment and director authority (Section B: 4 issues)

CBS subscription and share class creation (Section C: 5 issues)

CBS loan facility and security (Section D: 14 issues)

Related-party conflicts and governance (Section E: 9 issues)

The register identified 6 CRITICAL and 15 HIGH severity issues, concentrated in areas directly affecting CBS Group's interests.

3.2 Proposed Recapitalisation Structure

The WaterRoads board discussed and approved in principle a comprehensive recapitalisation comprising:

Step 1: Cancellation of all legacy shares

1,000 founders/FOU/Class A shares held by CobaltBlu Pty Ltd

100 Class B shares held by CBS Group Pty Ltd

Total: 1,100 shares cancelled

Step 2: Issue of new shares in new class structure

9,600,000 F Shares issued to CobaltBlu Pty Ltd (96%)

400,000 Common Shares issued to CBS Group Pty Ltd (4%)

Total: 10,000,000 shares issued

Step 3: 10-for-1 share split

F Shares: 9,600,000 → 96,000,000

Common Shares: 400,000 → 4,000,000

Total: 100,000,000 shares on issue

Rationale presented by WaterRoads:

Correct historical cap table error: intended 96/4 split was incorrectly implemented as 90.9/9.1 at incorporation

Eliminate all defects in original share class creation and CBS subscription

Create clean chain of title appropriate for institutional Series A investment

Align ASIC filings, constitution and internal registers on single transaction

3.3 CBS Loan – Variation and Discharge Proposal

The WaterRoads board discussed the CBS secured loan facility and identified issues including:

Unregistered (unperfected) security interest

Negative pledge and change-of-control provisions that may affect Series A

Asset disposal restrictions that may constrain future group restructuring

WaterRoads proposed that:

CBS agree to a variation and waiver deed to carve out the Recapitalisation and Series A from restrictive covenants

The loan be repaid in full from Series A proceeds at completion

CBS provide a full discharge of security and covenants upon repayment

3.4 Governance Remediation

The WaterRoads board also addressed:

Tabling of Standing Notices from both Sarah Taylor and Jeff Dusting disclosing their interests and spousal relationship

Adoption of a new Amended & Restated Constitution

Approval in principle of a 10% ESOP framework

Commitment to appoint at least one independent director at or within 60 days of Series A close

3.5 Requests to CBS Group

Mr Ellwood reported that WaterRoads will be requesting CBS Group to:

Consent to the Recapitalisation, including cancellation of CBS's 100 Class B shares and issue of 400,000 Common Shares (4,000,000 post-split)

Waive any claims arising from the reduction in percentage ownership or documentation defects in the original subscription

Vary and waive loan covenants to permit the Recapitalisation and Series A to proceed without triggering defaults

Discharge the loan and security upon full repayment at Series A completion

The board noted that these matters would require CBS Group's careful consideration and formal approval.

The board NOTED the report and thanked Mr Ellwood for attending the WaterRoads meeting as CBS's representative.

4. CBS Equity Position in WaterRoads – Assessment of Recap / 4% Holding

The board discussed CBS Group's current and proposed equity position in WaterRoads.

4.1 Current Position

CBS Group currently holds 100 Class B non-voting shares in WaterRoads, representing approximately 9.09% of the issued capital (100 of 1,100 total shares).

However, the board noted that this 9.09% position was the result of a drafting error at incorporation, where:

The commercial intent was for a 96% founder / 4% CBS supporter split

The share issuance was incorrectly implemented as 1,000 founders + 100 CBS = 90.9% / 9.1%

The correct implementation should have been 2,400 founders + 100 CBS = 96% / 4%

4.2 Proposed Position

Under the Recapitalisation:

CBS's 100 Class B shares will be cancelled

CBS will receive 400,000 Common Shares (10,000,000 share base)

Following 10-for-1 split: 4,000,000 Common Shares of 100,000,000 total

Ownership: 4.00%

4.3 Commercial Assessment

The board considered whether accepting a 4% position (versus the current 9.09% ledger position) is in CBS Group's commercial interests.

Jeff Dusting confirmed that, at the time of the original WaterRoads incorporation discussions, the commercial understanding was that CBS would provide early-stage support in exchange for a small equity stake of approximately 4%, with the founders holding approximately 96%.

Jeff noted that the 9.09% position reflected in the current register was an unintended consequence of the way the share classes were set up, not the intended economic deal.

Jim Ellwood, as independent decision-maker for CBS, assessed that:

CBS's primary interest in WaterRoads is strategic, not financial – supporting a business aligned with CBS's infrastructure and transport expertise

A 4% equity stake in a properly capitalised, Series-A-funded company is commercially more valuable than a 9% stake in a company that cannot raise institutional capital due to cap table defects

CBS's interests are best served by facilitating a clean recapitalisation that enables WaterRoads to attract institutional investment

The Recap proposal corrects the cap table to the originally intended 96/4 split and eliminates legal and governance risks

The board RESOLVED that:

Subject to final legal documentation acceptable to Jim Ellwood, CBS Group approves in principle the conversion of its existing Class B interest into a 4% Common shareholding in WaterRoads Pty Ltd under the proposed Recapitalisation.

(Jeff Dusting abstained from voting on this resolution as a related party.)

5. CBS Loan to WaterRoads – Variation, Waiver and Intended Discharge

The board reviewed CBS Group's loan facility to WaterRoads and the issues identified in the Due Diligence Risk Register.

5.1 Current Loan Position

Principal amount: Approximately A$200,000 (exact amount to be confirmed)

Security: General security deed over WaterRoads' assets (not registered on PPSR)

Restrictive covenants: Negative pledge, change-of-control restrictions, asset disposal limitations

Status: Performing, no defaults

5.2 DD Issues Identified

The board noted that the WaterRoads DD Risk Register identified the following issues with the CBS loan:

Security interest never registered on PPSR (unperfected security)

Negative pledge clause may prevent WaterRoads granting security to Series A investors

Change-of-control provisions may be triggered by Recapitalisation or new equity issuance

Asset disposal restrictions may constrain future group restructuring (HoldCo/OpCo structure)

Absence of formal lender consent provisions for capital structure changes

These issues were described as potentially preventing WaterRoads from completing an institutional Series A raise unless addressed.

5.3 WaterRoads Proposal

WaterRoads has proposed that:

CBS agree to a Loan Variation & Waiver Deed to carve out the Recapitalisation and Series A equity raise from default triggers and restrictive covenants

The loan be repaid in full from Series A proceeds at completion (expected March 2026)

CBS provide a full discharge of the loan and security upon repayment, releasing all covenants and confirming no PPSR registrations remain

5.4 CBS Commercial Assessment

The board discussed CBS Group's strategic position as both equity holder and lender.

Jim Ellwood assessed that:

CBS's loan was provided as early-stage support to enable WaterRoads to commence operations

CBS's risk profile is already equity-like given the company's stage and absence of alternative security

CBS's strategic interest in WaterRoads is more as a long-term shareholder and supporter than as a secured lender

Full repayment at Series A completion, combined with a 4% equity stake in a properly capitalised business, represents a superior outcome for CBS than continuing as a lender with unperfected security

Agreeing to the variation and discharge facilitates WaterRoads' ability to raise institutional capital, which is in CBS's interests as a shareholder

The board RESOLVED that:

Subject to legal documentation satisfactory to Jim Ellwood, CBS Group:

Approves a Loan Variation & Waiver Deed to carve out the Recapitalisation and Series A equity raise from default triggers, negative pledge, change-of-control, and asset disposal restrictions

Agrees in principle to provide a full discharge of the loan and security upon receipt of full repayment at Series A completion

(Jeff Dusting abstained from voting on this resolution as a related party.)

6. Approval to Enter Recap Consent & Waiver and Loan Documents

The board considered the formal documentation required to implement CBS Group's in-principle approvals.

6.1 Required Documents

The board noted that the following documents will be required:

WaterRoads–CBS Recapitalisation Consent & Waiver Deed, including:

CBS's express consent to cancellation of 100 Class B shares

CBS's consent to issue of 400,000 Common Shares (4,000,000 post-split)

Acknowledgement of 4% ownership and confirmation CBS regards this as fair

Waiver of any claims arising from percentage reduction or documentation defects

Confirmation CBS will not allege oppression or seek relief in relation to Recap

CBS Loan Variation & Waiver Deed, including:

Carve-out of Recapitalisation from change-of-control and negative pledge provisions

Carve-out of Series A equity raise from restrictive covenants

Clarification that these transactions are not defaults or mandatory prepayment events

Permission for future group restructuring (HoldCo/LeaseCo/OpCo) if required

CBS Loan Discharge and Release of Security (to be signed at Series A completion), including:

Acknowledgement of receipt of full repayment (principal and accrued interest)

Release and discharge of all security interests, covenants, negative pledges

Confirmation no PPSR registrations remain

Confirmation CBS has no further lender rights or claims

6.2 Related-Party Transaction Recognition

The board noted that these transactions constitute related-party dealings under the Corporations Act given Jeff Dusting's dual directorship of CBS and WaterRoads and his relationship with Sarah Taylor.

To ensure the approvals are independent and defensible, the board confirmed that:

Jeff Dusting has disclosed his interests and will abstain from voting

Jim Ellwood, as non-conflicted director, will make the approval decisions

Jim Ellwood will have authority to sign all documents on behalf of CBS Group Pty Ltd

6.3 Board Resolution

IT WAS RESOLVED that:

CBS Group Pty Ltd approves its entry into:

The WaterRoads–CBS Recapitalisation Consent & Waiver Deed

The CBS Loan Variation & Waiver Deed

The CBS Loan Discharge and Release of Security (to be signed at Series A completion)

on terms substantially consistent with those outlined in this meeting, subject to final legal review.

CBS Group Pty Ltd authorises Jim Ellwood, as non-conflicted director, to:

Review and approve the final form of the above deeds, with any non-material amendments recommended by legal counsel

Execute the deeds and any ancillary documents on behalf of CBS Group Pty Ltd

Do all acts and things necessary to give effect to CBS's consents, waivers and discharge

The Company Secretary is directed to prepare certified copies of these resolutions for provision to WaterRoads and its advisers.

(Jeff Dusting abstained from voting on this resolution as a related party.)

7. Documentation, DD Support and Next Steps

The board discussed CBS Group's role in supporting WaterRoads' due diligence process for the Series A capital raise.

7.1 Documents to be Provided to WaterRoads

The board noted that WaterRoads will need the following documents from CBS for inclusion in the Series A data room:

Executed copy of CBS Recapitalisation Consent & Waiver Deed

Executed copy of CBS Loan Variation & Waiver Deed

CBS board resolutions evidencing approval and authorisation of Jim Ellwood to sign

Copy of these board minutes (with appropriate redactions if necessary)

Loan Discharge and Release (to be provided at Series A completion)

7.2 Purpose of CBS Documentation

The board noted that investors conducting due diligence on WaterRoads will want to see that:

CBS Group's consent to the Recapitalisation was properly authorised and documented

CBS Group's decision-making was independent of the Taylor–Dusting family interests

The loan variation and discharge were approved by appropriate CBS governance processes

There are no residual claims or disputes between CBS and WaterRoads

7.3 Timeline

The board noted that:

WaterRoads intends to execute the Recapitalisation Deed and lodge ASIC filings during February 2026

The Series A capital raise is targeted for completion in early March 2026

CBS should aim to execute the Consent & Waiver and Loan Variation documents by late January / early February 2026

The Loan Discharge will be executed upon receipt of repayment at Series A close

The board RESOLVED that:

CBS Group Pty Ltd will provide to WaterRoads Pty Ltd and its investors, upon request:

Executed copies of the Recapitalisation Consent & Waiver Deed and Loan Variation & Waiver Deed

Certified copies of CBS board resolutions authorising Jim Ellwood to execute these documents

A copy of the minutes of this 16 January 2026 board meeting (with any commercially sensitive information redacted as appropriate)

8. General Business

No other matters were raised.

9. Close

The Chair confirmed that all business on the agenda had been completed.

The Chair thanked the directors for their attendance and careful consideration of the WaterRoads matters.

There being no further business, the meeting was declared closed at [time].

These minutes will be confirmed at the next meeting of the board.

Conflict Management Approach

To ensure CBS Group's decision-making is independent of the Taylor–Dusting family interests in CobaltBlu and WaterRoads:

Jeff Dusting abstains from voting on all CBS board resolutions concerning WaterRoads transactions

Jim Ellwood, as non-conflicted director, makes approval decisions and signs documents on behalf of CBS

CBS board minutes record the conflict disclosure and management process

WaterRoads governance narrative references CBS's independent approval via Jim Ellwood

This approach ensures that CBS Group's consents and waivers are given independently and are defensible to WaterRoads' Series A investors during due diligence.

Corporations Act Compliance

The board has considered the following provisions:

Section 191: Director must disclose material personal interests to other directors

Section 192: Director may give standing notice of interests

Section 195: Interested director must not be present or vote (unless exception applies)

The conflict management approach adopted by CBS ensures:

Full disclosure of Jeff's interests (s191 compliance)

Interested director abstains from voting (s195 compliance)

Non-conflicted director (Jim) makes decisions independently

Process is documented in board minutes for investor due diligence
