### 04.1 WaterRoads_Conflict_of_Interest_Policy_v1. DATA ROOM READYocx.docx

*File: `04.1 WaterRoads_Conflict_of_Interest_Policy_v1. DATA ROOM READYocx.docx`*

WATERROADS PTY LTD

ACN 686 900 014

CONFLICT OF INTEREST POLICY

1.  Purpose

This policy establishes the framework by which directors and officers of WaterRoads Pty Ltd (the Company) identify, disclose, and manage conflicts of interest and material personal interests in connection with the affairs of the Company. It is designed to:

(a) ensure compliance with sections 191, 192, 194, and 195 of the Corporations Act 2001 (Cth) (the Act) and Chapter 2E (Related Party Transactions);

(b) satisfy the disinterested director and related-party provisions of the Company’s Constitution (including Clause 48.1);

(c) provide a clear, auditable governance trail for investors, regulators, and future board members;

(d) meet the governance standards expected by institutional investors, including private equity and venture capital funds undertaking due diligence; and

(e) establish practical procedures that reflect the Company’s current board composition and transition to independent board oversight following the Series A investment.

2.  Scope

This policy applies to all directors of the Company, including any alternate directors, and to any officer or senior manager who participates in board-level decision-making or has authority to bind the Company.

Series A Transition: Upon appointment of an independent director (targeted at or within 60 days of the Series A close), this policy continues to apply to all directors, and the enhanced procedures in Section 7 (Independent Director Oversight) will activate automatically.

Post-Series A Alignment: Within 30 days of Series A close, this policy will be reviewed to ensure alignment with the shareholders’ agreement, reserved matters, investor consent rights, and board composition requirements.

3.  Definitions

In this Policy, unless the context otherwise requires:

4.  Current Board Composition and Standing Disclosures

The Board acknowledges the following facts relevant to conflict management as at the date of this policy:

4.1  Directors and Relationships

Sarah Margaret Taylor — Director, CEO, and Company Secretary. Also Director and 50% beneficial owner of CobaltBlu Pty Ltd (ACN 103 595 071). Spouse of Jeffrey Alan Dusting.

Jeffrey Alan Dusting — Director. Also Director and 50% beneficial owner of CobaltBlu Pty Ltd. Also Director of CBS Group Pty Ltd (ACN 164 870 080). Spouse of Sarah Margaret Taylor.

4.2  Structural Governance Position

The Board acknowledges that, as at the date of this policy:

(a) both directors have material personal interests in all matters involving CobaltBlu (as directors and 50% beneficial owners) and CBS Group (Jeff’s directorship, Sarah’s indirect interest through spousal relationship);

(b) no genuinely disinterested director currently exists on the Board;

(c) the requirement in Constitution Clause 48.1 for disinterested director approval of related-party transactions cannot currently be satisfied by the existing board composition;

(d) section 194 of the Act permits directors of a proprietary company to vote on matters in which they have a material personal interest, provided that interest has been disclosed in accordance with sections 191 or 192; and

(e) the appointment of an independent director at or within 60 days of Series A close will resolve this structural limitation and activate enhanced oversight procedures under Section 7.

4.3  Standing Notices on File

Both directors have executed Standing Notices under section 192 of the Act, tabled at Board Meeting WR-2026-004, disclosing all interests described in Section 4.1 above. Those Standing Notices remain in effect and are filed in the Company’s governance records and investor data room.

5.  Disclosure Obligations

5.1  Statutory Disclosure (s191/s192)

A director who has a material personal interest in a matter relating to the affairs of the Company must, as soon as practicable after becoming aware of the interest, disclose the nature and extent of that interest to the other directors. Disclosure may be given:

(a) orally at a board meeting, to be recorded in the minutes of that meeting (s191); or

(b) by Standing Notice in writing, tabled at the next board meeting (s192).

Penalty for non-disclosure: Section 191(1) creates a strict liability offence carrying a penalty of up to 50 penalty units (currently A$22,200) per director per undisclosed matter.

5.2  When Disclosure Is Required

Disclosure is required whenever a director has, or may reasonably be perceived to have, a material personal interest in a matter before the Board. This includes, without limitation:

(a) any transaction, arrangement, or dealing between the Company and CobaltBlu, CBS Group, or any entity in which a director holds an interest;

(b) any matter that confers or may confer a financial benefit on a related party (as those terms are defined in sections 228–229 of the Act);

(c) any matter in which a director’s spouse, de facto partner, or close family member has a material interest;

(d) any matter in which a director has a conflicting duty to another entity (including a directorship obligation to CobaltBlu or CBS Group);

(e) approval of the Company’s remuneration, equity grants, or benefits to directors or their associates;

(f) any contract or proposed contract in which a director has a direct or indirect pecuniary interest; and

(g) any matter where the director’s judgment may reasonably be perceived as influenced by interests other than the Company’s interests.

5.3  Standing Notices

Where a director’s interest in a matter is of an ongoing nature (for example, a directorship of another entity, a shareholding, or a spousal relationship), the director should give a Standing Notice under section 192. A Standing Notice must:

(a) be in writing;

(b) set out the nature and extent of the interest;

(c) include explicit acknowledgment of the director’s obligations under this Policy;

(d) include a statement that the notice extends to any matter in which the interests may reasonably be perceived to influence the director’s judgment;

(e) be tabled at the next board meeting after it is given; and

(f) be updated whenever the nature or extent of the interest materially changes.

A Standing Notice has ongoing effect and covers all matters within its stated scope. It does not need to be re-given at each meeting, but the Chair should note at the commencement of each meeting whether any Standing Notices are in effect and whether any updates are required.

5.4  Timing and Form

On appointment: Each new director must complete a disclosure form and provide a Standing Notice (if applicable) before attending their first board meeting.

Annually: Each director must confirm annually that their Standing Notice remains current or provide an updated notice.

As conflicts arise: Directors must disclose new conflicts immediately upon becoming aware of them.

At meetings: The Chair will ask for conflict declarations at the start of each meeting for matters on the agenda.

6.  Procedures for Managing Conflicts

6.1  General Procedure

When a conflict of interest or material personal interest is identified in relation to a matter before the Board, the following procedure applies:

Step 1 — Disclosure. The conflicted director discloses the interest (if not already covered by a Standing Notice). The disclosure is recorded in the minutes.

Step 2 — Assessment. The Board (or, where available, the disinterested directors) assesses the nature and severity of the conflict. The assessment considers:

• whether the interest is direct or indirect;

• whether it is financial or non-financial;

• the materiality of the interest and the transaction;

• whether it could objectively influence the director’s judgment;

• whether there is a reasonable perception of conflict; and

• whether Independent Advice or other safeguards are required.

Step 3 — Management. Based on the assessment, the Board applies one or more of the following management strategies:

Step 4 — Record. The minutes of the meeting must record the conflict management approach taken, including:

• which strategy was applied and why;

• if s194 reliance, the commercial rationale for the decision;

• if Independent Advice obtained, the conclusions and where it is filed;

• cross-reference to Register of Interests entry (Appendix B); and

• for Material Transactions, confirmation of arm’s length terms or member approval obtained.

Step 5 — Register Update. The Company Secretary (or, upon activation of Section 11.1, the Governance Custodian) updates the Register of Interests (Appendix B) and Related Party Transaction Register (Appendix A).

6.2  Specific Conflict Protocols

The following standing protocols apply to known, recurring conflicts:

6.2.1  CBS Group Matters

Jeffrey Alan Dusting holds a directorship at CBS Group and owes fiduciary duties to both companies. For any matter involving CBS Group (including but not limited to the Secured Loan Agreement, loan repayment, Recapitalisation consent, and any future dealings):

(a) Jeff must recuse from the decision (leave the meeting for discussion and vote);

(b) Sarah Taylor, as the sole remaining director, discloses her indirect interest through the spousal relationship and votes under s194;

(c) the minutes record Jeff’s recusal, Sarah’s disclosure, and the s194 basis for Sarah’s vote;

(d) all communications with CBS Group on Company matters are directed to Jim Ellwood or another CBS officer independent of the Dusting–Taylor family; and

(e) CBS Group documents requiring execution are signed by a CBS officer other than Jeff (Jim Ellwood is the current appropriate signatory).

Rationale: Jeff has a direct conflict (CBS directorship). Sarah has an indirect conflict (spousal relationship) but is the less-conflicted director for CBS matters because she holds no CBS role. Recusing Jeff and having Sarah vote under s194 with full disclosure is the best available governance outcome pending appointment of an independent director.

Post-Loan Discharge Review: Following repayment and discharge of the CBS Group Secured Loan Agreement, the Board will review these CBS-specific protocols. Upon discharge, Jeff’s CBS directorship remains a standing conflict, but the materiality and operational significance of the conflict is substantially reduced (CBS Group becomes a passive 4% shareholder with no contractual leverage over the Company). The Board may, following that review, reclassify future routine CBS matters as minor conflicts under Section 6.2.4, subject to Jeff continuing to disclose and recuse from any matter in which his CBS duties create a competing obligation.

6.2.2  CobaltBlu Matters

Both directors are directors and 50% beneficial owners of CobaltBlu. Neither director can be disinterested for CobaltBlu matters. For any matter involving CobaltBlu (including but not limited to the Recapitalisation, share issuances, founder equity, and any future dealings):

(a) both directors disclose their interests (covered by Standing Notices);

(b) both directors participate and vote under s194;

(c) the minutes record the disclosures, the s194 basis, and the commercial rationale;

(d) for Material Transactions, the Board obtains Independent Advice (legal, financial, or valuation) to confirm arm’s length terms; and

(e) the rationale emphasises that the transaction serves the Company’s commercial interests and strategic objectives.

Rationale: With both directors equally interested, recusal would leave no quorum. Section 194 participation with full disclosure is the only available mechanism until an independent director is appointed. Independent Advice provides external validation of commercial reasonableness.

6.2.3  Director Remuneration and Benefits

Decisions on director remuneration, equity grants, expense reimbursement, or other benefits to directors or their associates require:

(a) disclosure of the interest by the relevant director(s);

(b) where an independent director has been appointed, approval by the independent director(s);

(c) where no independent director is available, both directors vote under s194 with the decision benchmarked against market comparables (including comparable roles at similar-stage companies, industry surveys, or adviser recommendations) and documented in the minutes;

(d) consideration of whether member approval is required under Chapter 2E (s208); and

(e) for Material Transactions or non-standard arrangements, Independent Advice on market terms.

6.2.4  Materiality Guidance

To assist in applying the conflict management framework, the Board has adopted the following materiality guidance:

Minor conflicts (typically managed via monitoring):

• Transactions under A$10,000 on arm’s length terms

• Standard commercial hospitality or gifts of trivial value (under A$250)

• Matters where the director’s interest is remote or purely theoretical

Material conflicts (require recusal, Independent Advice, or heightened safeguards):

• Transactions exceeding A$50,000

• Any transaction involving non-standard or preferential terms

• Any transaction where the director has competing fiduciary duties

• Director remuneration or equity grants

• Enforcement, waiver, or variation of existing related party contracts

When in doubt, directors should err on the side of disclosure and seek guidance from the Chair or Company Secretary.

6.3  Interim Period Protocol — Pre-Independent Director

High-risk transaction deferral: For the period between Series A close and appointment of the independent director, the following transactions should be deferred unless failure to act would materially prejudice the Company’s interests:

(a) new related-party contracts or arrangements with CobaltBlu or CBS Group (excluding ordinary-course transactions contemplated in existing agreements);

(b) material changes to the terms of the CBS Loan or any other existing related-party arrangement;

(c) significant amendments to director remuneration or equity incentive arrangements; and

(d) any transaction exceeding A$100,000 involving a related party.

Exception for urgent matters: If a high-risk transaction cannot be deferred, the Board must:

• obtain Independent Advice;

• document clearly why deferral would prejudice the Company;

• obtain investor notification or consent if required under the shareholders’ agreement; and

• minute the decision comprehensively.

7.  Independent Director Oversight

7.1  Independent Director Selection

The Series A lead investor will be consulted in the nomination and approval process for the first independent director to ensure the appointee meets institutional investor expectations for independence and expertise.

7.2  Enhanced Conflict Procedures

Once an independent director is appointed:

(a) Related-party transactions must be approved by the independent director(s) before the Board proceeds. Where the independent director does not approve, the matter may only proceed with member approval under s208 or if it falls within a recognised Chapter 2E exception.

(b) CBS Group matters: Jeff recuses. The independent director and Sarah (with spousal interest disclosed) form the decision-making quorum. The independent director’s concurrence is required for any resolution to proceed.

(c) CobaltBlu matters: Both founding directors disclose and participate under s194. The independent director provides a disinterested vote. The independent director’s concurrence is required for the resolution to be treated as having disinterested approval under Constitution Clause 48.1.

(d) Director remuneration: Approval by independent director required. Founding directors may not vote on their own remuneration packages once an independent director is available to provide disinterested oversight.

(e) Quarterly conflict review: The independent director will lead a quarterly review of all Standing Notices, any new conflicts, and the adequacy of conflict management procedures (see Section 9).

7.3  Committee Structures

Upon appointment of the independent director, the Board will consider establishing:

(a) an Audit and Risk Committee (chaired by the independent director); and/or

(b) a Remuneration and Nomination Committee (including the independent director).

These committees, if established, will have specific responsibilities for reviewing related-party transactions, director remuneration, and conflict management processes.

8.  Chapter 2E — Related Party Transactions

The Company must comply with Chapter 2E of the Act when giving a financial benefit to a related party. The Board must consider, for each proposed related-party transaction:

(a) whether the transaction constitutes a “financial benefit” to a “related party” within the meaning of sections 228–229 (noting that each director, CobaltBlu, CBS Group, and the spouse of each director are related parties);

(b) whether an exception under sections 210–216 applies — in particular:

s210: arm’s length exception (terms no more favourable than reasonably expected if dealing at arm’s length)

s211: reasonable remuneration exception

s212: small amounts exception (less than A$5,000 and reasonable in the circumstances)

(c) if no exception applies, whether member approval has been or can be obtained under section 208;

(d) the documentation required to evidence the exception relied upon (for example, Independent Advice, market comparables, valuation report, or legal opinion); and

(e) for Material Transactions (over A$50,000), mandatory Independent Advice to confirm arm’s length terms or commercial reasonableness.

8.1  Related Party Transaction Register

The Board maintains a Related Party Transaction Register (Appendix A) recording each related-party transaction, including:

• date and description of transaction

• related party involved

• Chapter 2E exception relied upon

• supporting documentation (Independent Advice, legal opinion, valuation)

• board approval reference

• cross-reference to minutes

This register is available for inspection by directors, auditors, and (to the extent required) investors, and is maintained in the Company’s governance data room.

8.2  Independent Advice Requirements

The following transactions require Independent Advice:

(a) any related-party transaction exceeding A$50,000;

(b) any related-party transaction involving non-standard or preferential terms;

(c) any material variation, waiver, or enforcement decision relating to existing related-party contracts;

(d) any transaction where reliance on the s210 arm’s length exception is proposed; and

(e) any transaction where the Board determines Independent Advice would strengthen the governance record.

Independent Advice must be filed in the Company’s records, cross-referenced in the minutes, and made available in the investor data room.

9.  Quarterly Conflict Review

The Board will conduct a conflict review at the first board meeting of each calendar quarter (or more frequently if circumstances require). The review will cover:

(a) confirmation that all Standing Notices remain current and accurate;

(b) identification of any new conflicts or changes in existing interests;

(c) review of the Related Party Transaction Register;

(d) assessment of whether conflict management procedures are operating effectively;

(e) any recommendations for policy amendments; and

(f) progress on appointment of independent director (pre-appointment) or effectiveness of independent director oversight (post-appointment).

The outcome of each quarterly review will be recorded in the minutes of the relevant board meeting. Once an independent director is appointed, the independent director will chair the conflict review.

10.  New Director Onboarding

Upon appointment, each new director must:

(a) receive a copy of:

this Policy;

the Company’s Constitution;

any shareholders’ agreement;

copies of all current Standing Notices of other directors;

(b) complete and deliver a disclosure form covering all interests;

(c) execute and deliver a Standing Notice under section 192 disclosing all material personal interests (or confirm in writing that they have none); and

(d) sign a written acknowledgment that they have read, understood, and will comply with this Policy.

The Company Secretary (or Governance Custodian, if appointed under Section 11.1) will maintain a register of all Standing Notices, acknowledgments, and annual attestations, available for inspection in the investor data room.

11.  Record-Keeping

The following records will be maintained by the Company Secretary and made available in the investor data room:

(a) this policy (current version and version history);

(b) all Standing Notices given by directors (current and historical);

(c) board minutes recording conflict disclosures, management decisions, and s194 reliance;

(d) the Register of Interests (Appendix B);

(e) the Related Party Transaction Register (Appendix A);

(f) all Independent Advice obtained in connection with related-party transactions;

(g) quarterly conflict review minutes; and

(h) annual director attestations and onboarding acknowledgments.

Data room structure: These documents will be organised in the investor data room under “Corporate Governance > Conflict of Interest Management” with clear file naming and cross-referencing to board meeting minutes.

11.1  Governance Custodian — Company Secretary Conflict

The Board acknowledges that the current Company Secretary (Sarah Margaret Taylor) is also a director and a conflicted party under this Policy. While the Company Secretary may continue to perform administrative governance functions in the ordinary course, the following safeguards apply:

(a) the independent director, upon appointment, will oversee and have unrestricted access to all conflict-related governance records maintained under this Section 11, and will review those records as part of the quarterly conflict review (Section 9);

(b) within 60 days of appointment of the independent director, the Board will consider whether the Company Secretary function for conflict-related governance records (including the Register of Interests, the Related Party Transaction Register, Standing Notices, and conflict management minutes) should be:

(i)  performed or overseen by the independent director;

(ii)  transferred to an external company secretary; or

(iii)  retained by the current Company Secretary subject to independent director oversight and sign-off.

(c) until an independent director is appointed, both directors will jointly review and countersign all conflict-related register entries and governance filings to provide a mutual check on the integrity of records; and

(d) any material discrepancy in conflict-related records identified by a director, investor, or auditor must be reported to the Board immediately and recorded in the minutes of the next board meeting.

Rationale: The integrity of conflict management depends on the integrity of the underlying records. Where the record-keeper is herself a conflicted party, additional oversight is required to ensure the governance framework is credible to investors and auditors.

12.  Consequences of Breach

A breach of this policy may result in:

(a) the relevant board resolution being voidable (s195);

(b) criminal liability under section 191(1) (strict liability, up to 50 penalty units / A$22,200 per director);

(c) civil liability for breach of fiduciary duties or the statutory duty of good faith (s181) and duty not to improperly use position (s182);

(d) remedial action determined by the Board, which may include requiring the director to resign from the conflicting position, divest the conflicting interest, or (in serious cases) recommending removal from the Board; and

(e) where a breach involves potential Corporations Act contravention, consideration of whether a report to ASIC or other regulator is required.

The Chair must report any material breach to the Board at the next meeting. The Board will determine appropriate action and, if applicable, notify investors.

13.  Review and Amendment

This policy must be reviewed:

(a) within 12 months of adoption (by 5 February 2027);

(b) upon appointment of an independent director (to activate Section 7 and review all procedures);

(c) within 30 days of Series A close (to align with new shareholders’ agreement and investor rights);

(d) upon any material change in the Company’s board composition, shareholding structure, or related-party relationships; and

(e) upon receipt of investor feedback or due diligence requests relating to conflict management.

13.1  Post-Series A Review

Within 30 days of Series A close, the Board will conduct a comprehensive review of this Policy to ensure alignment with:

(a) the shareholders’ agreement, including reserved matters and investor consent rights;

(b) board composition requirements and committee structures;

(c) any specific governance commitments made to Series A investors;

(d) investor expectations for conflict management and independent oversight; and

(e) any updates required following legal advice on the Series A transaction structure.

13.2  Amendment Process

This policy may be amended by resolution of the Board. Any amendment must be:

(a) recorded in the minutes;

(b) communicated to all directors within 7 days;

(c) provided to investors via the data room; and

(d) reflected in an updated version number and effective date.

Adoption

This policy was adopted by resolution of the Board of Directors of WaterRoads Pty Ltd on 5 February 2026 at Board Meeting WR-2026-004.

Appendix A — Related Party Transaction Register

This register records all transactions between the Company and related parties. It is maintained by the Company Secretary (or Governance Custodian) and reviewed quarterly by the Board.

Additional rows to be added as transactions arise. Each entry to be reviewed at the quarterly conflict review (Section 9).

Appendix B — Register of Interests

This register records the material personal interests disclosed by each director. It is maintained by the Company Secretary (or Governance Custodian) and reviewed quarterly by the Board. It supplements (and cross-references) the Standing Notices filed by each director.

Additional rows to be added as directors are appointed or interests change. Jeff Dusting’s CBS Group directorship interest is flagged for review following discharge of the CBS Secured Loan (see Section 6.2.1). Each entry to be confirmed at the quarterly conflict review (Section 9).

Document Control

END OF POLICY



| Version | 1.0 |

| Adopted by the Board | 5 February 2026 (Board Meeting WR-2026-004) |

| Classification | Board Policy — Series A Data Room Document |



| Term | Meaning |

| Conflict of Interest | Any situation in which a director’s personal interests, duties to another entity, or relationships (including spousal, familial, or financial relationships) could, or could reasonably be perceived to, influence their judgment, decisions, or actions in relation to the Company’s affairs. |

| Material Personal Interest | An interest as defined in section 191 of the Act — an interest that could objectively influence, or be seen to influence, the director’s approach to a matter. Includes direct financial interests, interests arising through related entities (such as CobaltBlu or CBS Group), and interests arising through spousal or familial relationships. |

| Related Party | As defined in sections 228–229 of the Act. Includes directors, entities controlled by directors, spouses of directors, and entities in which directors hold material interests. For the avoidance of doubt, CobaltBlu Pty Ltd, CBS Group Pty Ltd, Sarah Margaret Taylor, and Jeffrey Alan Dusting are each related parties of the Company. |

| Disinterested Director | A director who has no material personal interest (direct or indirect, including through spousal relationship) in the matter under consideration and who is not a related party in respect of the relevant transaction. |

| Independent Director | A director who: (a) is not an employee or officer of the Company, CobaltBlu, or CBS Group; (b) has no material business relationship with any of those entities; (c) is not a spouse, de facto partner, or close family member of any other director; and (d) satisfies the independence criteria in ASX Corporate Governance Principles (4th edition, Recommendation 2.3) to the extent applicable, or any independence criteria in the Company’s Constitution or shareholders’ agreement. |

| Standing Notice | A notice given under section 192 of the Act, disclosing the nature and extent of a director’s interests in a matter. A Standing Notice has ongoing effect and covers all future matters within its stated scope until varied or withdrawn. |

| Material Transaction | Any related party transaction involving consideration or value exceeding A$50,000, or any transaction which, regardless of value, is outside ordinary course or involves non-standard terms. |

| Independent Advice | Advice from a qualified external adviser (legal, financial, valuation, or other relevant expert) who has no material relationship with the Company, the conflicted director, or any Related Party. |



| Early-Stage Context
This structural position is common for founder-led companies in the pre-Series A stage. The Company has implemented robust safeguards including:
•  Full disclosure via Standing Notices (section 192)
•  Independent advice for material transactions
•  Member (shareholder) approvals where required
•  Detailed documentation and rationale for all decisions
•  Commitment to appoint independent director post-Series A |



| Strategy | When Appropriate |

| Recusal | The conflicted director leaves the meeting room (or is excluded from the relevant portion of a virtual meeting) for the duration of the discussion and vote. The minutes record the director’s departure and return. This is the preferred approach where a disinterested quorum can be maintained. |

| Disclosure and participation under s194 | Where the Company is a proprietary company and no disinterested quorum is available (including the current board composition), the conflicted director(s) may participate in discussion and vote, provided the interest has been fully disclosed under s191 or s192. The minutes must record: the disclosure, the basis for relying on s194, the commercial rationale for the decision, and that the Board was satisfied the decision was in the Company’s interests. |

| Independent Advice | For Material Transactions, the Board obtains Independent Advice (legal, financial, or valuation) to confirm that the transaction is on arm’s length terms or is otherwise in the Company’s commercial interests. This strengthens the governance record and supports the arm’s length exception under s210. |

| Member approval | For transactions that constitute a “financial benefit to a related party” under Chapter 2E and do not fall within a recognised exception (arm’s length terms under s210, reasonable remuneration under s211, or other exceptions in ss212–216), the Company must obtain member approval under s208 before giving the benefit. |



| THIS SECTION ACTIVATES UPON APPOINTMENT OF THE FIRST INDEPENDENT DIRECTOR
The Company has committed to appointing an independent director at or within 60 days of the Series A close. Upon that appointment, the procedures in this section take effect and supplement (but do not replace) the procedures in Section 6. |

### 05.  WaterRoads_Recapitalisation_Deed_V7_COMPLETE.docx

*File: `05.  WaterRoads_Recapitalisation_Deed_V7_COMPLETE.docx`*

RECAPITALISATION DEED

Version 7 — Final Aligned

WATER ROADS PTY LTD

ACN 686 900 014

DATE: 15 January 2026

CONFIDENTIAL

Changes from V6.1: CBS Loan date changed to placeholder (was hardcoded “1 August 2025”, needs verification against Loan Variation V7 which flags 1 Aug vs 31 Aug). Schedule 2 and 3 notes updated to reflect CBS Consent V7 and CBS Loan Variation V7 now exist. CBS execution block updated with abstention/independent director note for consistency with CBS Consent V7 and Loan Variation V7. No substantive legal content changed.

Changes from V5 (in V6.1): Board date corrected (14→15 Jan). Share numbers confirmed at 100K pre-split / 1M post-split (matching original V5). CBS deed dates changed to placeholders. Constitution reference updated to V3.1. Conflict disclosure framework added (clause 7). CobaltBlu address to be verified.

PARTIES

WATER ROADS PTY LTD ACN 686 900 014 of Unit 142, 19 Hickson Road, Dawes Point NSW 2000 (Company)

COBALTBLU PTY LTD ACN 103 595 071 of [INSERT COBALTBLU ADDRESS — verify against ASIC extract] (CobaltBlu)

CBS GROUP PTY LTD ACN 164 870 080 of [INSERT CBS ADDRESS — verify against ASIC extract] (CBS)

(CobaltBlu and CBS together, the Shareholders)

RECITALS

A.	The Company was incorporated on 8 May 2025 as an Australian proprietary company limited by shares.

B.	As at the date of this Deed, the Company has on issue:

(i)	1,000 shares described on the ASIC register as “FOU” or “FOUNDER’S” shares, held by CobaltBlu; and

(ii)	100 shares described on the ASIC register as “CLASS B” shares, held by CBS,

(together, the Existing Shares).

C.	The Company’s historic capital structure contains procedural and documentation defects, including:

(i)	mismatch between the ASIC register class codes and the Company’s constitution;

(ii)	sequencing issues in relation to prior share issuances;

(iii)	authority defects in relation to share issuances made under CEO delegation;

(iv)	misalignment between the agreed economic deal between the Shareholders and the recorded ownership percentages; and

(v)	inconsistency between the constitution’s share class framework and the intended capital structure,

(together, the Historic Defects).

D.	The Shareholders have agreed that the intended economic arrangement between them is:

(i)	CobaltBlu: 96% of the Company’s issued share capital; and

(ii)	CBS: 4% of the Company’s issued share capital,

(the Agreed Ownership).

E.	The parties have agreed to implement a recapitalisation of the Company (the Recapitalisation) to:

(i)	cancel all Existing Shares;

(ii)	issue new shares in new share classes to achieve the Agreed Ownership;

(iii)	implement a share split to achieve a practical share count for Series A fundraising and ESOP purposes; and

(iv)	adopt an amended and restated constitution,

thereby creating a clean break in the Company’s chain of title and remedying the Historic Defects.

F.	The Shareholders have each consented to the Recapitalisation and waived any claims arising from the Historic Defects or the implementation of the Recapitalisation.

G.	The directors of the Company (Sarah Margaret Taylor and Jeffrey Alan Dusting) are married to each other, are each directors and 50% shareholders of CobaltBlu, and Jeffrey Alan Dusting is also a director of CBS. Each director has given standing notices of interest under section 192 of the Corporations Act dated 1 January 2026, and has disclosed their interests at the board meeting of 15 January 2026 in reliance on section 194 of the Corporations Act (the Company being a proprietary company). CBS has obtained independent board approval for the Recapitalisation through Jim Ellwood as independent CBS director, with Jeffrey Alan Dusting abstaining from all CBS votes on the matter.

1.	DEFINITIONS AND INTERPRETATION

1.1	Definitions

In this Deed, unless the context otherwise requires:

“ASIC” means the Australian Securities and Investments Commission.

“Board” means the board of directors of the Company from time to time.

“Business Day” means a day that is not a Saturday, Sunday or public holiday in Sydney, New South Wales.

“CBS Consent and Waiver Deed” means the deed between the Company, CobaltBlu, and CBS in the form set out in Schedule 2, to be executed on or before the Completion Date.

“CBS Loan” means the secured loan facility provided by CBS to the Company pursuant to the loan agreement dated [INSERT LOAN DATE — verify: 1 August or 31 August 2025] between the Company and CBS, as varied by the CBS Loan Variation and Waiver Deed.

“CBS Loan Variation and Waiver Deed” means the deed between the Company and CBS in the form set out in Schedule 3, to be executed on or before the Completion Date.

“Common Shares” means ordinary shares in the capital of the Company designated as “Common Shares” having the rights set out in clause 5 of the New Constitution.

“Completion” means completion of the Recapitalisation in accordance with clause 4.

“Completion Date” means the date on which the last of the conditions precedent in clause 2.1 is satisfied or waived, or such other date as the parties agree in writing.

“Corporations Act” means the Corporations Act 2001 (Cth).

“Effective Time” means 11:59 pm (Sydney time) on the Completion Date.

“Existing Shares” has the meaning given in Recital B.

“F Shares” means ordinary shares in the capital of the Company designated as “F Shares” (Founder Shares) having the rights set out in clause 4 of the New Constitution, including the right to auto-convert into Common Shares upon a Qualifying Financing (as defined in the New Constitution).

“Historic Defects” has the meaning given in Recital C.

“New Constitution” means the amended and restated constitution of the Company in the form set out in Schedule 1 (being the Amended and Restated Constitution V3.1 effective 15 January 2026).

“New Shares” means:

(a)	96,000 F Shares to be issued to CobaltBlu; and

(b)	4,000 Common Shares to be issued to CBS,

pursuant to clause 3.2.

“Recapitalisation” has the meaning given in Recital E.

“Share Split” means the subdivision of each issued share in the Company into 10 shares of the same class pursuant to clause 3.3.

“Split Shares” means the shares on issue following the Share Split, being:

(a)	960,000 F Shares held by CobaltBlu; and

(b)	40,000 Common Shares held by CBS.

1.2	Interpretation

In this Deed, unless the context otherwise requires:

(a)	headings are for convenience only and do not affect interpretation;

(b)	the singular includes the plural and vice versa;

(c)	a reference to a party includes that party’s successors and permitted assigns;

(d)	a reference to a statute includes any amendment, consolidation or replacement of that statute;

(e)	a reference to a clause or Schedule is a reference to a clause of, or Schedule to, this Deed;

(f)	where a word or phrase is defined, other grammatical forms of that word or phrase have corresponding meanings;

(g)	a reference to “$” or “dollars” is a reference to Australian dollars; and

(h)	a reference to a document includes any variation or replacement of that document.

2.	CONDITIONS PRECEDENT

2.1	Conditions

Completion is conditional upon:

(a)	the Board having passed resolutions approving the Recapitalisation on 15 January 2026, including:

(i)	the cancellation of the Existing Shares;

(ii)	the creation of the F Shares and Common Shares classes;

(iii)	the issue of the New Shares;

(iv)	the Share Split;

(v)	the adoption of the New Constitution; and

(vi)	the lodgement of all necessary ASIC forms;

(b)	each director of the Company having disclosed any material personal interest in the Recapitalisation in accordance with sections 191 and 192 of the Corporations Act, including:

(i)	standing notices dated 1 January 2026 (tabled at the board meeting of 15 January 2026); and

(ii)	verbal disclosures at the board meetings of 15 January 2026 (WaterRoads) and 16 January 2026 (CBS),

with all directors voting in reliance on section 194 of the Corporations Act (the Company being a proprietary company);

(c)	the Shareholders having passed special resolutions approving:

(i)	the cancellation of the Existing Shares as a selective reduction of capital under section 256C of the Corporations Act;

(ii)	the issue of the New Shares;

(iii)	the Share Split under section 254H of the Corporations Act; and

(iv)	the adoption of the New Constitution under section 136 of the Corporations Act;

(d)	the directors of the Company having made a solvency declaration in accordance with section 256B(1) of the Corporations Act;

(e)	CBS having executed the CBS Consent and Waiver Deed in the form set out in Schedule 2;

(f)	CBS having executed the CBS Loan Variation and Waiver Deed in the form set out in Schedule 3; and

(g)	CobaltBlu having executed a shareholder consent in the form set out in Schedule 4.

2.2	Satisfaction of Conditions

The parties must use reasonable endeavours to satisfy the conditions in clause 2.1 as soon as practicable after the date of this Deed.

2.3	Waiver

A condition in clause 2.1 may only be waived in writing by all parties.

2.4	Long Stop Date

If the conditions in clause 2.1 are not satisfied or waived by 28 February 2026 (or such later date as the parties agree in writing) (Long Stop Date), any party may terminate this Deed by written notice to the other parties, and the parties will have no further obligations under this Deed other than obligations that have accrued before termination.

3.	RECAPITALISATION STEPS

3.1	Cancellation of Existing Shares

At the Effective Time, and subject to the satisfaction or waiver of the conditions in clause 2.1:

(a)	all Existing Shares are cancelled and cease to exist;

(b)	the rights attaching to the Existing Shares are extinguished;

(c)	the share classes to which the Existing Shares belonged (including any class described as “FOU”, “FOUNDER’S”, “Class A”, or “Class B”) are abolished; and

(d)	the Company’s share capital is reduced to zero.

3.2	Issue of New Shares

Immediately following the cancellation in clause 3.1:

(a)	the Company creates two new classes of shares:

(i)	F Shares (Founder Shares); and

(ii)	Common Shares,

each having the rights set out in the New Constitution;

(b)	the Company issues:

(i)	96,000 F Shares to CobaltBlu, credited as fully paid; and

(ii)	4,000 Common Shares to CBS, credited as fully paid;

(c)	the New Shares are issued for nil additional cash consideration, in recognition of the cancellation of the Existing Shares and the Shareholders’ agreement to the Recapitalisation; and

(d)	the Company’s issued share capital immediately following the issue of New Shares is 100,000 shares.

3.3	Share Split

Immediately following the issue of New Shares in clause 3.2:

(a)	each F Share is subdivided into 10 F Shares;

(b)	each Common Share is subdivided into 10 Common Shares;

(c)	the Company’s issued share capital immediately following the Share Split is 1,000,000 shares, comprising:

(i)	960,000 F Shares held by CobaltBlu (96%); and

(ii)	40,000 Common Shares held by CBS (4%); and

(d)	the rights attaching to each class of shares are unaffected by the Share Split.

3.4	Adoption of New Constitution

With effect from Completion:

(a)	the Company’s existing constitution (including the Deed of Amendment to Constitution dated 1 August 2025) is repealed in its entirety; and

(b)	the New Constitution (being the Amended and Restated Constitution V3.1, set out in Schedule 1) is adopted as the constitution of the Company.

3.5	Sequencing

The steps in clauses 3.1, 3.2, 3.3 and 3.4 occur in the order set out in this clause 3, and each step is conditional upon the completion of the preceding step. For the avoidance of doubt:

(a)	the cancellation of Existing Shares occurs first;

(b)	the issue of New Shares occurs immediately after the cancellation;

(c)	the Share Split occurs immediately after the issue of New Shares; and

(d)	the adoption of the New Constitution occurs simultaneously with Completion.

4.	COMPLETION

4.1	Time and Place

Completion takes place at 2:00 pm (Sydney time) on the Completion Date at the registered office of the Company, or at such other time and place as the parties agree in writing. Completion may occur by exchange of executed counterparts in electronic form.

4.2	Completion Actions

At Completion:

(a)	the Company must:

(i)	deliver to each Shareholder a share certificate for their Split Shares;

(ii)	update the Company’s share register to reflect the Split Shares;

(iii)	deliver to each Shareholder a copy of the post-Recapitalisation share register in the form set out in Schedule 5;

(iv)	deliver to each Shareholder a copy of the New Constitution; and

(v)	deliver to each Shareholder a copy of the board and shareholder resolutions passed pursuant to clause 2.1;

(b)	each Shareholder must:

(i)	deliver to the Company their existing share certificates (if any) for cancellation; and

(ii)	execute any documents reasonably required to give effect to the Recapitalisation.

4.3	ASIC Lodgement

Within 28 days after Completion, the Company must lodge with ASIC in sequential order:

(a)	Form 484 (Change to Company Details) — Step 1: notifying the cancellation of the Existing Shares (section C1), the post-cancellation share structure (section C3), and the updated members register (section C4);

(b)	Form 484 (Change to Company Details) — Step 2 (lodged after Step 1 is processed): notifying the issue of the New Shares (section C2), the post-issue share structure (section C3), and the updated members register (section C4);

(c)	Form 2205 (Notification of Share Split) — Step 3A (lodged after Step 2 is processed): notifying the 10-for-1 share split; and

(d)	Form 484 (Change to Company Details) — Step 3B (lodged with or immediately after Step 3A): notifying the post-split share structure (section C3) and the updated members register (section C4).

The Company must not lodge any subsequent step until the preceding step has been confirmed as processed by ASIC.

5.	REPRESENTATIONS AND WARRANTIES

5.1	Company Representations

The Company represents and warrants to each Shareholder that, as at the date of this Deed and at Completion:

(a)	it is a company duly incorporated and validly existing under the laws of Australia;

(b)	it has full power and authority to enter into and perform its obligations under this Deed;

(c)	this Deed constitutes a legal, valid and binding obligation of the Company, enforceable in accordance with its terms;

(d)	the execution and performance of this Deed does not breach any law, regulation, order, or agreement to which the Company is a party or by which it is bound;

(e)	the Existing Shares are the only shares on issue in the Company; and

(f)	there are no options, warrants, convertible securities, or other rights to acquire shares in the Company.

5.2	Shareholder Representations

Each Shareholder represents and warrants to the Company and the other Shareholder that, as at the date of this Deed and at Completion:

(a)	it is a company duly incorporated and validly existing under the laws of Australia;

(b)	it has full power and authority to enter into and perform its obligations under this Deed;

(c)	this Deed constitutes a legal, valid and binding obligation of that Shareholder, enforceable in accordance with its terms;

(d)	the execution and performance of this Deed does not breach any law, regulation, order, or agreement to which that Shareholder is a party or by which it is bound;

(e)	it is the sole legal and beneficial owner of the Existing Shares registered in its name, free from any encumbrance (other than the security interest granted under the CBS Loan);

(f)	it has received independent legal and financial advice in relation to this Deed and the Recapitalisation, or has had the opportunity to do so and has chosen not to; and

(g)	it enters into this Deed voluntarily and with full knowledge of its terms and consequences.

5.3	No Other Securities or Arrangements

Each Shareholder represents and warrants to the Company and the other Shareholder that, as at the date of this Deed and at Completion:

(a)	there are no warrants, options, convertible notes, simple agreements for future equity (SAFEs), or other instruments convertible into or exchangeable for shares in the Company;

(b)	there are no phantom equity, profit participation rights, or synthetic equity arrangements;

(c)	there are no side letters, supplemental agreements, or undisclosed arrangements that modify the economic terms of this Deed or the Agreed Ownership;

(d)	there are no most-favoured-nation (MFN) rights, ratchet provisions, or preferential rights granted to any person in respect of the Company’s securities;

(e)	there are no put options, call options, rights of first refusal, or other arrangements that would require the Company or any Shareholder to issue, transfer, or repurchase securities;

(f)	the Split Shares represent the entire issued share capital of the Company;

(g)	there are no agreements, understandings, or arrangements (written or oral) between any Shareholder and any third party that would alter the economic benefits or voting rights associated with the Split Shares; and

(h)	each Shareholder’s economic interest in the Company is accurately reflected by its percentage holding of Split Shares as set out in Schedule 5.

6.	RELEASES AND WAIVERS

6.1	Release of Historic Claims

Each Shareholder, for itself and its related bodies corporate, officers, employees, and agents:

(a)	releases and discharges the Company and its directors, officers, and employees from any and all claims, demands, actions, suits, or proceedings arising from or in connection with the Historic Defects;

(b)	releases and discharges the other Shareholder and its directors, officers, and employees from any and all claims, demands, actions, suits, or proceedings arising from or in connection with the Historic Defects; and

(c)	agrees not to make any claim against any person in respect of the Historic Defects.

6.2	Waiver of Pre-emptive Rights

Each Shareholder waives any pre-emptive rights, rights of first refusal, or similar rights it may have under the Company’s constitution or any shareholders’ agreement in respect of:

(a)	the cancellation of the Existing Shares;

(b)	the issue of the New Shares; and

(c)	the Share Split.

6.3	Waiver of Oppression Claims

Each Shareholder acknowledges and agrees that:

(a)	the Recapitalisation is fair and reasonable to all Shareholders;

(b)	the Recapitalisation does not constitute oppressive, unfairly prejudicial, or unfairly discriminatory conduct within the meaning of section 232 of the Corporations Act;

(c)	the reduction in CBS’s proportionate shareholding from 9.09% to 4.00% reflects the correction of a historical error to the Agreed Ownership, not a dilutive or prejudicial act; and

(d)	it will not make any application under Part 2F.1 of the Corporations Act in respect of the Recapitalisation.

7.	CONFLICT DISCLOSURE AND GOVERNANCE

7.1	Acknowledgement of Interests

The parties acknowledge that:

(a)	Sarah Margaret Taylor is a director and Company Secretary of the Company, a director and 50% shareholder of CobaltBlu, and the spouse of Jeffrey Alan Dusting;

(b)	Jeffrey Alan Dusting is a director of the Company, a director and 50% shareholder of CobaltBlu, a director of CBS, and the spouse of Sarah Margaret Taylor; and

(c)	each of Sarah Margaret Taylor and Jeffrey Alan Dusting has a material personal interest in the Recapitalisation by reason of their interests described in paragraphs (a) and (b).

7.2	Disclosure and Compliance

The parties record that:

(a)	each director of the Company gave standing notices of interest under section 192 of the Corporations Act dated 1 January 2026, which were tabled at the board meeting of 15 January 2026;

(b)	each director verbally disclosed the nature and extent of their interests at the board meeting of 15 January 2026;

(c)	the directors voted on the Recapitalisation in reliance on section 194 of the Corporations Act (the Company being a proprietary company with only two directors, both of whom are interested);

(d)	Jeffrey Alan Dusting abstained from all votes at the CBS board meeting of 16 January 2026 relating to the Recapitalisation, CBS Consent and Waiver Deed, and CBS Loan Variation and Waiver Deed; and

(e)	Jim Ellwood, as independent CBS director, chaired the CBS board meeting of 16 January 2026 and has been authorised to execute all CBS-side documents in connection with the Recapitalisation.

7.3	Investor Disclosure

The parties agree that the conflict of interest framework described in this clause 7, including the spousal relationship, multi-directorship positions, and the governance measures adopted, will be fully disclosed in the Series A data room and investor materials.

8.	CLEAN BREAK

8.1	Effect of Recapitalisation

The parties acknowledge and agree that:

(a)	the Recapitalisation creates a clean break in the Company’s chain of title;

(b)	all securities currently on issue in the Company are the product of the Recapitalisation and the Share Split, implemented under the New Constitution, with unanimous Shareholder approval;

(c)	from the Effective Time onwards, the Company’s capital structure, share classes, and governance are clean, internally consistent, and aligned with Series A investment norms;

(d)	the Historic Defects relate only to instruments and transactions that have been superseded by this Deed; and

(e)	prospective investors may rely on this Deed as evidence of a clean and enforceable chain of title to the Company’s issued share capital.

8.2	Data Room Narrative

The parties agree that the following statement may be included in any investor data room or due diligence materials:

“The Company’s historic capital structure had procedural and drafting defects (see DD register), but those instruments have been superseded. All currently issued securities are the product of a single Recapitalisation and share split, implemented under a new constitution, with unanimous shareholder approval and properly documented consents and waivers (including CBS). From the Recapitalisation Effective Date onwards, the cap table, share classes and governance are clean, internally consistent, and aligned with Series A norms.”

9.	DIRECTORS’ SOLVENCY DECLARATION

9.1	Declaration

The directors of the Company declare that, in their opinion:

(a)	immediately after the Recapitalisation, there are reasonable grounds to believe that the Company will be able to pay its debts as and when they become due and payable; and

(b)	the Recapitalisation is fair and reasonable to all Shareholders and to prospective Series A investors.

9.2	Basis of Declaration

The declaration in clause 9.1 is made on the basis that:

(a)	the Recapitalisation does not involve any payment to Shareholders;

(b)	the Company’s assets and liabilities are unaffected by the Recapitalisation;

(c)	the Company’s creditors are not prejudiced by the Recapitalisation;

(d)	the directors have made reasonable inquiries into the Company’s financial position;

(e)	the Historic Defects identified in the due diligence risk register have been remediated through this Deed and the associated CBS deeds;

(f)	the Agreed Ownership (96% CobaltBlu / 4% CBS) reflects the original economic deal between the Shareholders;

(g)	CBS has provided informed consent and independent board approval (16 January 2026) to the Recapitalisation; and

(h)	the CBS Loan risk has been addressed through the CBS Loan Variation and Waiver Deed (carving out the Recapitalisation and Series A from restrictive covenants) and the binding commitment to discharge the CBS Loan in full upon receipt of repayment at Series A close.

10.	GENERAL PROVISIONS

10.1	Entire Agreement

This Deed, together with the Schedules, the CBS Consent and Waiver Deed, the CBS Loan Variation and Waiver Deed, and the New Constitution, constitutes the entire agreement between the parties in relation to the Recapitalisation and supersedes all prior agreements, understandings, and negotiations.

10.2	Amendment

This Deed may only be amended by a written document signed by all parties.

10.3	Waiver

A waiver of any right under this Deed is only effective if it is in writing and signed by the party granting the waiver.

10.4	Severability

If any provision of this Deed is invalid or unenforceable, it will be severed from this Deed and the remaining provisions will continue in full force and effect.

10.5	Counterparts

This Deed may be executed in any number of counterparts (including electronic counterparts), each of which is an original and all of which together constitute one instrument.

10.6	Governing Law

This Deed is governed by the laws of New South Wales, Australia.

10.7	Jurisdiction

Each party irrevocably submits to the non-exclusive jurisdiction of the courts of New South Wales and courts of appeal from them.

10.8	Costs

Each party bears its own costs in connection with the negotiation, preparation, and execution of this Deed.

10.9	Further Assurances

Each party must do all things and execute all documents necessary or desirable to give full effect to this Deed.

11.	EXECUTION

EXECUTED as a deed.

SIGNED, SEALED AND DELIVERED by WATER ROADS PTY LTD ACN 686 900 014 in accordance with section 127 of the Corporations Act 2001 (Cth):

### CBS_Board_Paper_Resolutions_16Jan2026.docx

BOARD PAPER AND RESOLUTIONS

Recapitalisation of Water Roads Pty Ltd — CBS Participation

1. Conflict Management Framework

IMPORTANT: Unlike Water Roads and CobaltBlu (which rely on section 194), CBS has an independent director available. Accordingly, section 195 applies and Jeff Dusting must abstain from voting on all matters relating to the Recapitalisation.

2. Declarations of Interest

2.1 Standing Notice Tabled

Jeff Dusting's Standing Notice under section 192 of the Corporations Act was tabled:

2.2 Abstention Recorded

3. Recapitalisation Deed — CBS Participation

3.1 Background

CBS Group holds 4% of Water Roads Pty Ltd. The Recapitalisation will:

(a)  Cancel all existing shares in Water Roads (which may have Historic Defects)

(b)  Issue new shares to achieve the Agreed Ownership: CobaltBlu 96% / CBS 4%

(c)  Require CBS to provide consents and waivers as shareholder and lender

(d)  Create a 'clean break' in chain of title for Series A readiness

3.2 CBS Position

4. CBS Consent and Waiver Deed

4.1 Background

The CBS Loan Agreement dated 31 August 2025 contains covenants that would otherwise be triggered by the Recapitalisation, including:

(a)  Negative pledge (clause 8.1) — prevents granting security to Series A investors

(b)  Change of control provisions (clause 9.2) — could trigger loan acceleration

(c)  Consent requirements — for material corporate changes

The CBS Consent and Waiver Deed V7 provides CBS's consent to the Recapitalisation and waives the blocking rights that would otherwise apply.

4.2 Key Terms

5. CBS Loan Variation and Waiver Deed

5.1 Background

The CBS Loan Variation and Waiver Deed V7 varies the CBS Loan Agreement to:

(a)  Subordinate the CBS Loan to Series A investor rights

(b)  Require mandatory repayment of the loan from Series A proceeds

(c)  Carve out the Recapitalisation and Series A from covenant restrictions

5.2 Key Commercial Terms

6. Commercial Rationale Confirmation

6.1 Background

Given Jeff Dusting's conflict of interest, the Board must be satisfied that the transactions are in the best interests of CBS, independent of any benefit to Jeff personally or to CobaltBlu.

6.2 Jim Ellwood's Assessment

Jim Ellwood, as independent director, has considered the commercial rationale for CBS's participation:

7. Authorisation to Execute Documents

7.1 Documents Requiring Execution

Note: Jeff Dusting signs for s127 validity only (two directors required). Jim Ellwood has voted alone to approve the transactions.

8. Circulating Resolutions — January Resolutions

8.1 Background

Pursuant to section 248A of the Corporations Act, resolutions may be passed without a meeting if all directors entitled to vote sign a document stating they are in favour of the resolution.

The CBS January Resolutions document consolidates all resolutions passed at this meeting for execution as a written resolution.

8.2 Execution

The January Resolutions will be signed by:

(a)  Jim Ellwood — in favour of all resolutions

(b)  Jeff Dusting — noting abstention from all substantive votes; signing for s127 validity only

9. Summary of Resolutions

CERTIFIED as the resolutions passed at the Board Meeting held on 16 January 2026:

Date: 16 January 2026

| MINUTE NOTE: Jeff Dusting Abstention — s195
The Chair (Jim Ellwood) noted for the record that:

(a)  Jeffrey Alan Dusting has given a Standing Notice dated 1 January 2026 disclosing his material personal interests in the Recapitalisation of Water Roads Pty Ltd;

(b)  the nature of Jeff's interests is that he is a director and 50% shareholder of CobaltBlu Pty Ltd (which will hold 96% of Water Roads post-Recapitalisation), a director of Water Roads, and is married to Sarah Margaret Taylor;

(c)  pursuant to section 195 of the Corporations Act 2001, Jeff Dusting will abstain from voting on all resolutions relating to the Recapitalisation;

(d)  Jim Ellwood, as the sole disinterested director, will vote on all substantive resolutions;

(e)  Jeff Dusting remains present for quorum purposes and will sign documents for s127 execution validity.

Jeff Dusting confirmed his understanding and intention to abstain on that basis. |



| Current Holding: | 4% of Water Roads (subject to Historic Defects) |

| Post-Recapitalisation: | 40,000 Common Shares (4% on clean chain of title) |

| Share Class: | Common Shares (no Founder Protective Provisions) |

| CBS Loan Position: | Secured lender; $200,000 facility dated 31 August 2025 |

| Benefit to CBS: | Clean title to shares; mandatory loan repayment at Series A; subordination protection |



| RESOLUTION 1: Approve CBS Entry into Recapitalisation Deed
[Jim Ellwood voting; Jeff Dusting abstaining]
RESOLVED that:

(a)  CBS Group Pty Ltd enter into the Recapitalisation Deed V7 as a party in its capacity as a shareholder and lender of Water Roads Pty Ltd;

(b)  CBS consent to the cancellation of its existing shares in Water Roads and the issue of 4,000 Common Shares (40,000 post-split) in exchange;

(c)  CBS provide the consents, waivers, and acknowledgments required of it under the Recapitalisation Deed;

(d)  the entry into the Recapitalisation Deed is in the best interests of CBS, having regard to the confirmation of CBS's 4% shareholding on a clean chain of title and the mandatory loan repayment at Series A. |



| Element | CBS Consent/Waiver |

| Negative Pledge Waiver | CBS waives negative pledge to permit Series A security arrangements |

| Change of Control Waiver | CBS waives right to accelerate loan on Series A closing |

| Recapitalisation Consent | CBS consents to cancellation/reissue of shares, adoption of Constitution V3.1 |

| Covenant Waiver | CBS waives any breach of financial covenants as at Recapitalisation date |



| RESOLUTION 2: Approve CBS Consent and Waiver Deed
[Jim Ellwood voting; Jeff Dusting abstaining]
RESOLVED that:

(a)  CBS Group Pty Ltd execute the CBS Consent and Waiver Deed V7;

(b)  CBS waive its rights under the negative pledge, change of control, and other restrictive covenants in the CBS Loan Agreement to the extent necessary to permit the Recapitalisation and Series A;

(c)  CBS waive any existing or potential breach of financial covenants as at the Recapitalisation Effective Date;

(d)  the waiver of these rights is in the best interests of CBS, having regard to the commercial rationale set out in section 7 of this paper. |



| Term | Effect |

| Subordination | CBS Loan subordinated to Series A investor rights; CBS ranks behind Series A on enforcement |

| Mandatory Repayment | CBS Loan to be repaid in full from Series A proceeds within 5 business days of closing |

| Interest | Accrued interest to Series A close capitalised and repaid with principal |

| PPSR | CBS to release PPSR registration within 2 business days of repayment |

| Standstill | CBS agrees not to enforce loan until 7 March 2026 (Series A target close + buffer) |



| RESOLUTION 3: Approve CBS Loan Variation and Waiver Deed
[Jim Ellwood voting; Jeff Dusting abstaining]
RESOLVED that:

(a)  CBS Group Pty Ltd execute the CBS Loan Variation and Waiver Deed V7;

(b)  CBS agree to the subordination of the CBS Loan to Series A investor rights;

(c)  CBS agree to mandatory repayment of the CBS Loan from Series A proceeds;

(d)  CBS agree to the standstill period until 7 March 2026;

(e)  the variation of the loan terms is in the best interests of CBS, having regard to:
     (i)   the certainty of repayment from Series A proceeds;
     (ii)  the preservation of CBS's 4% equity position; and
     (iii) the commercial rationale set out in section 7 of this paper. |



| Factor | Benefit to CBS |

| Clean Title | CBS's 4% shareholding confirmed on clean chain of title, eliminating Historic Defect risk |

| Loan Repayment | Mandatory repayment from Series A provides certainty of recovery; superior to relying on WR's operating cash flow |

| Equity Upside | CBS retains 4% equity in a company raising at $380M post-money valuation; potential for significant upside |

| Series A Enablement | CBS consent enables Series A to proceed; without it, WR cannot raise and CBS loan recovery is uncertain |

| Subordination Trade-off | Acceptable given mandatory repayment from Series A; subordination only applies during short window before repayment |



| MINUTE NOTE: Commercial Rationale — Jim Ellwood Confirmation
Jim Ellwood, as independent director, confirmed that:

(a)  he has reviewed the Recapitalisation Deed V7, CBS Consent and Waiver Deed V7, and CBS Loan Variation and Waiver Deed V7;

(b)  he has considered the commercial rationale for CBS's participation, independent of any benefit to Jeff Dusting or CobaltBlu;

(c)  in his assessment, the transactions are in the best interests of CBS because:
     (i)   CBS's 4% shareholding is confirmed on a clean chain of title;
     (ii)  CBS receives mandatory loan repayment from Series A proceeds;
     (iii) CBS retains equity upside in a company valued at $380M post-money;
     (iv)  the alternative (no Recapitalisation) leaves CBS with uncertain title and uncertain loan recovery;

(d)  he is satisfied that the terms are arm's length and commercially reasonable;

(e)  he approves the transactions on behalf of CBS as the sole disinterested director. |
