### CBS Consent Waiver V7 - signed.pdf

*File: `CBS Executed/CBS Consent Waiver V7 - signed.pdf`*

WATER ROADS PTY LTD
                                            ACN 686 900 014
                                         DATE: 15 January 2026

                                             CONFIDENTIAL



                          CBS CONSENT AND WAIVER DEED


                                                PARTIES
CBS GROUP PTY LTD ACN 164 870 080 of Level 22, 180 George Street, Sydney, NSW 2000 (CBS)
WATER ROADS PTY LTD ACN 686 900 014 of Unit 142, 19 Hickson Road, Dawes Point NSW 2000
(Company)
COBALTBLU PTY LTD ACN 103 595 071 ATF the Cobaltblu Unit Trust of 6 Arthur Street,
Sandringham, Victoria, 3191 (CobaltBlu)
(CBS, the Company, and CobaltBlu together, the Parties)

                                               RECITALS
A. The Company was incorporated on 8 May 2025 and has implemented a recapitalisation pursuant to a
Recapitalisation Deed dated 15 January 2026 (the Recapitalisation Deed).
B. Pursuant to the Recapitalisation (including the 10-for-1 share split), CBS holds 40,000 Common
Shares in the Company, representing 4% of the issued share capital.
C. CBS acknowledges that it acquired its shareholding in the Company in its capacity as a strategic
advisor and early supporter of the Company’s business, and not as a financial investor seeking preferred
share rights or investor protections.
D. The Company intends to pursue institutional equity financing (Series A), and CBS acknowledges that:
         (i) its Common Shares rank pari passu with F Shares held by CobaltBlu;
         (ii) CBS does not hold, and has never held, any preferred rights, veto rights, board appointment
         rights, anti-dilution rights, or other special protections beyond those available to ordinary
         shareholders; and
         (iii) CBS’s economic interest is accurately reflected by its 4% shareholding on a fully diluted
         basis.
E. CBS was a director of the Company at the time certain historic corporate actions were taken, and CBS
wishes to confirm that:
         (i) all such actions were taken with CBS’s knowledge and consent (or ratified retrospectively);
         (ii) CBS does not claim any breach of director duties or oppressive conduct; and
         (iii) CBS releases all parties from any claims arising from historic governance matters.
F. CBS is a party to a loan agreement with the Company dated [INSERT LOAN DATE], as varied by the
CBS Loan Variation and Waiver Deed (the CBS Loan Deed), which together address all matters relating
to the loan facility.
G. The Parties have agreed to document CBS’s consents, waivers, and acknowledgments in this Deed to
provide certainty for the Company’s Series A fundraising process.
H. Jeffrey Alan Dusting is a director of both the Company and CBS, a director and 50% shareholder of
CobaltBlu, and the spouse of Sarah Margaret Taylor (director and Company Secretary of the Company,
and director and 50% shareholder of CobaltBlu). Jim Ellwood is a director of CBS and an observer (not a
director) of the Company. The parties have managed these conflicts through:
         (i) the comprehensive conflict of interest framework documented in the WaterRoads Conflict of
         Interest Policy (Version 6.0 – Institutional) and CBS Group Conflict of Interest Board Policy
         (Version 6.0 – Institutional);
         (ii) standing notices of interest given by Sarah Margaret Taylor and Jeffrey Alan Dusting under
         section 192 of the Corporations Act, which were tabled at the Company board meeting of 15
         January 2026 and are recorded in the Company’s Related Party Transaction Register
         maintained under Constitution clause 18.6;
         (iii) verbal disclosures at the board meetings of 15 January 2026 (WaterRoads) and 16 January
         2026 (CBS), recorded in minutes;
         (iv) Jeffrey Alan Dusting’s abstention from all CBS votes relating to the Recapitalisation, this
         Deed, and related transactions; and
         (v) Jim Ellwood (as independent CBS director) chairing the CBS board meeting of 16 January
         2026 and being authorised to execute all CBS-side documents.

                                    OPERATIVE PROVISIONS

1. DEFINITIONS AND INTERPRETATION
1.1 Definitions
In this Deed, unless the context otherwise requires:
   “ASIC” means the Australian Securities and Investments Commission.
   “Board” means the board of directors of the Company from time to time.
   “Business Day” means a day that is not a Saturday, Sunday or public holiday in Sydney, New South
   Wales.
   “CBS Loan Deed” means the CBS Loan Variation and Waiver Deed between CBS and the Company.
   “Common Shares” means ordinary shares in the capital of the Company designated as “Common
   Shares” as defined in clause 5 of the Constitution.
   “Completion Date” means 15 January 2026, being the effective date of the Recapitalisation.
   “Constitution” means the Company’s Amended and Restated Constitution V3.1 adopted by special
   resolution on [date] 2026, effective from 15 January 2026.
   “Corporations Act” means the Corporations Act 2001 (Cth).
   “F Share Majority” has the meaning given in clause 3.1 of the Constitution (being the holders of more
   than 50% of the F Shares on issue, calculated on an as-converted basis, voting as a separate class).
   “F Shares” means ordinary shares in the capital of the Company designated as “F Shares” (Founder
   Shares) as defined in clause 4 of the Constitution, including the right to auto-convert into Common
   Shares upon a Qualifying Financing (clause 4.4 of the Constitution).
   “Founder Protective Provisions” means the matters listed in clause 20.2 of the Constitution requiring F
   Share Majority written consent while Founders hold at least 30% of issued Shares on a Fully Diluted
   Basis.
   “Fully Diluted Basis” has the meaning given in clause 3.1 of the Constitution (being the total number of
   Shares that would be on issue if all options, warrants, convertible securities, and other rights to
   acquire Shares were exercised or converted in full).
   “Historic Defects” has the meaning given in the Recapitalisation Deed.
   “Independent Director” has the meaning given in clause 3.1 of the Constitution (being a Director who is
   not a Founder or associate, not an employee/officer, not a related party director/officer/employee, and
   not a spouse/family member of any such person).
   “Investor Majority” has the meaning given in clause 3.1 of the Constitution (being, while any single
   holder of Series A Preferred Shares holds 40% or more, that holder; otherwise, holders of more than
   50% of Series A Preferred Shares on issue, voting as a separate class).
   “Investor Reserved Matters” means the matters listed in clause 21.2 of the Constitution requiring
   Investor Majority written consent while Series A Preferred Shareholders hold at least 20% of issued
   Shares on a Fully Diluted Basis.
   “Preferred Shares” or “Series A Preferred Shares” means any class of shares designated as Series A
   Preferred Shares and issued by the Company in connection with a Qualifying Financing, having such
   rights as determined by the Board and F Share Majority and set out in the SHA or any amendment to
   the Constitution (as contemplated by clause 6.1 of the Constitution).
   “Qualifying Financing” means the completion of one or more equity capital raisings by the Company in
   a single round or series of related closings, with aggregate gross cash proceeds to the Company of
   not less than A$5,000,000, on terms approved by the Board and the F Share Majority (as defined in
   clause 3.1 of the Constitution).
   “Recapitalisation” means the recapitalisation implemented pursuant to the Recapitalisation Deed.
   “Recapitalisation Deed” means the Recapitalisation Deed dated 15 January 2026 between the
   Company, CBS, and CobaltBlu.
   “Related Party Transaction” has the meaning given in clause 3.1 of the Constitution (being a
   transaction or arrangement in which a Director, a Founder, or an associate has a material personal
   interest).
   “Series A Investors” means investors who subscribe for Series A Preferred Shares in a Qualifying
   Financing.
   “SHA” or “Shareholders Agreement” means any shareholders’ agreement entered into by the
   Company and its Members (or any of them) from time to time, as amended or restated (as defined in
   clause 3.1 of the Constitution).
1.2 Interpretation
In this Deed, unless the context otherwise requires:
      (a) headings are for convenience only and do not affect interpretation;
      (b) the singular includes the plural and vice versa;
      (c) a reference to a party includes that party’s successors and permitted assigns;
      (d) a reference to a statute includes any amendment, consolidation or replacement of that statute;
      (e) a reference to a clause is a reference to a clause of this Deed;
      (f) where a word or phrase is defined, other grammatical forms of that word or phrase have
      corresponding meanings;
      (g) a reference to “$” or “dollars” is a reference to Australian dollars; and
      (h) a reference to a document includes any variation or replacement of that document.

2. CONSENT TO RECAPITALISATION
2.1 Informed Consent
CBS confirms that:
      (a) it has received and reviewed the Recapitalisation Deed, the Constitution (V3.1), and all related
      documentation;
      (b) it has received independent legal and financial advice in relation to the Recapitalisation, or has
      had the opportunity to do so and has chosen not to;
      (c) it understands the effect of the Recapitalisation on its shareholding, including:
             (i) the cancellation of its previous 100 Class B shares;
             (ii) the issue of 4,000 Common Shares (being 40,000 Common Shares after the 10-for-1
             share split) representing 4% of the issued share capital; and
             (iii) the pari passu ranking of Common Shares with F Shares (clauses 4 and 5 of the
             Constitution);
      (d) it consents to the Recapitalisation and agrees that it is fair and reasonable; and
      (e) it enters into this Deed voluntarily and with full knowledge of its terms and consequences.
2.2 Board Approval
CBS confirms that:
      (a) its board of directors met on 16 January 2026 and approved CBS’s participation in the
      Recapitalisation;
      (b) independent board approval was obtained, with Jim Ellwood chairing the CBS board meeting
      and Jeffrey Alan Dusting abstaining from all votes due to his interests in the Company and
      CobaltBlu; and
      (c) CBS’s board considered the interests of CBS separately from the interests of the Company or
      CobaltBlu.
2.3 No Duress or Undue Influence
CBS confirms that:
      (a) it was not subject to any duress, undue influence, or improper pressure in agreeing to the
      Recapitalisation;
      (b) it had adequate time to consider the terms of the Recapitalisation and seek advice; and
      (c) the terms of the Recapitalisation reflect the agreed economic arrangement between CBS and
      CobaltBlu.

3. ACKNOWLEDGMENT OF SHAREHOLDING TERMS
3.1 Economic Interest
CBS acknowledges and agrees that:
      (a) its economic interest in the Company is accurately reflected by its 4% shareholding in Common
      Shares;
      (b) the 4% shareholding was agreed between CBS and CobaltBlu as fair consideration for CBS’s
      early strategic advice, business development support, provision of the loan facility, and ongoing
      support;
      (c) CBS does not have any undisclosed economic rights, profit participation arrangements, or side
      agreements that would increase its economic interest beyond 4%; and
      (d) CBS has no claim for additional shares, value adjustments, or true-up payments.
3.2 Ordinary Share Status
CBS acknowledges and agrees that:
      (a) its Common Shares are ordinary shares that rank pari passu with F Shares in all respects,
      including:
            (i) voting rights (one vote per share) (clauses 4.1 and 5.1 of the Constitution);
            (ii) dividend rights (equal participation) (clauses 4.2 and 5.2 of the Constitution);
            (iii) return of capital rights (equal participation, subject to prior rights of Series A Preferred
            Shares if issued) (clauses 4.3 and 5.3 of the Constitution); and
            (iv) participation in surplus assets on winding up;
      (b) CBS does not hold, and has never held, any preferred share rights, including:
            (i) liquidation preferences;
            (ii) dividend preferences;
            (iii) conversion rights (other than as provided in the Constitution);
            (iv) redemption rights;
            (v) anti-dilution protection;
            (vi) pre-emptive rights beyond those in clause 8 of the Constitution; or
            (vii) any other preferential economic rights;
      (c) CBS does not hold, and has never held, any special governance rights, including:
             (i) veto rights over company decisions;
             (ii) board appointment or observer rights;
             (iii) information rights beyond those available to ordinary shareholders under the
             Corporations Act;
             (iv) drag-along or tag-along rights beyond those in clauses 11 and 12 of the Constitution; or
             (v) any other special protective provisions;
      (d) the only rights CBS has as a shareholder are those expressly set out in the Constitution, the
      Corporations Act, and general law applicable to all shareholders; and
      (e) CBS acquired its shareholding as a strategic supporter and advisor, not as a financial investor,
      and did not negotiate or expect to receive investor protections typical of venture capital or private
      equity investments.
3.3 No Implied Rights
CBS acknowledges and agrees that:
      (a) the fact that CBS is a related party of the Company (by virtue of director overlap) does not give
      CBS any special rights beyond those of an ordinary shareholder;
      (b) the fact that CBS provided a loan to the Company does not give CBS any equity rights beyond
      its 4% Common Share holding;
      (c) the fact that CBS participated in the Company’s early development does not give CBS any
      “founder-equivalent” rights beyond its Common Shares; and
      (d) there are no implied or unwritten understandings that would give CBS rights beyond those
      expressly documented in this Deed, the Constitution, and the CBS Loan Deed.

4. WAIVER OF CLAIMS ARISING FROM RECAPITALISATION
4.1 Release of Historic Claims
CBS, for itself and its related bodies corporate, officers, employees, and agents, irrevocably and
unconditionally:
      (a) releases and discharges the Company and its directors, officers, and employees from any and
      all claims, demands, actions, suits, or proceedings arising from or in connection with:
             (i) the Historic Defects identified in the Recapitalisation Deed;
             (ii) any procedural or documentation irregularities in the Company’s historic capital structure;
             (iii) any share issuances, capital reductions, or corporate actions prior to the Completion
             Date;
             (iv) any valuation methodologies or allocation of equity between shareholders;
             (v) any decisions made by the Board (including decisions in which CBS’s nominee
             participated); or
             (vi) the implementation of the Recapitalisation;
      (b) releases and discharges CobaltBlu and its directors, officers, and employees from any and all
      such claims; and
      (c) agrees not to make any claim against any person in respect of the matters set out in clause
      4.1(a).
4.2 Waiver of Oppression Claims
CBS acknowledges and agrees that:
      (a) the Recapitalisation is fair and reasonable to CBS;
      (b) the Recapitalisation does not constitute oppressive, unfairly prejudicial, or unfairly
      discriminatory conduct within the meaning of section 232 of the Corporations Act;
      (c) the reduction in CBS’s proportionate shareholding from 9.09% to 4.00% reflects the correction
      of a historical error to the Agreed Ownership (as defined in the Recapitalisation Deed), not a
      dilutive or prejudicial act;
      (d) CBS will not make any application under Part 2F.1 of the Corporations Act in respect of the
      Recapitalisation, the allocation of equity, any historic corporate actions, or any future actions
      contemplated by the Recapitalisation Deed or this Deed; and
      (e) CBS waives any rights it may have had to challenge the Recapitalisation or seek alternative
      relief.
4.3 Waiver of Director Duties Claims
CBS acknowledges and agrees that:
      (a) Jeffrey Alan Dusting was a director of both the Company and CBS throughout the relevant
      period, and Jim Ellwood served as an observer at Company board meetings;
      (b) during that period, certain corporate actions were taken by the Company, including share
      issuances, capital structure decisions, and governance matters;
      (c) CBS participated in, consented to, or ratified all such actions (or had the opportunity to do so
      and chose not to object);
      (d) CBS does not claim any breach of director duties by any director of the Company in respect of
      any corporate action taken prior to the Completion Date;
      (e) CBS releases all directors (past and present) from any claims arising from their conduct as
      directors; and
      (f) CBS acknowledges that all directors acted in good faith and in the best interests of the
      Company.
4.4 Waiver of Pre-emptive and Similar Rights
CBS waives any pre-emptive rights, rights of first refusal, tag-along rights, drag-along rights, or similar
rights it may have (whether under the Constitution, common law, or otherwise) in respect of:
      (a) the Recapitalisation, including the cancellation and reissue of shares;
      (b) any future issue of Series A Preferred Shares in a Qualifying Financing (subject to the carve-out
      in clause 8.4 of the Constitution);
      (c) any future issue of shares under the Company’s employee share option plan (ESOP) within the
      approved 10% pool (clause 26 of the Constitution, with carve-out in clause 8.3); and
      (d) any future transfer of shares by CobaltBlu to third parties,
except to the extent such rights are expressly preserved in the Constitution for all ordinary shareholders.
5. DIRECTOR CONFLICTS AND RATIFICATION
5.1 Acknowledgment of Conflicts
CBS acknowledges that:
      (a) Jeffrey Alan Dusting is a director of the Company, a director of CBS, and a director and 50%
      shareholder of CobaltBlu;
      (b) Sarah Margaret Taylor is a director and Company Secretary of the Company, and a director
      and 50% shareholder of CobaltBlu;
      (c) Jeffrey Alan Dusting and Sarah Margaret Taylor are married to each other;
      (d) Jim Ellwood is a director of CBS and has been invited to attend Company board meetings as an
      observer (he is not a director of the Company);
      (e) these relationships create actual and potential conflicts of interest in relation to decisions
      affecting the relative rights of CBS and CobaltBlu, the Recapitalisation and allocation of equity, and
      the terms of the CBS loan facility; and
      (f) the Company has managed these conflicts through the comprehensive governance framework
      described in clause 5.2.
5.2 Disclosure and Governance Framework
CBS records and confirms that:
      (a) Sarah Margaret Taylor and Jeffrey Alan Dusting each gave standing notices of interest under
      section 192 of the Corporations Act, which were tabled at the Company board meeting of 15
      January 2026 and recorded in the Company’s Related Party Transaction Register maintained
      under Constitution clause 18.6;
      (b) the Company has adopted and implemented the WaterRoads Conflict of Interest Policy
      (Version 6.0 – Institutional), which provides a comprehensive framework for identifying, disclosing,
      and managing conflicts of interest;
      (c) CBS has adopted and implemented the CBS Group Conflict of Interest Board Policy (Version
      6.0 – Institutional), which mirrors the WaterRoads policy and ensures consistent conflict
      management across both entities;
      (d) each Company director verbally disclosed the nature and extent of their interests at the board
      meeting of 15 January 2026, in accordance with sections 191–192 of the Corporations Act and
      clause 18.1 of the Constitution;
      (e) the Company directors voted on the Recapitalisation in reliance on section 194 of the
      Corporations Act (the Company being a proprietary company), with the reliance documented in
      board minutes in accordance with clause 18.4 of the Constitution;
      (f) Jeffrey Alan Dusting abstained from all votes at the CBS board meeting of 16 January 2026
      relating to the Recapitalisation, this Deed, and the CBS Loan Deed;
      (g) Jim Ellwood, as independent CBS director, chaired the CBS board meeting of 16 January 2026
      and has been authorised to execute all CBS-side documents in connection with the
      Recapitalisation;
      (h) the Recapitalisation has been recorded in the Company’s Related Party Transaction Register
      maintained under Constitution clause 18.6, including the date, parties, terms, disclosures made,
      and basis of approval; and
      (i) the full conflict of interest framework (including the Version 6.0 policies, Standing Notices,
      Related Party Transaction Register, and relevant board minutes) will be disclosed to prospective
      Series A Investors in the data room.
5.3 Ratification of Prior Actions
CBS ratifies and confirms all actions taken by the Board prior to the Completion Date, including:
      (a) decisions in which Jeffrey Alan Dusting participated or voted as both a Company director and
      CBS director;
      (b) decisions affecting CBS’s rights as a shareholder or creditor;
      (c) share issuances and capital structure decisions; and
      (d) approval of Related Party Transactions involving CBS,
and agrees that such actions were valid and binding notwithstanding any actual or potential conflicts of
interest.

6. NO RESIDUAL SPECIAL RIGHTS; CONSENT TO SERIES A
6.1 Acknowledgment of No Special Rights
CBS acknowledges and confirms that, following completion of the Recapitalisation:
      (a) CBS holds only Common Shares, which are ordinary shares ranking pari passu with F Shares
      (clauses 4 and 5 of the Constitution);
      (b) CBS does not have, and does not claim to have:
             (i) veto rights (other than those available to all shareholders under the Corporations Act);
             (ii) board appointment or observer rights (other than Jim Ellwood’s observer invitation, which
             is at the Company’s discretion and may be revoked at any time);
             (iii) information rights beyond those available to ordinary shareholders under the
             Corporations Act and clause 25 of the Constitution;
             (iv) anti-dilution protection;
             (v) liquidation preferences;
             (vi) drag-along, tag-along, or co-sale rights beyond those in clauses 11 and 12 of the
             Constitution (which apply equally to all shareholders);
             (vii) MFN rights or ratchet provisions;
             (viii) rights to participate in future financings on preferential terms; or
             (ix) any other special protective provisions;
      (c) there are no side letters, supplemental agreements, oral understandings, or undisclosed
      arrangements between CBS and any other party that would give CBS rights beyond those
      expressly set out in the Constitution and the CBS Loan Deed;
      (d) CBS’s only relationship with the Company is as:
            (i) a 4% ordinary shareholder (through its Common Shares);
            (ii) a secured creditor (under the CBS Loan Deed); and
            (iii) a related party (by virtue of director overlap, managed through the conflict framework);
            and
      (e) CBS’s economic interest in the Company is fully and accurately reflected by its 4%
      shareholding on a Fully Diluted Basis, with no additional undisclosed economic arrangements.
6.2 Consent to Series A and Investor Protections
CBS acknowledges and consents to the Company’s pursuit of institutional equity financing (Series A),
and specifically agrees that:
      (a) Series A Preferred Shares and Senior Rights: The Company may create and issue Series A
      Preferred Shares to Series A Investors with rights that are senior to CBS’s Common Shares,
      including:
            (i) liquidation preferences (priority in distribution of proceeds on exit);
            (ii) dividend preferences;
            (iii) redemption rights;
            (iv) conversion rights and anti-dilution protection;
            (v) class voting rights (including the right to approve certain matters as a separate class);
            and
            (vi) any other preferential economic or governance rights negotiated with Series A Investors
            and determined by the Board and F Share Majority in accordance with clause 6.1 of the
            Constitution;
      (b) Investor Governance Rights: Series A Investors may receive governance and protective rights
      that CBS does not have, including:
            (i) board appointment rights (Investor Majority may nominate one Investor Director per
            clause 16.3 of the Constitution);
            (ii) board observer rights;
            (iii) veto rights over specified corporate actions through Investor Reserved Matters (clause
            21.2 of the Constitution);
            (iv) enhanced information and inspection rights (clause 25.3 of the Constitution and SHA);
            (v) rights to approve budgets and strategic decisions;
            (vi) drag-along rights under clauses 11.1(b) and 11.2 of the Constitution (requiring Investor
            Majority approval for drag-along sales);
            (vii) tag-along rights under clause 12 of the Constitution; and
            (viii) any other governance rights typical of institutional venture capital investments;
      (c) Dilution of CBS’s Interest: The issue of Series A Preferred Shares will dilute CBS’s percentage
      ownership, and CBS:
            (i) consents to such dilution;
      (ii) waives any pre-emptive rights in respect of Series A Preferred Share issuances
      (recognising the carve-out in clause 8.4 of the Constitution for Qualifying Financing approved
      by F Share Majority);
      (iii) acknowledges it will not receive anti-dilution protection; and
      (iv) agrees that such dilution is fair and reasonable;
(d) Shareholders Agreement: Series A Investors may require the Company to enter into a
Shareholders Agreement (SHA) that:
      (i) modifies or overrides certain provisions of the Constitution (as contemplated by clause
      22.2 of the Constitution, which provides that as between SHA parties, the SHA prevails);
      (ii) imposes obligations on CBS as a shareholder;
      (iii) grants Series A Investors superior rights to CBS; and
      (iv) CBS agrees to become a party to such SHA if required by Series A Investors or the
      Company;
(e) Conversion of F Shares: Upon completion of a Qualifying Financing, F Shares held by
CobaltBlu will automatically convert into Common Shares (clause 4.4 of the Constitution), and
CBS:
      (i) consents to such conversion;
      (ii) acknowledges that CobaltBlu’s converted Common Shares will have the same class
      rights as CBS’s Common Shares (both ranking behind Series A Preferred Shares); and
      (iii) acknowledges that the Founder Protective Provisions in clause 20 of the Constitution will
      continue to apply while Founders hold at least 30% of issued Shares on a Fully Diluted
      Basis, notwithstanding conversion;
(f) Independent Director Appointment: CBS consents to the appointment of at least one
Independent Director within 60 days of Series A completion, as required by clause 16.1(b) of the
Constitution;
(g) Investor Reserved Matters: CBS acknowledges and consents to the Investor Reserved Matters
in clause 21.2 of the Constitution, which require Investor Majority written consent for specified
actions (including material transactions, capital structure changes, and budget approvals), and
agrees that where an action requires both F Share Majority consent (clause 20) and Investor
Majority consent (clause 21), both consents must be obtained (clause 21.3);
(h) No Right to Equivalent Treatment: CBS acknowledges that:
      (i) it is not entitled to receive the same rights as Series A Investors;
      (ii) it is not entitled to MFN (most favoured nation) treatment;
      (iii) it will not claim that any preferential treatment of Series A Investors constitutes
      oppressive conduct under section 232 of the Corporations Act; and
      (iv) the differential treatment reflects the different commercial positions of strategic
      supporters (CBS) versus institutional financial investors (Series A);
(i) No Blocking Rights: CBS confirms that it does not have any right to:
      (i) veto, block, or delay the issue of Series A Preferred Shares;
            (ii) veto, block, or delay the negotiation or execution of an SHA;
            (iii) veto, block, or delay any Constitution amendments required for the Series A (subject to
            section 136 voting requirements); or
            (iv) veto, block, or delay any other corporate action required to complete the Series A; and
      (j) Facilitation Obligations: CBS agrees to:
            (i) execute any documents reasonably required by Series A Investors or the Company
            (including SHA deeds of adherence, amended Constitution approvals, and consents);
            (ii) provide information requested by Series A Investors as part of due diligence;
            (iii) cooperate fully with Series A due diligence inquiries;
            (iv) attend shareholder meetings and vote in favour of resolutions required to complete the
            Series A (except to the extent doing so would breach CBS’s duties under the Corporations
            Act); and
            (v) not take any action that would impede, delay, or frustrate the Series A financing.
6.3 Acknowledgment for Benefit of Series A Investors
CBS acknowledges that the consents and agreements in clause 6.2 are made for the benefit of:
      (a) the Company;
      (b) CobaltBlu; and
      (c) prospective Series A Investors, who may rely on this Deed in their due diligence and investment
      decision-making.
This Deed may be disclosed to prospective Series A Investors as part of the Company’s data room, and
Series A Investors are entitled to rely on the statements, acknowledgments, undertakings, and
indemnities given by CBS in this Deed.

7. SEPARATION OF LOAN AND EQUITY ARRANGEMENTS
7.1 Acknowledgment of Separate Arrangements
CBS acknowledges and agrees that:
      (a) its status as a secured creditor under the CBS loan facility is entirely separate from its status as
      a 4% shareholder;
      (b) all matters relating to the loan facility (including interest, repayment, security, subordination, and
      discharge) are addressed comprehensively in the CBS Loan Deed;
      (c) the loan facility does not give CBS any additional equity rights, governance rights, or
      preferential treatment as a shareholder;
      (d) CBS’s security interest under the loan facility:
            (i) is unperfected (not registered on the Personal Property Securities Register);
            (ii) ranks behind any security interests granted to institutional lenders or Series A Investors
            (as provided in the CBS Loan Deed); and
            (iii) will be fully released and discharged upon repayment at Series A completion (as required
            by the CBS Loan Deed);
      (e) upon discharge of the loan facility at Series A completion, CBS’s only remaining relationship
      with the Company will be as a 4% ordinary shareholder and a related party (by virtue of director
      overlap); and
      (f) CBS’s shareholding and the loan facility are distinct commercial arrangements, and no rights
      under one arrangement carry over to or enhance the other.
7.2 No Equity Conversion Rights
CBS confirms that:
      (a) the loan facility does not contain, and has never contained, any right for CBS to convert the loan
      principal or accrued interest into equity;
      (b) CBS has no right to acquire additional shares at a discounted valuation by reason of the loan
      facility;
      (c) the loan facility is a debt obligation only, with no equity features, equity-linked rights, or
      warrants; and
      (d) any suggestion that the loan facility includes equity conversion rights is incorrect and is hereby
      expressly disclaimed by CBS.

8. UNDERTAKINGS FOR BENEFIT OF SERIES A INVESTORS
8.1 Cooperation with Due Diligence
CBS undertakes to cooperate fully with due diligence inquiries from prospective Series A Investors,
including:
      (a) responding promptly and accurately to written and oral questions;
      (b) providing access to relevant CBS records and documents (subject to confidentiality obligations
      owed to third parties);
      (c) providing written certifications as reasonably requested by Series A Investors or their advisors;
      (d) making Jim Ellwood and other CBS representatives available for meetings and calls; and
      (e) not making any statements to Series A Investors that are inconsistent with this Deed or the CBS
      Loan Deed.
8.2 Execution of Series A Documentation
CBS undertakes to execute, within 5 Business Days of written request by the Company:
      (a) any accession deed or deed of adherence to the SHA;
      (b) any deed of priority, subordination deed, or intercreditor agreement relating to the CBS loan
      facility and Series A investor security;
      (c) any written consents required for Series A completion (including consents to Constitution
      amendments or SHA terms);
      (d) any shareholder resolutions or written approvals required under the Constitution or
      Corporations Act; and
      (e) any other documents reasonably required by Series A Investors or their advisors,
provided that such documents are consistent with this Deed and the CBS Loan Deed and do not
materially adversely affect CBS’s rights as a 4% ordinary shareholder or secured creditor (acknowledging
that subordination to Series A investors and repayment at Series A close are already agreed and do not
constitute adverse effects).
8.3 No Inconsistent Claims
CBS undertakes that it will not, at any time:
      (a) make claims to Series A Investors, the Company, or CobaltBlu of special rights, preferential
      treatment, or undisclosed arrangements beyond those expressly documented in this Deed, the
      Constitution, and the CBS Loan Deed;
      (b) assert veto or blocking rights over the Series A or any corporate action required to complete the
      Series A;
      (c) claim entitlement to preferential treatment equivalent to Series A Investors;
      (d) seek to renegotiate the terms of this Deed, the CBS Loan Deed, or CBS’s shareholding as a
      condition of providing consent to the Series A;
      (e) take any action (including threatening litigation, making ASIC complaints, or asserting director
      duties breaches) that would reasonably be expected to impede, delay, or frustrate the Series A; or
      (f) make disparaging public statements about the Company, CobaltBlu, the Founders, or the Series
      A process.

9. REPRESENTATIONS AND WARRANTIES
9.1 CBS Representations
CBS represents and warrants to the Company, CobaltBlu, and Series A Investors that, as at the date of
this Deed:
      (a) CBS is a company duly incorporated and validly existing under the laws of Australia;
      (b) CBS has full power and authority to enter into and perform its obligations under this Deed;
      (c) this Deed has been duly authorised, executed, and delivered by CBS and constitutes a legal,
      valid, and binding obligation of CBS, enforceable in accordance with its terms;
      (d) the execution and performance of this Deed does not and will not:
             (i) breach any law, regulation, or court order applicable to CBS;
             (ii) breach CBS’s constitution or any resolution of CBS’s directors or shareholders;
             (iii) breach or constitute a default under any agreement, deed, or instrument to which CBS is
             a party or by which CBS is bound; or
             (iv) require any consent, approval, or authorisation that has not been obtained;
      (e) there are no agreements, understandings, or arrangements (written or oral) between CBS and
      any person that:
             (i) are inconsistent with this Deed;
             (ii) would give CBS additional rights beyond those expressly set out in this Deed, the
             Constitution, and the CBS Loan Deed; or
             (iii) would modify CBS’s economic interest in the Company;
      (f) CBS has received independent legal and financial advice regarding this Deed and the
      Recapitalisation, or has had a reasonable opportunity to do so and has chosen not to;
      (g) CBS enters into this Deed voluntarily, without duress, undue influence, or unconscionable
      conduct, and with full knowledge of its rights and obligations;
      (h) CBS is the sole legal and beneficial owner of 40,000 Common Shares in the Company,
      representing 4% of the issued share capital on a Fully Diluted Basis, and such shares are free from
      any mortgage, charge, lien, pledge, or other encumbrance;
      (i) there is no litigation, arbitration, administrative proceeding, or governmental investigation
      pending or threatened against CBS that would materially affect CBS’s ability to perform its
      obligations under this Deed; and
      (j) all statements, acknowledgments, confirmations, and disclosures made by CBS in this Deed are
      true, accurate, complete, and not misleading, and CBS has not omitted any material fact that would
      make such statements misleading.
9.2 Survival of Representations
The representations and warranties in clause 9.1:
      (a) survive the execution and delivery of this Deed;
      (b) continue in full force and effect for the benefit of the Company, CobaltBlu, and Series A
      Investors; and
      (c) are made as at the date of this Deed and deemed to be repeated:
             (i) on the date of completion of the Series A; and
             (ii) on the date CBS executes any SHA or deed of adherence.

10. INDEMNITY
10.1 CBS Indemnity
CBS indemnifies and holds harmless the Company, CobaltBlu, and any Series A Investors (and their
respective directors, officers, employees, agents, and advisors) against any loss, damage, liability, cost,
or expense (including reasonable legal fees on a solicitor-client basis) arising from or in connection with:
      (a) any breach by CBS of its obligations, undertakings, or covenants under this Deed;
      (b) any misrepresentation or breach of warranty by CBS under this Deed (whether innocent,
      negligent, or fraudulent);
      (c) any claim by CBS that is inconsistent with this Deed, including:
             (i) claims of special rights, preferential treatment, or undisclosed arrangements;
             (ii) claims that the Recapitalisation was unfair, prejudicial, or oppressive;
             (iii) claims that the Series A unfairly prejudices CBS or breaches CBS’s rights; or
             (iv) claims of breach of director duties in connection with the Recapitalisation or Series A; or
      (d) any action by CBS that impedes, delays, or frustrates the Series A financing, including:
             (i) refusing or delaying execution of required documents;
             (ii) threatening or commencing litigation or regulatory complaints;
              (iii) making inconsistent or misleading statements to Series A Investors; or
              (iv) any other conduct contrary to clause 8.3.
10.2 Limitation
The indemnity in clause 10.1 does not apply to the extent that the loss arises directly from:
      (a) fraud, wilful misconduct, or gross negligence by the Company, CobaltBlu, the Founders, or
      Series A Investors; or
      (b) breach of the Constitution, the Corporations Act, or this Deed by the Company or CobaltBlu.

11. GENERAL PROVISIONS
11.1 Entire Agreement
This Deed, together with:
      (a) the Recapitalisation Deed dated 15 January 2026;
      (b) the CBS Loan Deed;
      (c) the Constitution (V3.1); and
      (d) any SHA executed following Series A completion,
constitutes the entire agreement between the Parties in relation to its subject matter and supersedes all
prior agreements, understandings, representations, and negotiations (whether written or oral).
11.2 Amendment
This Deed may only be amended by a written document signed by all Parties.
Following completion of the Series A, clauses 6.2, 8, 9, and 10 (relating to Series A investor protections)
may not be amended without the prior written consent of the Investor Majority (or such other approval
mechanism as may be specified in the SHA).
11.3 Waiver
A waiver of any right or remedy under this Deed is only effective if it is in writing and signed by the party
granting the waiver.
No waiver of a breach of any provision of this Deed operates as a waiver of any other breach of that
provision or any other provision.
11.4 Severability
If any provision of this Deed is invalid, illegal, or unenforceable in any jurisdiction:
      (a) that provision is severed from this Deed in that jurisdiction to the extent of the invalidity,
      illegality, or unenforceability; and
      (b) the remaining provisions continue in full force and effect in that jurisdiction and in all other
      jurisdictions.
11.5 Counterparts
This Deed may be executed in any number of counterparts (including electronic counterparts transmitted
by email or DocuSign). Each counterpart is an original, and all counterparts together constitute one
instrument.
11.6 Governing Law
This Deed is governed by the laws of New South Wales, Australia.
11.7 Jurisdiction
Each Party irrevocably:
      (a) submits to the non-exclusive jurisdiction of the courts of New South Wales and courts of appeal
      from them for any proceedings arising out of or in connection with this Deed; and
      (b) waives any objection to proceedings in those courts on the ground of venue or on the ground
      that the proceedings have been brought in an inconvenient forum.
11.8 Costs
Each Party bears its own legal, accounting, and advisory costs incurred in connection with the
negotiation, preparation, execution, and performance of this Deed.
11.9 Further Assurances
Each Party must, at its own expense, do all things and execute all documents necessary or desirable to
give full effect to this Deed and the transactions contemplated by it.
11.10 Third Party Beneficiaries
This Deed is intended to benefit Series A Investors, who are entitled to:
      (a) rely on the statements, acknowledgments, representations, warranties, undertakings, and
      indemnities given by CBS in this Deed; and
      (b) enforce this Deed directly against CBS as third party beneficiaries under the principles
      recognised in Trident General Insurance Co Ltd v McNiece Bros Pty Ltd (1988) 165 CLR 107 and
      the Contracts (Rights of Third Parties) Act (if applicable in the relevant jurisdiction).
Series A Investors may enforce this Deed without joining the Company or CobaltBlu as parties to any
proceedings.
11.11 Notices
Any notice, demand, consent, or other communication under this Deed must be:
      (a) in writing;
      (b) signed by an authorised officer of the sender; and
      (c) delivered by hand, sent by email, or sent by prepaid registered post to the recipient’s address
      set out in this Deed (or such other address as the recipient notifies in writing).
A notice is deemed to be received:
      (d) if delivered by hand, on delivery;
      (e) if sent by email, on the earlier of the sender receiving an automated receipt confirmation or at
      the time sent (if sent on a Business Day before 5:00pm at the recipient’s location, otherwise the
      next Business Day); or
      (f) if sent by prepaid registered post, 3 Business Days after posting (or 7 Business Days if posted to
      or from a location outside Australia).

STANDING NOTICE OF MATERIAL PERSONAL INTEREST

Section 192, Corporations Act 2001 (Cth)

To: The Directors of CBS Group Pty Ltd (ACN 164 870 080)
From: JeJrey Alan Dusting
Date: 14 January 2026

Re: Standing Notice of Material Personal Interest under section 192 of the Corporations
Act 2001 (Cth)



1. NATURE OF INTERESTS

1.1 WaterRoads Directorship

I am a director of WaterRoads Pty Ltd (ACN 686 900 014) (WaterRoads). CBS Group
holds 100 Class B Shares in WaterRoads, representing 9.09% of the issued share capital
prior to the recapitalisation described in WaterRoads Board Resolutions WR-2026-000
to WR-2026-003 (the Recapitalisation), and will hold 4,000,000 Common Shares
(4.00%) following the Recapitalisation and share subdivision. CBS Group is also the
lender under a Secured Loan Agreement dated 31 August 2025, providing a facility of up
to A$500,000 secured over WaterRoads' assets. As a director of WaterRoads, I owe
duties to WaterRoads under sections 180–184 of the Corporations Act 2001 (Cth), which
may conﬂict with my duties as a director of CBS Group Pty Ltd (CBS Group or
the Company).

1.2 CobaltBlu Directorship

I am a director of CobaltBlu Pty Ltd (ACN 103 595 071) (CobaltBlu). CobaltBlu is the
majority shareholder of WaterRoads, holding 1,000 Founder's Shares (90.91%) prior to
the Recapitalisation and 96,000,000 F Shares (96.00%) following the Recapitalisation
and share subdivision. As a director of CobaltBlu, I owe duties to CobaltBlu under
sections 180–184 of the Corporations Act 2001 (Cth), which may conﬂict with my duties
as a director of CBS Group.

1.3 CobaltBlu Beneﬁcial Ownership

I hold a 50% beneﬁcial interest in the issued share capital of CobaltBlu, acting as the
Trustee for the CobaltBlu Unit Trust of which I hold a 50% beneﬁciary interest. The
remaining interest is held by my spouse, Sarah Margaret Taylor. I therefore have a direct
beneﬁcial interest in CobaltBlu's shareholding in WaterRoads, which increases from
90.91% to 96.00% under the Recapitalisation. The Recapitalisation beneﬁts CobaltBlu
(and therefore me personally) at the expense of CBS Group's proportionate
shareholding in WaterRoads (which decreases from 9.09% to 4.00%).
1.4 Spousal Relationship

I am the spouse of Sarah Margaret Taylor. Sarah Taylor is a director and the Company
Secretary of WaterRoads, and a director and 50% beneﬁcial owner of CobaltBlu. By
reason of this spousal relationship, I have an interest in any matter that aJects Sarah
Taylor's interests as a director, oJicer, or beneﬁcial owner of any entity that deals with
CBS Group or in which CBS Group holds an interest.



2. EXTENT OF INTERESTS

 Entity / Person         Position /         Nature of Potential Conﬂict with CBS Group
                         Interest           Duties


                                            Owes duties to CBS Group and its
 CBS Group Pty Ltd       Director           stakeholders.


                                            Concurrent duties to WaterRoads; may
                                            conﬂict where CBS Group's interests as
                                            shareholder and lender diverge from
                                            WaterRoads' interests as borrower and
 WaterRoads Pty Ltd      Director           investee.


                                            CobaltBlu is the majority WaterRoads
                                            shareholder whose ownership increases

                                            Spousal relationship creates indirect interest
                                            in all matters aJecting Sarah Taylor's

 Taylor                  Spouse             CobaltBlu director and owner.

Summary of conﬂict: I simultaneously owe duties to CBS Group (as its director), to
WaterRoads (as its director), and to CobaltBlu (as its director and 50% beneﬁcial
owner). Where CBS Group is asked to consent to, approve, or facilitate any matter that
beneﬁts WaterRoads or CobaltBlu — including the Recapitalisation, which reduces CBS
Group's ownership from 9.09% to 4.00% while increasing CobaltBlu's from 90.91% to
96.00% — I have a material personal interest that may conﬂict with CBS Group's
interests. My spousal relationship with Sarah Taylor further compounds this conﬂict.



3. MATTERS TO WHICH THIS NOTICE RELATES

This Standing Notice relates to, but is not limited to, the following matters considered by
the CBS Group board:

(a) The consent by CBS Group to the Recapitalisation of WaterRoads, including the
cancellation and reissuance of shares, adoption of a new Constitution, share
subdivision, and the reduction of CBS Group's ownership from 9.09% to 4.00%
(Schedule D — Existing Shareholder Consent);

(b) Any decision by CBS Group regarding the Secured Loan Agreement dated 31 August
2025 with WaterRoads, including any repayment, prepayment, conversion, waiver,
amendment, discharge, or enforcement of that facility;

(c) Any waiver by CBS Group of its pre-emptive rights, anti-dilution protections, or other
shareholder rights in connection with WaterRoads' Series A capital raise or any future
equity issuance;

(d) Any decision by CBS Group to transfer, encumber, or otherwise deal with its shares
in WaterRoads, including any exercise of drag-along or tag-along rights;

(e) Any negotiation, amendment, or variation of the terms on which CBS Group holds
shares in WaterRoads, including any shareholders' agreement, constitutional
amendments, or changes to class rights;

(f) Any decision regarding the release of security interests granted by WaterRoads in
favour of CBS Group, including any discharge of the general security arrangement under
the Secured Loan Agreement;

(g) Any related-party transaction within the meaning of Chapter 2E of the Corporations
Act 2001 (Cth) between CBS Group and WaterRoads, CobaltBlu, Sarah Taylor, or any
entity controlled by or associated with any of them;

(h) Any future investment by CBS Group in WaterRoads, including any follow-on
investment, convertible note, or participation in future equity rounds; and

(i) Any other matter in which the interests described in section 1 may reasonably be
perceived to inﬂuence my judgment as a director of CBS Group.
4. RECOMMENDATION FOR INDEPENDENT DECISION-MAKING

Given the nature and extent of my interests as described above, I recommend that any
CBS Group board decision in respect of the matters listed in Section 3 be made by CBS
Group directors who do not have a material personal interest in those matters. In
particular, I recommend that:

(a) The CBS Group consent to the WaterRoads Recapitalisation (Schedule D) be signed
by a CBS Group director other than myself;

(b) Any CBS Group decision regarding the Secured Loan Agreement, including
acceptance of prepayment and execution of any discharge conﬁrmation, be approved
by a CBS Group director other than myself;

(c) I abstain from voting on any CBS Group board resolution relating to the matters
described in this notice, unless all other CBS Group directors determine that my
participation is appropriate.

Note: Jim Ellwood, a director of CBS Group who is independent of the Taylor–Dusting
family, has been identiﬁed as the appropriate signatory for all CBS Group documents
relating to WaterRoads matters.



5. POLICY ACKNOWLEDGMENTS

I acknowledge that:

(a) This Standing Notice does not authorise me to act improperly or relieve me of my
duties as a director of CBS Group under sections 180–184 of the Corporations Act 2001
(Cth);

(b) I remain obliged to act in good faith in the best interests of CBS Group, to exercise
care and diligence, and not to improperly use my position or information obtained as a
director;

(c) I have received, read, and will comply with CBS Group's Conﬂict of Interest — Board
Policy (Version 6.0 – Institutional), including the portfolio company and investment
conﬂict provisions in section 6.2 and Annexure C (CBS–WaterRoads–CobaltBlu Case
Study);

(d) I will update this Standing Notice if the nature or extent of any interest disclosed
above changes materially;

(e) By reason of my concurrent directorships of WaterRoads and CobaltBlu, my 50%
beneﬁcial ownership of CobaltBlu, and my spousal relationship with Sarah Taylor, my
judgment on WaterRoads-related matters may reasonably be perceived as inﬂuenced
by interests other than those of CBS Group;
(f) Where CBS Group requires disinterested director approval for a WaterRoads-related
matter, a director other than myself (such as Jim Ellwood) should provide that approval;
and

(g) This Standing Notice extends to any matter in which the interests described in
section 1 may reasonably be perceived to inﬂuence my judgment as a director.



6. DURATION AND TABLING

This Standing Notice remains in eJect until:

(a) I notify the Board that an interest has ceased or materially changed; or
(b) I withdraw or vary this notice in writing.

Under section 192(3) of the Corporations Act 2001 (Cth), this Standing Notice must be
tabled at the next directors' meeting of CBS Group after it is given. I request that this
notice be tabled accordingly and recorded in the minutes of that meeting.

## CBS Board Meeting — February 2026


### 04.1 CBS Group Conflict of Interest Policy V6.0 (Institutional) copy.docx

*File: `04.1 CBS Group Conflict of Interest Policy V6.0 (Institutional) copy.docx`*

CBS GROUP PTY LTD

ACN 164 870 080

CONFLICT OF INTEREST — BOARD POLICY

Version: 6.0 (Institutional)

Adopted by the Board: 5 February 2026

Effective Date: 5 February 2026

Next Review: 5 February 2027

Classification: Board Policy — Investment Governance Document

Supersedes: Version 1.0 (February 2026)

1. PURPOSE

This policy establishes the framework by which directors and officers of CBS Group Pty Ltd (the Company) identify, disclose, and manage conflicts of interest and material personal interests in connection with the affairs of the Company and its investment portfolio. It is designed to:

(a) ensure compliance with sections 191, 192, 194, and 195 of the Corporations Act 2001 (Cth) (the Act) and Chapter 2E (Related Party Transactions);

(b) satisfy the disinterested director and related-party provisions of the Company's Constitution;

(c) provide a clear, auditable governance trail for stakeholders, regulators, and future directors;

(d) establish practical procedures that reflect the Company's current board composition and investment activities; and

(e) address the specific conflicts arising from the Company's investment in WaterRoads Pty Ltd (ACN 686 900 014) (WaterRoads), where a CBS Group director also serves on the WaterRoads board.

2. SCOPE

This policy applies to all directors of the Company, including any alternate directors, and to any officer or senior manager who participates in board-level decision-making or has authority to bind the Company.

Portfolio Company Context: This policy includes specific protocols for managing conflicts arising from the Company's investment in WaterRoads and the concurrent directorship held by Jeffrey Alan Dusting on both the CBS Group and WaterRoads boards (Section 6.2 and Annexure C).

3. DEFINITIONS

In this Policy, unless the context otherwise requires:

4. CURRENT BOARD COMPOSITION AND STANDING DISCLOSURES

The Board acknowledges the following facts relevant to conflict management as at the date of this policy:

4.1 Directors and Relationships

Jeffrey Alan Dusting — Director of CBS Group. Also Director of WaterRoads Pty Ltd (ACN 686 900 014) and Director and 50% beneficial owner of CobaltBlu Pty Ltd (ACN 103 595 071). Spouse of Sarah Margaret Taylor.

Jim Ellwood — Director of CBS Group. No material personal interest in WaterRoads, CobaltBlu, or the Taylor–Dusting family.

[Other directors, if any] — [To be completed based on current board composition]

4.2 WaterRoads Investment and Concurrent Directorship

CBS Group holds 100 Class B Shares in WaterRoads, representing 9.09% of WaterRoads' issued share capital prior to the WaterRoads recapitalisation (Board Resolutions WR-2026-000 to WR-2026-003), and 4,000,000 Common Shares (4.00%) following the recapitalisation and share subdivision.

CBS Group is also the lender under a Secured Loan Agreement dated 31 August 2025 with WaterRoads, providing a facility of up to A$500,000 secured over WaterRoads' assets.

Jeffrey Alan Dusting serves as a director of both CBS Group and WaterRoads, creating a concurrent directorship and fiduciary duty conflict. Jeff also serves as a director and 50% beneficial owner of CobaltBlu Pty Ltd, which is the majority shareholder of WaterRoads (holding 96% following the recapitalisation). This creates a direct conflict where CBS Group's interests as a minority WaterRoads shareholder and lender may diverge from the interests of CobaltBlu (the majority shareholder) and WaterRoads itself.

4.3 Standing Disclosures

Jeffrey Alan Dusting has executed a Standing Notice under section 192 of the Act, tabled at the CBS Group board meeting on [●] February 2026, disclosing:

(a) his directorship of WaterRoads;

(b) his directorship and 50% beneficial ownership of CobaltBlu (the majority WaterRoads shareholder);

(c) his spousal relationship with Sarah Margaret Taylor (a director and company secretary of WaterRoads and director and 50% beneficial owner of CobaltBlu); and

(d) the material personal interests arising from these relationships in all CBS Group decisions relating to WaterRoads.

That Standing Notice remains in effect and is filed in the Company's governance records (Annexure B).

5. DISCLOSURE OBLIGATIONS

5.1 Statutory Disclosure (s191/s192)

A director who has a material personal interest in a matter relating to the affairs of the Company must, as soon as practicable after becoming aware of the interest, disclose the nature and extent of that interest to the other directors. Disclosure may be given:

(a) orally at a board meeting, to be recorded in the minutes of that meeting (s191); or

(b) by Standing Notice in writing, tabled at the next board meeting (s192).

Penalty for non-disclosure: Section 191(1) creates a strict liability offence carrying a penalty of up to 50 penalty units (currently A$22,200) per director per undisclosed matter.

5.2 When Disclosure Is Required

Disclosure is required whenever a director has, or may reasonably be perceived to have, a material personal interest in a matter before the Board. This includes, without limitation:

(a) any transaction, arrangement, or dealing involving a Portfolio Company in which the director holds a directorship, investment, or other material interest;

(b) any matter that confers or may confer a financial benefit (as defined in s229) on a related party;

(c) any matter in which a director's spouse, de facto partner, or close family member has a material interest;

(d) any matter in which a director has a conflicting duty to another entity (including a directorship obligation to a Portfolio Company);

(e) approval of the Company's remuneration, equity grants, or benefits to directors or their associates;

(f) any contract or proposed contract in which a director has a direct or indirect pecuniary interest; and

(g) any matter where the director's judgment may reasonably be perceived as influenced by interests other than the Company's interests.

5.3 Standing Notices

Where a director's interest in a matter is of an ongoing nature (for example, a directorship of another entity, a shareholding, or a spousal relationship), the director should give a Standing Notice under section 192. A Standing Notice must:

(a) be in writing;

(b) set out the nature and extent of the interest;

(c) include explicit acknowledgment of the director's obligations under this Policy;

(d) include a statement that the notice extends to any matter in which the interests may reasonably be perceived to influence the director's judgment;

(e) be tabled at the next board meeting after it is given; and

(f) be updated whenever the nature or extent of the interest materially changes.

A Standing Notice has ongoing effect and covers all matters within its stated scope. It does not need to be re-given at each meeting, but the Chair should note at the commencement of each meeting whether any Standing Notices are in effect and whether any updates are required.

5.4 Timing and Form

On appointment: Each new director must complete a disclosure form and provide a Standing Notice (if applicable) before attending their first board meeting.

Annually: Each director must confirm annually that their Standing Notice remains current or provide an updated notice.

As conflicts arise: Directors must disclose new conflicts immediately upon becoming aware of them.

At meetings: The Chair will ask for conflict declarations at the start of each meeting for matters on the agenda.

6. PROCEDURES FOR MANAGING CONFLICTS

6.1 General Procedure

When a conflict of interest or material personal interest is identified in relation to a matter before the Board, the following procedure applies:

Step 1 — Disclosure. The conflicted director discloses the interest (if not already covered by a Standing Notice). The disclosure is recorded in the minutes.

Step 2 — Assessment. The Board (or, where available, the disinterested directors) assesses the nature and severity of the conflict. The assessment considers:

whether the interest is direct or indirect;

whether it is financial or non-financial;

the materiality of the interest and the transaction;

whether it could objectively influence the director's judgment;

whether there is a reasonable perception of conflict; and

whether Independent Advice or other safeguards are required.

Step 3 — Management. Based on the assessment, the Board applies one or more of the following management strategies:

Step 4 — Record. The minutes of the meeting must record the conflict management approach taken, including:

which strategy was applied and why;

if s194 reliance, the commercial rationale for the decision;

if Independent Advice obtained, the conclusions and where it is filed;

cross-reference to Register of Interests entry; and

for Material Transactions, confirmation of arm's length terms or member approval obtained.

Step 5 — Register Update. The Company Secretary updates the Register of Interests and Related Party Transaction Register (Annexure C).

6.2 Portfolio Company and Investment Conflicts

6.2.1 WaterRoads-Specific Protocol

For any CBS Group decision relating to WaterRoads (including the Secured Loan Agreement, loan repayment, consent to the WaterRoads recapitalisation, exercise of shareholder rights, or any future dealings):

(a) Jeffrey Alan Dusting must recuse from the discussion and vote (leave the meeting or be excluded from the relevant portion);

(b) the remaining disinterested directors (currently Jim Ellwood) approve the decision;

(c) the minutes record Jeff's recusal and the disinterested directors' approval;

(d) for Material Transactions, the Board obtains Independent Advice to confirm that the decision is in CBS Group's commercial interests;

(e) any CBS Group documents relating to WaterRoads are executed by a disinterested director (Jim Ellwood is the current appropriate signatory); and

(f) all communications between CBS Group and WaterRoads are directed to disinterested officers or directors on both sides (Jim Ellwood for CBS Group; Sarah Taylor for WaterRoads, noting her indirect spousal interest but lack of CBS directorship).

Rationale: Jeff has a direct conflict arising from his WaterRoads directorship, his CobaltBlu directorship and 50% beneficial ownership, and his spousal relationship with Sarah Taylor (who is also conflicted in WaterRoads matters). Recusal and disinterested director approval is the only appropriate governance mechanism.

Documented Transactions: The following WaterRoads-related decisions have been made under this protocol:

6.2.2 General Portfolio Company Conflicts

Where a CBS Group director holds a directorship, investment, or other material interest in a Portfolio Company (other than WaterRoads):

(a) the director must give a Standing Notice disclosing the interest;

(b) for investment decisions, valuation, or exit decisions relating to that Portfolio Company, the director must recuse unless all other directors determine that the director's participation is appropriate and the conflict is adequately managed;

(c) the minutes must record the conflict and the management approach; and

(d) for Material Transactions, Independent Advice should be obtained.

6.2.3 Materiality Guidance

To assist in applying the conflict management framework, the Board has adopted the following materiality guidance:

Minor conflicts (typically managed via monitoring):

Transactions under A$10,000 on arm's length terms

Standard commercial hospitality or gifts of trivial value (under A$250)

Matters where the director's interest is remote or purely theoretical

Material conflicts (require recusal, Independent Advice, or heightened safeguards):

Transactions exceeding A$50,000

Any transaction involving non-standard or preferential terms

Any transaction where the director has competing fiduciary duties (including concurrent directorships)

Director remuneration or equity grants

Enforcement, waiver, or variation of existing related party contracts

Portfolio Company investment, valuation, or exit decisions

When in doubt, directors should err on the side of disclosure and seek guidance from the Chair or Company Secretary.

7. CHAPTER 2E — RELATED PARTY TRANSACTIONS

The Company must comply with Chapter 2E of the Act when giving a financial benefit to a related party. The Board must consider, for each proposed related-party transaction:

(a) whether the transaction constitutes a "financial benefit" to a "related party" within the meaning of sections 228–229;

(b) whether an exception under sections 210–216 applies — in particular:

s210: arm's length exception (terms no more favourable than reasonably expected if dealing at arm's length)

s211: reasonable remuneration exception

s212: small amounts exception (less than A$5,000 and reasonable in the circumstances)

(c) if no exception applies, whether member approval has been or can be obtained under section 208;

(d) the documentation required to evidence the exception relied upon (for example, Independent Advice, market comparables, valuation report, or legal opinion); and

(e) for Material Transactions (over A$50,000), mandatory Independent Advice to confirm arm's length terms or commercial reasonableness.

7.1 Related Party Transaction Register

The Board maintains a Related Party Transaction Register (Annexure C) recording each related-party transaction, including:

date and description of transaction

related party involved

Chapter 2E exception relied upon

supporting documentation (Independent Advice, legal opinion, valuation)

board approval reference

cross-reference to minutes

This register is available for inspection by directors, auditors, and (to the extent required) members, and is maintained in the Company's governance records.

7.2 Independent Advice Requirements

The following transactions require Independent Advice:

(a) any related-party transaction exceeding A$50,000;

(b) any related-party transaction involving non-standard or preferential terms;

(c) any material variation, waiver, or enforcement decision relating to existing related-party contracts;

(d) any transaction where reliance on the s210 arm's length exception is proposed; and

(e) any transaction where the Board determines Independent Advice would strengthen the governance record.

Independent Advice must be filed in the Company's records, cross-referenced in the minutes, and made available to members upon request.

8. QUARTERLY CONFLICT REVIEW

The Board will conduct a conflict review at the first board meeting of each calendar quarter (or more frequently if circumstances require). The review will cover:

(a) confirmation that all Standing Notices remain current and accurate;

(b) identification of any new conflicts or changes in existing interests;

(c) review of the Related Party Transaction Register;

(d) assessment of whether conflict management procedures are operating effectively; and

(e) any recommendations for policy amendments.

The outcome of each quarterly review will be recorded in the minutes of the relevant board meeting.

9. NEW DIRECTOR ONBOARDING

Upon appointment, each new director must:

(a) receive a copy of:

this Policy;

the Company's Constitution;

copies of all current Standing Notices of other directors;

(b) complete and deliver a disclosure form covering all interests;

(c) execute and deliver a Standing Notice under section 192 disclosing all material personal interests (or confirm in writing that they have none); and

(d) sign a written acknowledgment that they have read, understood, and will comply with this Policy.

The Company Secretary will maintain a register of all Standing Notices, acknowledgments, and annual attestations.

10. RECORD-KEEPING

The following records will be maintained by the Company Secretary:

(a) this policy (current version and version history);

(b) all Standing Notices given by directors (current and historical);

(c) board minutes recording conflict disclosures, management decisions, and s194 reliance;

(d) the Register of Interests;

(e) the Related Party Transaction Register (Annexure C);

(f) all Independent Advice obtained in connection with related-party transactions;

(g) quarterly conflict review minutes; and

(h) annual director attestations and onboarding acknowledgments.

11. CONSEQUENCES OF BREACH

A breach of this policy may result in:

(a) the relevant board resolution being voidable (s195);

(b) criminal liability under section 191(1) (strict liability, up to 50 penalty units / A$22,200 per director);

(c) civil liability for breach of fiduciary duties or the statutory duty of good faith (s181) and duty not to improperly use position (s182);

(d) remedial action determined by the Board, which may include requiring the director to resign from the conflicting position, divest the conflicting interest, or (in serious cases) recommending removal from the Board; and

(e) where a breach involves potential Corporations Act contravention, consideration of whether a report to ASIC or other regulator is required.

The Chair must report any material breach to the Board at the next meeting. The Board will determine appropriate action and, if applicable, notify members.

12. REVIEW AND AMENDMENT

This policy must be reviewed:

(a) within 12 months of adoption (by 5 February 2027);

(b) upon any material change in the Company's board composition or investment portfolio; and

(c) upon receipt of member or stakeholder feedback relating to conflict management.

12.1 Amendment Process

This policy may be amended by resolution of the Board. Any amendment must be:

(a) recorded in the minutes;

(b) communicated to all directors within 7 days; and

(c) reflected in an updated version number and effective date.

ADOPTION

This policy was adopted by resolution of the Board of Directors of CBS Group Pty Ltd on 5 February 2026.

ANNEXURE A — REGISTER OF INTERESTS

This register records all Standing Notices and ongoing director interests. It is maintained by the Company Secretary and reviewed quarterly.

To be updated whenever a director gives, varies, or withdraws a Standing Notice.

ANNEXURE B — STANDING NOTICE (JEFFREY ALAN DUSTING)

Attached separately — see "Standing Notice — Jeffrey Alan Dusting — CBS Group V6 (Institutional).docx"

ANNEXURE C — RELATED PARTY TRANSACTION REGISTER (CBS–WATERROADS–COBALTBLU)

This register records all transactions between CBS Group and WaterRoads. It is maintained by the Company Secretary and reviewed quarterly by the Board.

Additional rows to be added as transactions arise. Each entry to be reviewed at the quarterly conflict review (Section 8).

END OF POLICY

Document Control:



| Term | Meaning |

| Conflict of Interest | Any situation in which a director's personal interests, duties to another entity, or relationships (including spousal, familial, or financial relationships) could, or could reasonably be perceived to, influence their judgment, decisions, or actions in relation to the Company's affairs. |

| Material Personal Interest | An interest as defined in section 191 of the Act — an interest that could objectively influence, or be seen to influence, the director's approach to a matter. Includes direct financial interests, interests arising through related entities or investments, and interests arising through spousal or familial relationships. |

| Related Party | As defined in sections 228–229 of the Act. Includes directors, entities controlled by directors, spouses of directors, and entities in which directors hold material interests. |

| Disinterested Director | A director who has no material personal interest (direct or indirect, including through spousal relationship) in the matter under consideration and who is not a related party in respect of the relevant transaction. |

| Standing Notice | A notice given under section 192 of the Act, disclosing the nature and extent of a director's interests in a matter. A Standing Notice has ongoing effect and covers all future matters within its stated scope until varied or withdrawn. |

| Material Transaction | Any related party transaction involving consideration or value exceeding A$50,000, or any transaction which, regardless of value, is outside ordinary course or involves non-standard terms. |

| Independent Advice | Advice from a qualified external adviser (legal, financial, valuation, or other relevant expert) who has no material relationship with the Company, the conflicted director, or any Related Party. |

| Portfolio Company | Any entity in which CBS Group holds, or is considering holding, an investment (including debt or equity). For the purposes of this policy, WaterRoads Pty Ltd is a Portfolio Company. |



| Strategy | When Appropriate |

| Recusal | The conflicted director leaves the meeting room (or is excluded from the relevant portion of a virtual meeting) for the duration of the discussion and vote. The minutes record the director's departure and return. This is the preferred approach where a disinterested quorum can be maintained. |

| Disclosure and participation under s194 | Where the Company is a proprietary company and no disinterested quorum is available, the conflicted director(s) may participate in discussion and vote, provided the interest has been fully disclosed under s191 or s192. The minutes must record: the disclosure, the basis for relying on s194, the commercial rationale for the decision, and that the Board was satisfied the decision was in the Company's interests. |

| Independent Advice | For Material Transactions, the Board obtains Independent Advice (legal, financial, or valuation) to confirm that the transaction is on arm's length terms or is otherwise in the Company's commercial interests. This strengthens the governance record and supports the arm's length exception under s210. |

| Member approval | For transactions that constitute a "financial benefit to a related party" under Chapter 2E and do not fall within a recognised exception (arm's length terms under s210, reasonable remuneration under s211, or other exceptions in ss212–216), the Company must obtain member approval under s208 before giving the benefit. |
