### 04.2 CBS_Board_Resolutions_V1_0_Institutional.docx

*File: `04.2 CBS_Board_Resolutions_V1_0_Institutional.docx`*

CBS GROUP PTY LTD

ACN 164 870 080

WRITTEN RESOLUTIONS OF DIRECTORS

Pursuant to section 248A of the Corporations Act 2001 (Cth)

Date: 16 January 2026

CONFIDENTIAL — BOARD PAPER

Version 1.0 (Institutional — Series A Optimised). Aligned with Constitution V3.1 and V7 document suite (Recapitalisation Deed V7, CBS Consent and Waiver Deed V7, CBS Loan Variation and Waiver Deed V7).

PREAMBLE

The undersigned, being all of the directors of CBS Group Pty Ltd ACN 164 870 080 (CBS or the Company), pass the following resolutions in writing pursuant to section 248A of the Corporations Act 2001 (Cth) (the Act). These resolutions are effective when signed by all directors entitled to vote on each resolution, and have the same effect as if passed at a duly convened meeting of directors.

BACKGROUND AND CONTEXT

A. CBS’s Interests in Water Roads

CBS holds 100 Class B shares in Water Roads Pty Ltd ACN 686 900 014 (Water Roads or Portfolio Company), representing 9.09% of Water Roads’ issued share capital as at the date of these resolutions.

CBS is also a secured lender to Water Roads pursuant to a loan agreement dated [INSERT LOAN DATE — verify: 1 August or 31 August 2025] (the Loan Agreement), under which approximately A$209,000 (principal and accrued interest) is outstanding.

B. The Recapitalisation

Water Roads proposes to implement a recapitalisation (the Recapitalisation) to correct historic defects in its capital structure and align the share register with the agreed ownership structure between CobaltBlu Pty Ltd ACN 103 595 071 (CobaltBlu) and CBS.

The Recapitalisation involves the following sequential steps:

(i) the cancellation of all 1,100 existing shares in Water Roads (including CBS’s 100 Class B shares);

(ii) the issue of 100,000 new shares (96,000 F Shares to CobaltBlu and 4,000 Common Shares to CBS);

(iii) a 10-for-1 share split, increasing total share count to 1,000,000 (960,000 F Shares held by CobaltBlu and 40,000 Common Shares held by CBS); and

(iv) the adoption of an Amended and Restated Constitution V3.1 for Water Roads (the New Constitution).

C. Effect on CBS’s Position

Following the Recapitalisation:

(a) CBS’s shareholding will decrease from 9.09% (100 Class B shares) to 4.00% (40,000 Common Shares after the share split);

(b) CBS’s shares will change class from “Class B” to “Common Shares” ranking in accordance with the New Constitution;

(c) the Loan Agreement will remain in force but will be subordinated to Series A investors and subject to mandatory repayment at Series A close; and

(d) CBS will retain its current rights under the Loan Agreement (as varied) until discharge at Series A close.

The directors note that the reduction from 9.09% to 4.00% reflects the correction of a historic defect in Water Roads’ capital structure and alignment with the Agreed Ownership (as defined in the Recapitalisation Deed). It does not represent a dilutive or prejudicial act against CBS.

D. Documents Requiring CBS Execution

CBS is required to execute the following documents in connection with the Recapitalisation:

(a) Recapitalisation Deed V7 dated 15 January 2026 between Water Roads, CobaltBlu, and CBS (the Recap Deed);

(b) CBS Consent and Waiver Deed V7 between Water Roads, CobaltBlu, and CBS (the Consent Deed), under which CBS:

(i) consents to the Recapitalisation and adoption of the New Constitution;

(ii) waives pre-emptive rights, change of control rights, and other rights that would be triggered by the Recapitalisation or Series A;

(iii) acknowledges its reduced shareholding of 4.00%; and

(iv) provides Series A-related consents and undertakings;

(c) CBS Loan Variation and Waiver Deed V7 between Water Roads and CBS (the Loan Variation Deed), under which CBS:

(i) waives all change of control and covenant rights under the Loan Agreement triggered by the Recapitalisation and Series A;

(ii) subordinates the Loan Agreement to Series A investors in right of payment and security;

(iii) permits Water Roads to grant security interests to Series A investors ranking ahead of CBS’s security;

(iv) commits to full discharge of the Loan Agreement upon receipt of repayment at Series A close; and

(v) agrees to execute all documents required to release security and remove PPSR registrations.

E. Series A Financing

Water Roads intends to pursue a Series A equity financing following the Recapitalisation. Key implications for CBS:

(a) CBS’s percentage shareholding will be further diluted by the Series A issuance;

(b) the Loan Agreement will be repaid in full from Series A proceeds and all security released;

(c) CBS will be required to enter into a Shareholders Agreement with Series A investors; and

(d) the waivers given by CBS in the Consent Deed and Loan Variation Deed are permanent and unconditional — they will not revive regardless of the post-Series A ownership structure.

CONFLICT OF INTEREST DISCLOSURE

Material Personal Interests

The directors make the following disclosures for the purposes of sections 191, 192, and 194 of the Act:

(a) Jeffrey Alan Dusting:

Director of CBS

Director of Water Roads

Director and 50% shareholder of CobaltBlu (which holds 90.91% pre-Recap / 96% post-Recap of Water Roads)

Spouse of Sarah Margaret Taylor (director and Company Secretary of Water Roads, and director and 50% shareholder of CobaltBlu)

(b) Jim Ellwood:

Director of CBS

Observer at Water Roads board meetings (not a director of Water Roads)

No shareholding in Water Roads or CobaltBlu

No familial or spousal relationship with any other director or shareholder of Water Roads or CobaltBlu

Nature of Conflict

Jeffrey Alan Dusting has a material personal interest in the resolutions below by virtue of:

(i) his role as a director of Water Roads (the company subject to the Recapitalisation);

(ii) his role as a director and 50% shareholder of CobaltBlu (the majority shareholder and counterparty to the Recap Deed);

(iii) his beneficial ownership interest in Water Roads through CobaltBlu’s shareholding; and

(iv) his spousal relationship with Sarah Margaret Taylor, who holds the same interests in CobaltBlu and Water Roads.

Jim Ellwood does not have a material personal interest in the resolutions below. He is a disinterested director for the purposes of these resolutions.

Statutory Basis for Voting

CBS has two directors: Jeffrey Alan Dusting (interested) and Jim Ellwood (disinterested).

Section 195(1) of the Act prohibits an interested director from being present at, or voting on, a matter in which they have a material personal interest, unless the remaining directors pass a resolution allowing participation, or an exception in s195(1) applies.

Resolution on Jeffrey Alan Dusting’s participation: Jim Ellwood, as the sole disinterested director, resolves under section 195(1)(b) of the Act that Jeffrey Alan Dusting may be present at the consideration of the resolutions in this document, but must abstain from voting on all resolutions. This is appropriate because:

(a) Jeff’s presence allows Jim Ellwood to ask questions and obtain information about the Recapitalisation and the CBS documents;

(b) Jeff’s multi-directorship position means he has detailed knowledge of the transaction that is relevant to Jim Ellwood’s decision-making; and

(c) Jeff will not vote on any resolution, ensuring the decisions are made solely by the disinterested director.

Alternative basis — s194: To the extent that any question arises as to whether s195 or s194 applies (CBS being a proprietary company), the directors note that both sections are satisfied: Jeff has disclosed his interests under s192, and the resolutions are approved by the disinterested director alone.

Standing Notices

Jeffrey Alan Dusting has given a Standing Notice under section 192 of the Act dated 1 January 2026, tabled at the CBS board meeting of 16 January 2026, disclosing his ongoing interests in:

Water Roads (directorship)

CobaltBlu (directorship, 50% shareholding)

Spousal relationship with Sarah Margaret Taylor and indirect interests

That Standing Notice remains in effect and covers all matters addressed in these resolutions.

Commercial Rationale

Jim Ellwood, as the sole voting director, is satisfied that the resolutions below are in CBS’s interests because:

(a) the Recapitalisation corrects Historic Defects in Water Roads’ capital structure and aligns the share register with the Agreed Ownership of 96% CobaltBlu / 4% CBS, which was always the intended deal;

(b) the reduction from 9.09% to 4.00% reflects the correction of a historical error, not a dilutive act against CBS;

(c) the Series A financing is necessary for Water Roads to execute its business plan, which in turn protects and enhances the value of CBS’s shareholding;

(d) the CBS Loan (approximately A$209,000 outstanding) will be repaid in full at Series A close from Series A proceeds, eliminating CBS’s credit exposure;

(e) the subordination of the Loan Agreement to Series A investors is commercially necessary to facilitate the Series A (no institutional investor would invest behind an unsubordinated related-party loan) and does not prejudice CBS because the loan will be repaid in full at close;

(f) the waivers given by CBS (change of control, pre-emptive rights, covenant waivers) are necessary to implement the Recapitalisation and Series A, and CBS’s economic position is preserved through its 4.00% equity holding and the mandatory loan repayment;

(g) the terms of the CBS documents (Consent Deed V7, Loan Variation Deed V7) are fair and reasonable, and have been drafted with appropriate protections for CBS’s economic interests; and

(h) the decision-making process (Jeff’s abstention, independent director approval, full disclosure, documentation of rationale) is appropriate and robust.

RESOLUTIONS

(Passed pursuant to section 248A of the Corporations Act)

Resolution 1 — Approval of Recapitalisation

RESOLVED (Jim Ellwood voting; Jeffrey Alan Dusting abstaining) that the directors of CBS approve CBS’s participation in the Recapitalisation of Water Roads on the terms set out in the Recapitalisation Deed V7 dated 15 January 2026, including:

(a) the surrender for cancellation of CBS’s 100 Class B shares in Water Roads for nil consideration;

(b) the acceptance of 4,000 Common Shares in Water Roads (being 40,000 Common Shares after the 10-for-1 share split), issued for nil cash consideration on a share-for-share basis;

(c) the acceptance that CBS’s post-Recapitalisation shareholding of 4.00% reflects the Agreed Ownership as between CobaltBlu and CBS;

(d) the 10-for-1 share split of all Water Roads shares; and

(e) the adoption of the Amended and Restated Constitution V3.1 for Water Roads.

Resolution 2 — Approval of CBS Consent and Waiver Deed V7

RESOLVED (Jim Ellwood voting; Jeffrey Alan Dusting abstaining) that the directors of CBS approve CBS’s entry into the CBS Consent and Waiver Deed V7, including without limitation:

(a) all consents to the Recapitalisation, including consent to the cancellation and reissue of shares, the share split, and the adoption of the New Constitution;

(b) the waiver of pre-emptive rights under clause 8 of the New Constitution and any other pre-emptive rights CBS may have in respect of the Recapitalisation and Series A;

(c) the waiver of change of control, tag-along, drag-along, and other rights that would otherwise be triggered by the Recapitalisation or Series A;

(d) the acknowledgment that CBS’s shareholding has been reduced from 9.09% to 4.00%;

(e) the Series A consents, including consent to the issue of preferred shares with preferential rights ranking ahead of CBS’s Common Shares;

(f) the director conflict management provisions and undertakings; and

(g) all other consents, acknowledgments, confirmations, representations, and undertakings given by CBS in that deed.

Resolution 3 — Approval of CBS Loan Variation and Waiver Deed V7

RESOLVED (Jim Ellwood voting; Jeffrey Alan Dusting abstaining) that the directors of CBS approve CBS’s entry into the CBS Loan Variation and Waiver Deed V7, including without limitation:

(a) the irrevocable waiver of all change of control, ownership covenant, and related rights under the Loan Agreement that would be triggered by the Recapitalisation or any bona fide equity financing approved by the Water Roads board;

(b) the subordination of the Loan Agreement to Series A investors in right of payment, including the agreement that CBS will not demand repayment, take enforcement action, or exercise secured creditor rights without Water Roads board consent (including Series A director consent);

(c) the variation of any negative pledge in the Loan Agreement to permit Water Roads to grant security interests to Series A investors ranking ahead of CBS’s security;

(d) the binding commitment to repay the Loan Agreement in full from Series A proceeds at Series A close, with no prepayment penalty;

(e) the commitment to execute a deed of discharge and release, and all documents necessary to remove PPSR registrations, within 2 Business Days of receiving full repayment; and

(f) the agreement to cooperate with Water Roads and Series A investors to facilitate the orderly repayment and discharge of the Loan Agreement.

Resolution 4 — Approval of Recapitalisation Deed V7

RESOLVED (Jim Ellwood voting; Jeffrey Alan Dusting abstaining) that the directors of CBS approve:

(a) CBS’s entry into the Recapitalisation Deed V7 dated 15 January 2026 among Water Roads, CobaltBlu, and CBS;

(b) the performance by CBS of all obligations under that deed; and

(c) the exercise by CBS of all rights under that deed.

Resolution 5 — Series A Acknowledgment and Prospective Consents

RESOLVED (Jim Ellwood voting; Jeffrey Alan Dusting abstaining) that the directors of CBS note and acknowledge Water Roads’ intention to pursue a Series A equity financing, and:

(a) note that CBS’s percentage shareholding will be further diluted by the Series A issuance;

(b) note that the waivers given in the Consent Deed and Loan Variation Deed are permanent and will not revive after the Series A;

(c) note that the CBS Loan will be repaid in full from Series A proceeds;

(d) authorise the directors to negotiate and enter into a Shareholders Agreement on behalf of CBS in connection with the Series A, subject to the terms being consistent with market practice and not materially prejudicial to CBS’s interests; and

(e) note that this resolution provides a general acknowledgment of the Series A process and does not constitute approval of specific Series A terms (which may be subject to further CBS board approval depending on their nature and impact on CBS).

Resolution 6 — Authorisation to Execute Documents

RESOLVED (Jim Ellwood voting; Jeffrey Alan Dusting abstaining) that Jim Ellwood is authorised to execute, on behalf of CBS, the following documents:

(a) the Recapitalisation Deed V7 dated 15 January 2026;

(b) the CBS Consent and Waiver Deed V7;

(c) the CBS Loan Variation and Waiver Deed V7;

(d) any Shareholders Agreement to be entered into in connection with the Series A financing (subject to the limitations in Resolution 5(d));

(e) any transfer forms, share certificates, or ASIC forms required to record CBS’s updated shareholding following the Recapitalisation;

(f) the deed of discharge and release contemplated by clause 6.4 of the Loan Variation Deed;

(g) any subordination deeds, intercreditor agreements, or PPSR financing change statements required by Series A investors or the Loan Variation Deed; and

(h) any other documents reasonably incidental to the foregoing.

Manner of execution: Documents are to be executed by Jim Ellwood together with one other director or the company secretary in accordance with section 127 of the Act, or by Jim Ellwood alone where execution by a sole director/secretary is permitted. Jeffrey Alan Dusting may co-sign as the second s127 signatory where required for formal validity, provided the substantive approval has been given by Jim Ellwood alone.

Electronic execution: Documents may be executed electronically in accordance with the Electronic Transactions Act 1999 (Cth) and applicable state or territory legislation.

Resolution 7 — Ratification of Prior Actions

RESOLVED (Jim Ellwood voting; Jeffrey Alan Dusting abstaining) that all actions taken by the directors of CBS prior to the date of these resolutions in connection with the Recapitalisation, the Recap Deed, the Consent Deed, the Loan Variation Deed, and related matters are ratified, confirmed, and approved, including:

(a) participation in negotiations and discussions with Water Roads, CobaltBlu, and their advisers;

(b) review of drafts of the Recap Deed, Consent Deed, Loan Variation Deed, New Constitution, and related documents;

(c) Jim Ellwood’s attendance at Water Roads board meetings as an observer;

(d) provision of information, consents, and confirmations to Water Roads and CobaltBlu; and

(e) any other actions reasonably incidental to the foregoing.

Resolution 8 — Conflict Acknowledgment and Record

RESOLVED (Jim Ellwood voting; Jeffrey Alan Dusting present but abstaining) that the directors:

(a) acknowledge the material personal interests and conflicts of interest disclosed in the “Conflict of Interest Disclosure” section of these resolutions;

(b) confirm that Jeffrey Alan Dusting has given a Standing Notice under section 192 of the Act dated 1 January 2026, which was tabled at this meeting and covers all matters addressed in these resolutions;

(c) record that Jeffrey Alan Dusting was present at the consideration of these resolutions (pursuant to the s195(1)(b) resolution above) but abstained from voting on all resolutions;

(d) record that all resolutions were passed by Jim Ellwood as the sole disinterested director;

(e) record the commercial rationale as set out in the “Commercial Rationale” section above; and

(f) authorise either director to file these resolutions in CBS’s minute book and governance records, and to provide copies to Water Roads, CobaltBlu, and their legal advisers as required.

EXECUTION

The undersigned, being all of the directors of CBS Group Pty Ltd, sign these resolutions in accordance with section 248A of the Corporations Act 2001 (Cth).

VOTING DIRECTOR

PRESENT BUT ABSTAINING ON ALL RESOLUTIONS

Jeffrey Alan Dusting confirms that he was present during the consideration of the above resolutions, that he abstained from voting on all resolutions, and that the resolutions were passed by Jim Ellwood as the sole disinterested director.

Version 2.0. Aligned with Constitution V3.1 and V7 document suite. Includes adoption of CBS Conflict of Interest Policy, acknowledgment of executed documents, and noting of Constitution V3.1 provisions affecting CBS.

Pack Contents

The chair will direct the meeting accordingly.

Paper 3. Acknowledgment of Executed Documents and Constitution V3.1

3.1 Purpose

This paper asks the board to (a) formally acknowledge receipt of the executed Recapitalisation documents from Water Roads and CobaltBlu, and (b) note and acknowledge the key provisions of the Amended and Restated Constitution V3.1 that specifically affect CBS’s rights and obligations as a shareholder.

3.2 Documents Received

The following executed documents have been received (or are expected to be received) by CBS:

3.3 Constitution V3.1 — Key Provisions Affecting CBS

The January resolutions (Resolution 1) already authorised CBS’s participation in the Recapitalisation, which included the adoption of Constitution V3.1. This section provides a detailed summary of the provisions that specifically affect CBS’s position as a 4.00% Common Shareholder, for the board’s information and record.

(a) CBS’s Share Class and Rights

CBS holds 40,000 Common Shares (post-split). Common Shares carry one vote per share, pro rata dividend rights, and pro rata participation on winding up. CBS no longer holds “Class B” shares — the new two-class structure comprises F Shares (held by CobaltBlu) and Common Shares (held by CBS and, after Series A, by Series A investors).

(b) Founder Protective Provisions (Clause 20)

While CobaltBlu (the “F Share Majority”) holds ≥30% of all shares on a Fully Diluted Basis, clause 20.2 requires the F Share Majority’s prior written consent for specified major decisions, including:

(i) amendments to the Constitution adversely affecting F Share rights;

(ii) issues of shares ranking senior to or pari passu with F Shares (other than ESOP or Qualifying Financing);

(iii) disposal of all or substantially all Company assets;

(iv) merger, consolidation, or sale of the Company;

(v) voluntary winding up; and

(vi) change in principal business.

Implication for CBS: CobaltBlu has effective veto rights over these matters while it holds ≥30%. CBS’s 4.00% holding does not carry equivalent protective provisions.

(c) Founder Director Appointment (Clause 16.2)

While the F Share Majority holds ≥20% on a Fully Diluted Basis, CobaltBlu has the right to appoint one Founder Director to the Water Roads board. CBS does not currently have a board appointment right under the Constitution, though Jim Ellwood attends as an observer.

(d) F Share Conversion (Clause 4.4)

F Shares automatically convert to Common Shares on a 1:1 basis upon a Qualifying Financing (broadly, a bona fide equity raising of at least A$[●] on arm’s-length terms). After conversion, all shareholders hold the same class (Common), and the Founder Protective Provisions continue based on percentage thresholds, not share class.

(e) Pre-emptive Rights (Clause 8)

All shareholders (including CBS) have pro rata pre-emptive rights on new share issues, subject to carve-outs for the ESOP and Qualifying Financing. CBS has waived pre-emptive rights in respect of the Recapitalisation and Series A under the CBS Consent and Waiver Deed V7.

(f) Transfer Restrictions (Clause 9) and Tag-Along / Drag-Along (Clauses 11–12)

Shares are subject to pre-emptive transfer restrictions (right of first refusal to existing shareholders). Tag-along (clause 11) and drag-along (clause 12) provisions apply to all shareholders. CBS has waived these rights in connection with the Recapitalisation under the Consent Deed.

(g) Related Party Transactions (Clause 18)

The Constitution requires board disclosure and management of related party transactions. This is relevant to CBS given Jeffrey Alan Dusting’s cross-directorships.

(h) ESOP Pool (Clause 26)

The Constitution authorises an ESOP pool of up to 10% of fully diluted share capital. ESOP issuances will dilute all shareholders (including CBS) proportionally. No ESOP options will be granted until the Qualifying Financing strike price is established (clause 26.6).

(i) SHA Supremacy (Clause 22.2)

If a Shareholders Agreement is entered into in connection with the Series A, its terms prevail over the Constitution to the extent of any inconsistency. CBS’s rights under the Constitution may therefore be modified by the SHA.

Paper 4. CBS Loan Status and Discharge Timeline

4.1 Current Loan Position

4.2 Effect of CBS Loan Variation and Waiver Deed V7

The Loan Variation Deed (if executed) has the following operative effects:

(a) Covenant waivers: All change of control, ownership, and related covenants triggered by the Recapitalisation or any bona fide equity financing have been irrevocably waived.

(b) Subordination: The Loan Agreement has been subordinated to Series A investors in right of payment and security. CBS may not demand repayment or take enforcement action without Water Roads board consent (including Series A director consent).

(c) Security release: The negative pledge has been varied to permit Water Roads to grant security interests to Series A investors ranking ahead of CBS’s security.

(d) Mandatory repayment at close: Water Roads must repay the Loan Agreement in full from Series A proceeds. No prepayment penalty.

(e) Discharge mechanics: CBS must execute a deed of discharge and release, and all PPSR removal documents, within 2 Business Days of receiving full repayment.

All waivers and variations are permanent and unconditional.

6.3 Related Party Transaction Register

6.4 CBS Conflict of Interest Policy — Adoption

The CBS January board resolutions and the CBS Consent and Waiver Deed V7 both reference a conflict of interest framework. However, CBS has not yet formally adopted a written Conflict of Interest Policy. The chair proposes that the board adopt the CBS Conflict of Interest Policy V1.0 (attached as Appendix E) at this meeting.

Policy scope: The policy establishes a framework for identifying, disclosing, and managing conflicts of interest arising from CBS directors’ roles in Water Roads, CobaltBlu, and related entities. Key features include:

(a) mandatory disclosure of material personal interests under s191 and standing notices under s192;

(b) procedures for managing conflicts at board meetings, including the chair’s power to direct abstention or recusal;

(c) reliance on s194 (proprietary company) and s195 (disinterested director resolution) as the statutory framework for voting;

(d) maintenance of a Register of Interests and Related Party Transaction Register;

(e) a requirement for independent director approval of all transactions involving a conflict, where a disinterested director is available;

(f) engagement of independent legal or financial advisers for Material Transactions (defined as transactions exceeding A$[INSERT THRESHOLD]);

(g) an annual review of the policy; and

(h) provisions for the appointment of additional independent directors if the conflict framework becomes insufficient.

Note: The draft policy is circulated as Appendix E. The chair invites comments and amendments before the resolution is put.

(c) notes that the policy is consistent with and complementary to the Water Roads Conflict of Interest Policy V6.0 — Institutional and the CobaltBlu Conflict of Interest Policy V6.0 — Institutional;

(d) directs that all existing conflict disclosures, standing notices, and register entries made prior to the adoption of this policy are deemed to satisfy the policy’s requirements (no retrospective gaps); and

(e) schedules the first annual review of the policy for [INSERT DATE — recommend February 2027 or the first board meeting following the 12-month anniversary of adoption].

7.2 Discharge Requirements

(a)  Provide a loan discharge letter confirming the loan is repaid in full

(c)  Provide a release of any security interests

Agenda Item 8: Series A Cooperation

8.1 Background

Water Roads is raising a Series A round of A$15M at A$380M post-money valuation, with Ocean Zero as lead investor (A$10M) and Australian co-investors for the balance (A$5M). Target close is 7 March 2026.

8.2 CBS Cooperation Requirements

Series A investors may request:

(a)  Confirmation of CBS's shareholding and loan position

(b)  Copies of executed Recapitalisation documents

(c)  Confirmation of CBS board approval process (independent director oversight)

(d)  Meeting availability for investor due diligence calls

(e)  Confirmation of discharge arrangements

Agenda Item 9: Next Meeting

Agenda Item 10: Close

There being no further business, the Chair declared the meeting closed at [TIME] AEDT.

Summary of Resolutions

Note: Resolution 1 (procedural — approval of previous minutes) may be voted on by both directors. Resolution 2 (substantive — policy adoption affecting Water Roads matters) requires Jeff Dusting to abstain.

CERTIFIED as the resolutions passed at the Board Meeting held on 5 February 2026:

### CBS_Consent_Waiver_V7.docx

*File: `CBS_Consent_Waiver_V7.docx`*

Version 7 — Constitution version label corrected to V3.1

WATER ROADS PTY LTD

ACN 686 900 014

DATE: [                    ] 2026

CONFIDENTIAL

Changes from V6: Constitution version label corrected from “V3.2” to “V3.1” throughout. The Constitution has not been renumbered — V6 incorrectly attributed the correction of clause cross-references (e.g. F Share conversion cl 4.3→4.4) to a Constitution version change, when in fact V3.1 always had conversion at cl 4.4. All clause numbers remain unchanged from V6 (and are verified correct against Constitution V3.1). No substantive legal content has changed.

CBS CONSENT AND WAIVER DEED

PARTIES

CBS GROUP PTY LTD ACN 164 870 080 of [INSERT CBS ADDRESS — verify against ASIC extract] (CBS)

WATER ROADS PTY LTD ACN 686 900 014 of Unit 142, 19 Hickson Road, Dawes Point NSW 2000 (Company)

COBALTBLU PTY LTD ACN 103 595 071 of [INSERT COBALTBLU ADDRESS — verify against ASIC extract] (CobaltBlu)

(CBS, the Company, and CobaltBlu together, the Parties)

RECITALS

A. The Company was incorporated on 8 May 2025 and has implemented a recapitalisation pursuant to a Recapitalisation Deed dated 15 January 2026 (the Recapitalisation Deed).

B. Pursuant to the Recapitalisation (including the 10-for-1 share split), CBS holds 40,000 Common Shares in the Company, representing 4% of the issued share capital.

C. CBS acknowledges that it acquired its shareholding in the Company in its capacity as a strategic advisor and early supporter of the Company’s business, and not as a financial investor seeking preferred share rights or investor protections.

D. The Company intends to pursue institutional equity financing (Series A), and CBS acknowledges that:

(i) its Common Shares rank pari passu with F Shares held by CobaltBlu;

(ii) CBS does not hold, and has never held, any preferred rights, veto rights, board appointment rights, anti-dilution rights, or other special protections beyond those available to ordinary shareholders; and

(iii) CBS’s economic interest is accurately reflected by its 4% shareholding on a fully diluted basis.

E. CBS was a director of the Company at the time certain historic corporate actions were taken, and CBS wishes to confirm that:

(i) all such actions were taken with CBS’s knowledge and consent (or ratified retrospectively);

(ii) CBS does not claim any breach of director duties or oppressive conduct; and

(iii) CBS releases all parties from any claims arising from historic governance matters.

F. CBS is a party to a loan agreement with the Company dated [INSERT LOAN DATE], as varied by the CBS Loan Variation and Waiver Deed (the CBS Loan Deed), which together address all matters relating to the loan facility.

G. The Parties have agreed to document CBS’s consents, waivers, and acknowledgments in this Deed to provide certainty for the Company’s Series A fundraising process.

H. Jeffrey Alan Dusting is a director of both the Company and CBS, a director and 50% shareholder of CobaltBlu, and the spouse of Sarah Margaret Taylor (director and Company Secretary of the Company, and director and 50% shareholder of CobaltBlu). Jim Ellwood is a director of CBS and an observer (not a director) of the Company. The parties have managed these conflicts through:

(i) the comprehensive conflict of interest framework documented in the WaterRoads Conflict of Interest Policy (Version 6.0 – Institutional) and CBS Group Conflict of Interest Board Policy (Version 6.0 – Institutional);

(ii) standing notices of interest given by Sarah Margaret Taylor and Jeffrey Alan Dusting under section 192 of the Corporations Act, which were tabled at the Company board meeting of 15 January 2026 and are recorded in the Company’s Related Party Transaction Register maintained under Constitution clause 18.6;

(iii) verbal disclosures at the board meetings of 15 January 2026 (WaterRoads) and 16 January 2026 (CBS), recorded in minutes;

(iv) Jeffrey Alan Dusting’s abstention from all CBS votes relating to the Recapitalisation, this Deed, and related transactions; and

(v) Jim Ellwood (as independent CBS director) chairing the CBS board meeting of 16 January 2026 and being authorised to execute all CBS-side documents.

OPERATIVE PROVISIONS

1. DEFINITIONS AND INTERPRETATION

1.1 Definitions

In this Deed, unless the context otherwise requires:

“ASIC” means the Australian Securities and Investments Commission.

“Board” means the board of directors of the Company from time to time.

“Business Day” means a day that is not a Saturday, Sunday or public holiday in Sydney, New South Wales.

“CBS Loan Deed” means the CBS Loan Variation and Waiver Deed between CBS and the Company.

“Common Shares” means ordinary shares in the capital of the Company designated as “Common Shares” as defined in clause 5 of the Constitution.

“Completion Date” means 15 January 2026, being the effective date of the Recapitalisation.

“Constitution” means the Company’s Amended and Restated Constitution V3.1 adopted by special resolution on [date] 2026, effective from 15 January 2026.

“Corporations Act” means the Corporations Act 2001 (Cth).

“F Share Majority” has the meaning given in clause 3.1 of the Constitution (being the holders of more than 50% of the F Shares on issue, calculated on an as-converted basis, voting as a separate class).

“F Shares” means ordinary shares in the capital of the Company designated as “F Shares” (Founder Shares) as defined in clause 4 of the Constitution, including the right to auto-convert into Common Shares upon a Qualifying Financing (clause 4.4 of the Constitution).

“Founder Protective Provisions” means the matters listed in clause 20.2 of the Constitution requiring F Share Majority written consent while Founders hold at least 30% of issued Shares on a Fully Diluted Basis.

“Fully Diluted Basis” has the meaning given in clause 3.1 of the Constitution (being the total number of Shares that would be on issue if all options, warrants, convertible securities, and other rights to acquire Shares were exercised or converted in full).

“Historic Defects” has the meaning given in the Recapitalisation Deed.

“Independent Director” has the meaning given in clause 3.1 of the Constitution (being a Director who is not a Founder or associate, not an employee/officer, not a related party director/officer/employee, and not a spouse/family member of any such person).

“Investor Majority” has the meaning given in clause 3.1 of the Constitution (being, while any single holder of Series A Preferred Shares holds 40% or more, that holder; otherwise, holders of more than 50% of Series A Preferred Shares on issue, voting as a separate class).

“Investor Reserved Matters” means the matters listed in clause 21.2 of the Constitution requiring Investor Majority written consent while Series A Preferred Shareholders hold at least 20% of issued Shares on a Fully Diluted Basis.

“Preferred Shares” or “Series A Preferred Shares” means any class of shares designated as Series A Preferred Shares and issued by the Company in connection with a Qualifying Financing, having such rights as determined by the Board and F Share Majority and set out in the SHA or any amendment to the Constitution (as contemplated by clause 6.1 of the Constitution).

“Qualifying Financing” means the completion of one or more equity capital raisings by the Company in a single round or series of related closings, with aggregate gross cash proceeds to the Company of not less than A$5,000,000, on terms approved by the Board and the F Share Majority (as defined in clause 3.1 of the Constitution).

“Recapitalisation” means the recapitalisation implemented pursuant to the Recapitalisation Deed.

“Recapitalisation Deed” means the Recapitalisation Deed dated 15 January 2026 between the Company, CBS, and CobaltBlu.

“Related Party Transaction” has the meaning given in clause 3.1 of the Constitution (being a transaction or arrangement in which a Director, a Founder, or an associate has a material personal interest).

“Series A Investors” means investors who subscribe for Series A Preferred Shares in a Qualifying Financing.

“SHA” or “Shareholders Agreement” means any shareholders’ agreement entered into by the Company and its Members (or any of them) from time to time, as amended or restated (as defined in clause 3.1 of the Constitution).

1.2 Interpretation

In this Deed, unless the context otherwise requires:

(a) headings are for convenience only and do not affect interpretation;

(b) the singular includes the plural and vice versa;

(c) a reference to a party includes that party’s successors and permitted assigns;

(d) a reference to a statute includes any amendment, consolidation or replacement of that statute;

(e) a reference to a clause is a reference to a clause of this Deed;

(f) where a word or phrase is defined, other grammatical forms of that word or phrase have corresponding meanings;

(g) a reference to “$” or “dollars” is a reference to Australian dollars; and

(h) a reference to a document includes any variation or replacement of that document.

2. CONSENT TO RECAPITALISATION

2.1 Informed Consent

CBS confirms that:

(a) it has received and reviewed the Recapitalisation Deed, the Constitution (V3.1), and all related documentation;

(b) it has received independent legal and financial advice in relation to the Recapitalisation, or has had the opportunity to do so and has chosen not to;

(c) it understands the effect of the Recapitalisation on its shareholding, including:

(i) the cancellation of its previous 100 Class B shares;

(ii) the issue of 4,000 Common Shares (being 40,000 Common Shares after the 10-for-1 share split) representing 4% of the issued share capital; and

(iii) the pari passu ranking of Common Shares with F Shares (clauses 4 and 5 of the Constitution);

(d) it consents to the Recapitalisation and agrees that it is fair and reasonable; and

(e) it enters into this Deed voluntarily and with full knowledge of its terms and consequences.

2.2 Board Approval

CBS confirms that:

(a) its board of directors met on 16 January 2026 and approved CBS’s participation in the Recapitalisation;

(b) independent board approval was obtained, with Jim Ellwood chairing the CBS board meeting and Jeffrey Alan Dusting abstaining from all votes due to his interests in the Company and CobaltBlu; and

(c) CBS’s board considered the interests of CBS separately from the interests of the Company or CobaltBlu.

2.3 No Duress or Undue Influence

CBS confirms that:

(a) it was not subject to any duress, undue influence, or improper pressure in agreeing to the Recapitalisation;

(b) it had adequate time to consider the terms of the Recapitalisation and seek advice; and

(c) the terms of the Recapitalisation reflect the agreed economic arrangement between CBS and CobaltBlu.

3. ACKNOWLEDGMENT OF SHAREHOLDING TERMS

3.1 Economic Interest

CBS acknowledges and agrees that:

(a) its economic interest in the Company is accurately reflected by its 4% shareholding in Common Shares;

(b) the 4% shareholding was agreed between CBS and CobaltBlu as fair consideration for CBS’s early strategic advice, business development support, provision of the loan facility, and ongoing support;

(c) CBS does not have any undisclosed economic rights, profit participation arrangements, or side agreements that would increase its economic interest beyond 4%; and

(d) CBS has no claim for additional shares, value adjustments, or true-up payments.

3.2 Ordinary Share Status

CBS acknowledges and agrees that:

(a) its Common Shares are ordinary shares that rank pari passu with F Shares in all respects, including:

(i) voting rights (one vote per share) (clauses 4.1 and 5.1 of the Constitution);

(ii) dividend rights (equal participation) (clauses 4.2 and 5.2 of the Constitution);

(iii) return of capital rights (equal participation, subject to prior rights of Series A Preferred Shares if issued) (clauses 4.3 and 5.3 of the Constitution); and

(iv) participation in surplus assets on winding up;

(b) CBS does not hold, and has never held, any preferred share rights, including:

(i) liquidation preferences;

(ii) dividend preferences;

(iii) conversion rights (other than as provided in the Constitution);

(iv) redemption rights;

(v) anti-dilution protection;

(vi) pre-emptive rights beyond those in clause 8 of the Constitution; or

(vii) any other preferential economic rights;

(c) CBS does not hold, and has never held, any special governance rights, including:

(i) veto rights over company decisions;

(ii) board appointment or observer rights;

(iii) information rights beyond those available to ordinary shareholders under the Corporations Act;

(iv) drag-along or tag-along rights beyond those in clauses 11 and 12 of the Constitution; or

(v) any other special protective provisions;

(d) the only rights CBS has as a shareholder are those expressly set out in the Constitution, the Corporations Act, and general law applicable to all shareholders; and

(e) CBS acquired its shareholding as a strategic supporter and advisor, not as a financial investor, and did not negotiate or expect to receive investor protections typical of venture capital or private equity investments.

3.3 No Implied Rights

CBS acknowledges and agrees that:

(a) the fact that CBS is a related party of the Company (by virtue of director overlap) does not give CBS any special rights beyond those of an ordinary shareholder;

(b) the fact that CBS provided a loan to the Company does not give CBS any equity rights beyond its 4% Common Share holding;

(c) the fact that CBS participated in the Company’s early development does not give CBS any “founder-equivalent” rights beyond its Common Shares; and

(d) there are no implied or unwritten understandings that would give CBS rights beyond those expressly documented in this Deed, the Constitution, and the CBS Loan Deed.

4. WAIVER OF CLAIMS ARISING FROM RECAPITALISATION

4.1 Release of Historic Claims

CBS, for itself and its related bodies corporate, officers, employees, and agents, irrevocably and unconditionally:

(a) releases and discharges the Company and its directors, officers, and employees from any and all claims, demands, actions, suits, or proceedings arising from or in connection with:

(i) the Historic Defects identified in the Recapitalisation Deed;

(ii) any procedural or documentation irregularities in the Company’s historic capital structure;

(iii) any share issuances, capital reductions, or corporate actions prior to the Completion Date;

(iv) any valuation methodologies or allocation of equity between shareholders;

(v) any decisions made by the Board (including decisions in which CBS’s nominee participated); or

(vi) the implementation of the Recapitalisation;

(b) releases and discharges CobaltBlu and its directors, officers, and employees from any and all such claims; and

(c) agrees not to make any claim against any person in respect of the matters set out in clause 4.1(a).

4.2 Waiver of Oppression Claims

CBS acknowledges and agrees that:

(a) the Recapitalisation is fair and reasonable to CBS;

(b) the Recapitalisation does not constitute oppressive, unfairly prejudicial, or unfairly discriminatory conduct within the meaning of section 232 of the Corporations Act;

(c) the reduction in CBS’s proportionate shareholding from 9.09% to 4.00% reflects the correction of a historical error to the Agreed Ownership (as defined in the Recapitalisation Deed), not a dilutive or prejudicial act;

(d) CBS will not make any application under Part 2F.1 of the Corporations Act in respect of the Recapitalisation, the allocation of equity, any historic corporate actions, or any future actions contemplated by the Recapitalisation Deed or this Deed; and

(e) CBS waives any rights it may have had to challenge the Recapitalisation or seek alternative relief.

4.3 Waiver of Director Duties Claims

CBS acknowledges and agrees that:

(a) Jeffrey Alan Dusting was a director of both the Company and CBS throughout the relevant period, and Jim Ellwood served as an observer at Company board meetings;

(b) during that period, certain corporate actions were taken by the Company, including share issuances, capital structure decisions, and governance matters;

(c) CBS participated in, consented to, or ratified all such actions (or had the opportunity to do so and chose not to object);

(d) CBS does not claim any breach of director duties by any director of the Company in respect of any corporate action taken prior to the Completion Date;

(e) CBS releases all directors (past and present) from any claims arising from their conduct as directors; and

(f) CBS acknowledges that all directors acted in good faith and in the best interests of the Company.

4.4 Waiver of Pre-emptive and Similar Rights

CBS waives any pre-emptive rights, rights of first refusal, tag-along rights, drag-along rights, or similar rights it may have (whether under the Constitution, common law, or otherwise) in respect of:

(a) the Recapitalisation, including the cancellation and reissue of shares;

(b) any future issue of Series A Preferred Shares in a Qualifying Financing (subject to the carve-out in clause 8.4 of the Constitution);

(c) any future issue of shares under the Company’s employee share option plan (ESOP) within the approved 10% pool (clause 26 of the Constitution, with carve-out in clause 8.3); and

(d) any future transfer of shares by CobaltBlu to third parties,

except to the extent such rights are expressly preserved in the Constitution for all ordinary shareholders.

5. DIRECTOR CONFLICTS AND RATIFICATION

5.1 Acknowledgment of Conflicts

CBS acknowledges that:

(a) Jeffrey Alan Dusting is a director of the Company, a director of CBS, and a director and 50% shareholder of CobaltBlu;

(b) Sarah Margaret Taylor is a director and Company Secretary of the Company, and a director and 50% shareholder of CobaltBlu;

(c) Jeffrey Alan Dusting and Sarah Margaret Taylor are married to each other;

(d) Jim Ellwood is a director of CBS and has been invited to attend Company board meetings as an observer (he is not a director of the Company);

(e) these relationships create actual and potential conflicts of interest in relation to decisions affecting the relative rights of CBS and CobaltBlu, the Recapitalisation and allocation of equity, and the terms of the CBS loan facility; and

(f) the Company has managed these conflicts through the comprehensive governance framework described in clause 5.2.

5.2 Disclosure and Governance Framework

CBS records and confirms that:

(a) Sarah Margaret Taylor and Jeffrey Alan Dusting each gave standing notices of interest under section 192 of the Corporations Act, which were tabled at the Company board meeting of 15 January 2026 and recorded in the Company’s Related Party Transaction Register maintained under Constitution clause 18.6;

(b) the Company has adopted and implemented the WaterRoads Conflict of Interest Policy (Version 6.0 – Institutional), which provides a comprehensive framework for identifying, disclosing, and managing conflicts of interest;

(c) CBS has adopted and implemented the CBS Group Conflict of Interest Board Policy (Version 6.0 – Institutional), which mirrors the WaterRoads policy and ensures consistent conflict management across both entities;

(d) each Company director verbally disclosed the nature and extent of their interests at the board meeting of 15 January 2026, in accordance with sections 191–192 of the Corporations Act and clause 18.1 of the Constitution;

(e) the Company directors voted on the Recapitalisation in reliance on section 194 of the Corporations Act (the Company being a proprietary company), with the reliance documented in board minutes in accordance with clause 18.4 of the Constitution;

(f) Jeffrey Alan Dusting abstained from all votes at the CBS board meeting of 16 January 2026 relating to the Recapitalisation, this Deed, and the CBS Loan Deed;

(g) Jim Ellwood, as independent CBS director, chaired the CBS board meeting of 16 January 2026 and has been authorised to execute all CBS-side documents in connection with the Recapitalisation;

(h) the Recapitalisation has been recorded in the Company’s Related Party Transaction Register maintained under Constitution clause 18.6, including the date, parties, terms, disclosures made, and basis of approval; and

(i) the full conflict of interest framework (including the Version 6.0 policies, Standing Notices, Related Party Transaction Register, and relevant board minutes) will be disclosed to prospective Series A Investors in the data room.

5.3 Ratification of Prior Actions

CBS ratifies and confirms all actions taken by the Board prior to the Completion Date, including:

(a) decisions in which Jeffrey Alan Dusting participated or voted as both a Company director and CBS director;

(b) decisions affecting CBS’s rights as a shareholder or creditor;

(c) share issuances and capital structure decisions; and

(d) approval of Related Party Transactions involving CBS,

and agrees that such actions were valid and binding notwithstanding any actual or potential conflicts of interest.

6. NO RESIDUAL SPECIAL RIGHTS; CONSENT TO SERIES A

6.1 Acknowledgment of No Special Rights

CBS acknowledges and confirms that, following completion of the Recapitalisation:

(a) CBS holds only Common Shares, which are ordinary shares ranking pari passu with F Shares (clauses 4 and 5 of the Constitution);

(b) CBS does not have, and does not claim to have:

(i) veto rights (other than those available to all shareholders under the Corporations Act);

(ii) board appointment or observer rights (other than Jim Ellwood’s observer invitation, which is at the Company’s discretion and may be revoked at any time);

(iii) information rights beyond those available to ordinary shareholders under the Corporations Act and clause 25 of the Constitution;

(iv) anti-dilution protection;

(v) liquidation preferences;

(vi) drag-along, tag-along, or co-sale rights beyond those in clauses 11 and 12 of the Constitution (which apply equally to all shareholders);

(vii) MFN rights or ratchet provisions;

(viii) rights to participate in future financings on preferential terms; or

(ix) any other special protective provisions;

(c) there are no side letters, supplemental agreements, oral understandings, or undisclosed arrangements between CBS and any other party that would give CBS rights beyond those expressly set out in the Constitution and the CBS Loan Deed;

(d) CBS’s only relationship with the Company is as:

(i) a 4% ordinary shareholder (through its Common Shares);

(ii) a secured creditor (under the CBS Loan Deed); and

(iii) a related party (by virtue of director overlap, managed through the conflict framework); and

(e) CBS’s economic interest in the Company is fully and accurately reflected by its 4% shareholding on a Fully Diluted Basis, with no additional undisclosed economic arrangements.

6.2 Consent to Series A and Investor Protections

CBS acknowledges and consents to the Company’s pursuit of institutional equity financing (Series A), and specifically agrees that:

(a) Series A Preferred Shares and Senior Rights: The Company may create and issue Series A Preferred Shares to Series A Investors with rights that are senior to CBS’s Common Shares, including:

(i) liquidation preferences (priority in distribution of proceeds on exit);

(ii) dividend preferences;

(iii) redemption rights;

(iv) conversion rights and anti-dilution protection;

(v) class voting rights (including the right to approve certain matters as a separate class); and

(vi) any other preferential economic or governance rights negotiated with Series A Investors and determined by the Board and F Share Majority in accordance with clause 6.1 of the Constitution;

(b) Investor Governance Rights: Series A Investors may receive governance and protective rights that CBS does not have, including:

(i) board appointment rights (Investor Majority may nominate one Investor Director per clause 16.3 of the Constitution);

(ii) board observer rights;

(iii) veto rights over specified corporate actions through Investor Reserved Matters (clause 21.2 of the Constitution);

(iv) enhanced information and inspection rights (clause 25.3 of the Constitution and SHA);

(v) rights to approve budgets and strategic decisions;

(vi) drag-along rights under clauses 11.1(b) and 11.2 of the Constitution (requiring Investor Majority approval for drag-along sales);

(vii) tag-along rights under clause 12 of the Constitution; and

(viii) any other governance rights typical of institutional venture capital investments;

(c) Dilution of CBS’s Interest: The issue of Series A Preferred Shares will dilute CBS’s percentage ownership, and CBS:

(i) consents to such dilution;

(ii) waives any pre-emptive rights in respect of Series A Preferred Share issuances (recognising the carve-out in clause 8.4 of the Constitution for Qualifying Financing approved by F Share Majority);

(iii) acknowledges it will not receive anti-dilution protection; and

(iv) agrees that such dilution is fair and reasonable;

(d) Shareholders Agreement: Series A Investors may require the Company to enter into a Shareholders Agreement (SHA) that:

(i) modifies or overrides certain provisions of the Constitution (as contemplated by clause 22.2 of the Constitution, which provides that as between SHA parties, the SHA prevails);

(ii) imposes obligations on CBS as a shareholder;

(iii) grants Series A Investors superior rights to CBS; and

(iv) CBS agrees to become a party to such SHA if required by Series A Investors or the Company;

(e) Conversion of F Shares: Upon completion of a Qualifying Financing, F Shares held by CobaltBlu will automatically convert into Common Shares (clause 4.4 of the Constitution), and CBS:

(i) consents to such conversion;

(ii) acknowledges that CobaltBlu’s converted Common Shares will have the same class rights as CBS’s Common Shares (both ranking behind Series A Preferred Shares); and

(iii) acknowledges that the Founder Protective Provisions in clause 20 of the Constitution will continue to apply while Founders hold at least 30% of issued Shares on a Fully Diluted Basis, notwithstanding conversion;

(f) Independent Director Appointment: CBS consents to the appointment of at least one Independent Director within 60 days of Series A completion, as required by clause 16.1(b) of the Constitution;

(g) Investor Reserved Matters: CBS acknowledges and consents to the Investor Reserved Matters in clause 21.2 of the Constitution, which require Investor Majority written consent for specified actions (including material transactions, capital structure changes, and budget approvals), and agrees that where an action requires both F Share Majority consent (clause 20) and Investor Majority consent (clause 21), both consents must be obtained (clause 21.3);

(h) No Right to Equivalent Treatment: CBS acknowledges that:

(i) it is not entitled to receive the same rights as Series A Investors;

(ii) it is not entitled to MFN (most favoured nation) treatment;

(iii) it will not claim that any preferential treatment of Series A Investors constitutes oppressive conduct under section 232 of the Corporations Act; and

(iv) the differential treatment reflects the different commercial positions of strategic supporters (CBS) versus institutional financial investors (Series A);

(i) No Blocking Rights: CBS confirms that it does not have any right to:

(i) veto, block, or delay the issue of Series A Preferred Shares;

(ii) veto, block, or delay the negotiation or execution of an SHA;

(iii) veto, block, or delay any Constitution amendments required for the Series A (subject to section 136 voting requirements); or

(iv) veto, block, or delay any other corporate action required to complete the Series A; and

(j) Facilitation Obligations: CBS agrees to:

(i) execute any documents reasonably required by Series A Investors or the Company (including SHA deeds of adherence, amended Constitution approvals, and consents);

(ii) provide information requested by Series A Investors as part of due diligence;

(iii) cooperate fully with Series A due diligence inquiries;

(iv) attend shareholder meetings and vote in favour of resolutions required to complete the Series A (except to the extent doing so would breach CBS’s duties under the Corporations Act); and

(v) not take any action that would impede, delay, or frustrate the Series A financing.

6.3 Acknowledgment for Benefit of Series A Investors

CBS acknowledges that the consents and agreements in clause 6.2 are made for the benefit of:

(a) the Company;

(b) CobaltBlu; and

(c) prospective Series A Investors, who may rely on this Deed in their due diligence and investment decision-making.

This Deed may be disclosed to prospective Series A Investors as part of the Company’s data room, and Series A Investors are entitled to rely on the statements, acknowledgments, undertakings, and indemnities given by CBS in this Deed.

7. SEPARATION OF LOAN AND EQUITY ARRANGEMENTS

7.1 Acknowledgment of Separate Arrangements

CBS acknowledges and agrees that:

(a) its status as a secured creditor under the CBS loan facility is entirely separate from its status as a 4% shareholder;

(b) all matters relating to the loan facility (including interest, repayment, security, subordination, and discharge) are addressed comprehensively in the CBS Loan Deed;

(c) the loan facility does not give CBS any additional equity rights, governance rights, or preferential treatment as a shareholder;

(d) CBS’s security interest under the loan facility:

(i) is unperfected (not registered on the Personal Property Securities Register);

(ii) ranks behind any security interests granted to institutional lenders or Series A Investors (as provided in the CBS Loan Deed); and

(iii) will be fully released and discharged upon repayment at Series A completion (as required by the CBS Loan Deed);

(e) upon discharge of the loan facility at Series A completion, CBS’s only remaining relationship with the Company will be as a 4% ordinary shareholder and a related party (by virtue of director overlap); and

(f) CBS’s shareholding and the loan facility are distinct commercial arrangements, and no rights under one arrangement carry over to or enhance the other.

7.2 No Equity Conversion Rights

CBS confirms that:

(a) the loan facility does not contain, and has never contained, any right for CBS to convert the loan principal or accrued interest into equity;

(b) CBS has no right to acquire additional shares at a discounted valuation by reason of the loan facility;

(c) the loan facility is a debt obligation only, with no equity features, equity-linked rights, or warrants; and

(d) any suggestion that the loan facility includes equity conversion rights is incorrect and is hereby expressly disclaimed by CBS.

8. UNDERTAKINGS FOR BENEFIT OF SERIES A INVESTORS

8.1 Cooperation with Due Diligence

CBS undertakes to cooperate fully with due diligence inquiries from prospective Series A Investors, including:

(a) responding promptly and accurately to written and oral questions;

(b) providing access to relevant CBS records and documents (subject to confidentiality obligations owed to third parties);

(c) providing written certifications as reasonably requested by Series A Investors or their advisors;

(d) making Jim Ellwood and other CBS representatives available for meetings and calls; and

(e) not making any statements to Series A Investors that are inconsistent with this Deed or the CBS Loan Deed.

8.2 Execution of Series A Documentation

CBS undertakes to execute, within 5 Business Days of written request by the Company:

(a) any accession deed or deed of adherence to the SHA;

(b) any deed of priority, subordination deed, or intercreditor agreement relating to the CBS loan facility and Series A investor security;

(c) any written consents required for Series A completion (including consents to Constitution amendments or SHA terms);

(d) any shareholder resolutions or written approvals required under the Constitution or Corporations Act; and

(e) any other documents reasonably required by Series A Investors or their advisors,

provided that such documents are consistent with this Deed and the CBS Loan Deed and do not materially adversely affect CBS’s rights as a 4% ordinary shareholder or secured creditor (acknowledging that subordination to Series A investors and repayment at Series A close are already agreed and do not constitute adverse effects).

8.3 No Inconsistent Claims

CBS undertakes that it will not, at any time:

(a) make claims to Series A Investors, the Company, or CobaltBlu of special rights, preferential treatment, or undisclosed arrangements beyond those expressly documented in this Deed, the Constitution, and the CBS Loan Deed;

(b) assert veto or blocking rights over the Series A or any corporate action required to complete the Series A;

(c) claim entitlement to preferential treatment equivalent to Series A Investors;

(d) seek to renegotiate the terms of this Deed, the CBS Loan Deed, or CBS’s shareholding as a condition of providing consent to the Series A;

(e) take any action (including threatening litigation, making ASIC complaints, or asserting director duties breaches) that would reasonably be expected to impede, delay, or frustrate the Series A; or

(f) make disparaging public statements about the Company, CobaltBlu, the Founders, or the Series A process.

9. REPRESENTATIONS AND WARRANTIES

9.1 CBS Representations

CBS represents and warrants to the Company, CobaltBlu, and Series A Investors that, as at the date of this Deed:

(a) CBS is a company duly incorporated and validly existing under the laws of Australia;

(b) CBS has full power and authority to enter into and perform its obligations under this Deed;

(c) this Deed has been duly authorised, executed, and delivered by CBS and constitutes a legal, valid, and binding obligation of CBS, enforceable in accordance with its terms;

(d) the execution and performance of this Deed does not and will not:

(i) breach any law, regulation, or court order applicable to CBS;

(ii) breach CBS’s constitution or any resolution of CBS’s directors or shareholders;

(iii) breach or constitute a default under any agreement, deed, or instrument to which CBS is a party or by which CBS is bound; or

(iv) require any consent, approval, or authorisation that has not been obtained;

(e) there are no agreements, understandings, or arrangements (written or oral) between CBS and any person that:

(i) are inconsistent with this Deed;

(ii) would give CBS additional rights beyond those expressly set out in this Deed, the Constitution, and the CBS Loan Deed; or

(iii) would modify CBS’s economic interest in the Company;

(f) CBS has received independent legal and financial advice regarding this Deed and the Recapitalisation, or has had a reasonable opportunity to do so and has chosen not to;

(g) CBS enters into this Deed voluntarily, without duress, undue influence, or unconscionable conduct, and with full knowledge of its rights and obligations;

(h) CBS is the sole legal and beneficial owner of 40,000 Common Shares in the Company, representing 4% of the issued share capital on a Fully Diluted Basis, and such shares are free from any mortgage, charge, lien, pledge, or other encumbrance;

(i) there is no litigation, arbitration, administrative proceeding, or governmental investigation pending or threatened against CBS that would materially affect CBS’s ability to perform its obligations under this Deed; and

(j) all statements, acknowledgments, confirmations, and disclosures made by CBS in this Deed are true, accurate, complete, and not misleading, and CBS has not omitted any material fact that would make such statements misleading.

9.2 Survival of Representations

The representations and warranties in clause 9.1:

(a) survive the execution and delivery of this Deed;

(b) continue in full force and effect for the benefit of the Company, CobaltBlu, and Series A Investors; and

(c) are made as at the date of this Deed and deemed to be repeated:

(i) on the date of completion of the Series A; and

(ii) on the date CBS executes any SHA or deed of adherence.

10. INDEMNITY

10.1 CBS Indemnity

CBS indemnifies and holds harmless the Company, CobaltBlu, and any Series A Investors (and their respective directors, officers, employees, agents, and advisors) against any loss, damage, liability, cost, or expense (including reasonable legal fees on a solicitor-client basis) arising from or in connection with:

(a) any breach by CBS of its obligations, undertakings, or covenants under this Deed;

(b) any misrepresentation or breach of warranty by CBS under this Deed (whether innocent, negligent, or fraudulent);

(c) any claim by CBS that is inconsistent with this Deed, including:

(i) claims of special rights, preferential treatment, or undisclosed arrangements;

(ii) claims that the Recapitalisation was unfair, prejudicial, or oppressive;

(iii) claims that the Series A unfairly prejudices CBS or breaches CBS’s rights; or

(iv) claims of breach of director duties in connection with the Recapitalisation or Series A; or

(d) any action by CBS that impedes, delays, or frustrates the Series A financing, including:

(i) refusing or delaying execution of required documents;

(ii) threatening or commencing litigation or regulatory complaints;

(iii) making inconsistent or misleading statements to Series A Investors; or

(iv) any other conduct contrary to clause 8.3.

10.2 Limitation

The indemnity in clause 10.1 does not apply to the extent that the loss arises directly from:

(a) fraud, wilful misconduct, or gross negligence by the Company, CobaltBlu, the Founders, or Series A Investors; or

(b) breach of the Constitution, the Corporations Act, or this Deed by the Company or CobaltBlu.

11. GENERAL PROVISIONS

11.1 Entire Agreement

This Deed, together with:

(a) the Recapitalisation Deed dated 15 January 2026;

(b) the CBS Loan Deed;

(c) the Constitution (V3.1); and

(d) any SHA executed following Series A completion,

constitutes the entire agreement between the Parties in relation to its subject matter and supersedes all prior agreements, understandings, representations, and negotiations (whether written or oral).

11.2 Amendment

This Deed may only be amended by a written document signed by all Parties.

Following completion of the Series A, clauses 6.2, 8, 9, and 10 (relating to Series A investor protections) may not be amended without the prior written consent of the Investor Majority (or such other approval mechanism as may be specified in the SHA).

11.3 Waiver

A waiver of any right or remedy under this Deed is only effective if it is in writing and signed by the party granting the waiver.

No waiver of a breach of any provision of this Deed operates as a waiver of any other breach of that provision or any other provision.

11.4 Severability

If any provision of this Deed is invalid, illegal, or unenforceable in any jurisdiction:

(a) that provision is severed from this Deed in that jurisdiction to the extent of the invalidity, illegality, or unenforceability; and

(b) the remaining provisions continue in full force and effect in that jurisdiction and in all other jurisdictions.

11.5 Counterparts

This Deed may be executed in any number of counterparts (including electronic counterparts transmitted by email or DocuSign). Each counterpart is an original, and all counterparts together constitute one instrument.

11.6 Governing Law

This Deed is governed by the laws of New South Wales, Australia.

11.7 Jurisdiction

Each Party irrevocably:

(a) submits to the non-exclusive jurisdiction of the courts of New South Wales and courts of appeal from them for any proceedings arising out of or in connection with this Deed; and

(b) waives any objection to proceedings in those courts on the ground of venue or on the ground that the proceedings have been brought in an inconvenient forum.

11.8 Costs

Each Party bears its own legal, accounting, and advisory costs incurred in connection with the negotiation, preparation, execution, and performance of this Deed.

11.9 Further Assurances

Each Party must, at its own expense, do all things and execute all documents necessary or desirable to give full effect to this Deed and the transactions contemplated by it.

11.10 Third Party Beneficiaries

This Deed is intended to benefit Series A Investors, who are entitled to:

(a) rely on the statements, acknowledgments, representations, warranties, undertakings, and indemnities given by CBS in this Deed; and

(b) enforce this Deed directly against CBS as third party beneficiaries under the principles recognised in Trident General Insurance Co Ltd v McNiece Bros Pty Ltd (1988) 165 CLR 107 and the Contracts (Rights of Third Parties) Act (if applicable in the relevant jurisdiction).

Series A Investors may enforce this Deed without joining the Company or CobaltBlu as parties to any proceedings.

11.11 Notices

Any notice, demand, consent, or other communication under this Deed must be:

(a) in writing;

(b) signed by an authorised officer of the sender; and

(c) delivered by hand, sent by email, or sent by prepaid registered post to the recipient’s address set out in this Deed (or such other address as the recipient notifies in writing).

A notice is deemed to be received:

(d) if delivered by hand, on delivery;

(e) if sent by email, on the earlier of the sender receiving an automated receipt confirmation or at the time sent (if sent on a Business Day before 5:00pm at the recipient’s location, otherwise the next Business Day); or

(f) if sent by prepaid registered post, 3 Business Days after posting (or 7 Business Days if posted to or from a location outside Australia).

EXECUTION

EXECUTED as a deed.
